The Benefit of Logic as a Foundational Principle
Author states the benefit of logic and commentary explains its status as a principle.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why knowing the benefit of logic is considered a principle of the science and why studying without it is futile.

Core Idea
The benefit of logic is not just practical; it is a foundational principle without which study is futile.

The matn opens by stating the benefit of logic: avoiding error in thought. The commentator immediately clarifies that this benefit is counted among the principles (mabādi) of the science. This may seem surprising—why is the benefit a principle? In this lesson, we will explore why the benefit is epistemologically prior and how it saves the student from aimless investigation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the benefit stated in the matn
Read the first sentence: 'وَأَمَّا فَائِدَتُهُ، فَهِيَ الِاحْتِرَازُ عَنِ الخَطَأ فِي الفِكْرِ'. The benefit of logic is avoidance of error in thought. This is a negative definition—it prevents something unwanted.
2
Understand why the benefit is a principle
The commentator says: 'إِنَّما عدُّوها مِنَ المبادئ ; لأنَّ البحث مع جهلها عبث وضلال'. Research (or study) with ignorance of the benefit is 'عبث وضلال' (futile and misguided). Thus, the benefit is a principle because it provides the telos and justification for the entire study.
In the Islamic sciences, 'mabda'' (principle) is what must be known before the science.
3
Apply this to a different Islamic science
Consider 'Ilm al-Kalām: Its benefit is defending the creed. If one studied kalām without knowing that benefit, their study would lack direction. The same applies to all 'ulūm.
This shows the universality of the principle: every science requires a known benefit.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَأَمَّا فَائِدَتُهُ ، فَهِيَ الِاحْتِرَازُ عَنِ الخَطَأ فِي الفِكْرِ . قوله : (وَأَمَّا فَائِدَتُهُ) إِنَّما عدُّوها مِنَ المبادئ ; لأنَّ البحث مع جهلها عبث وضلال. والفائدة في اللغة: «ما حصل من علم أو مال». ١ - مشتقة مِنَ «الفيد» ; بمعنى : استحداث المال والخير . ۲ - وقيل : اسم فاعل من «فأدته»: أصبتُ فؤاده، واعترض هذا بأنَّه شامل للشَّرِّ، مع أنَّها خاصة بالخير . وعلى المعنى الثَّاني مشى الشَّهاب الخفاجي، فقال: [من الرجز] مِنَ الفُؤَادِ اشْتَقَتِ الفَائِدَه وَالنَّفْسُ يَا صَاحِ بِذَا شَاهِدَه لِذَا تَرَى أَفْئِدَةُ النَّاسِ قَدْ مَالَتْ لِمَن فِي قُرْبِهِ فَائِدَه وفي العرف هي : المصلحة المرتبة على فعل من حيث ثمرته ونتيجته»; وتلك المصلحة : من حيث إنَّها في طرف الفعل; تسمّى : «غاية له». - ومن حيث إنّها مطلوبة للفاعل بالفعل ; تسمى: «غرضاً».
And as for its benefit, it is the avoidance of error in thought. His statement: 'And as for its benefit' — they only counted it among the principles because research with ignorance of it is futile and misguided. And 'fa'ida' linguistically: 'what is obtained of knowledge or wealth'. 1 - It is derived from 'al-fayd', meaning: acquisition of wealth and good. 2 - And it is said: it is a noun of the agent from 'fa'adathu': I struck his heart (fu'ad), and this was objected to because it includes evil, while it (benefit) is specific to good. And on the second meaning, al-Shihab al-Khafaji proceeded, saying (in rajaz): 'From the heart (fu'ad) is derived al-fa'ida, and the soul, O friend, witnesses this. Thus you see that people's hearts incline to one in whose nearness there is benefit.' And in common usage, it is: 'the interest (maslaha) that follows an action in terms of its fruit and result'; and that interest, from the perspective that it is on the side of the action, is called 'end' (ghaya); and from the perspective that it is sought by the doer through the action, it is called 'purpose' (gharad).
Source pages p. 410

Commentary
This passage defines the benefit (fā'ida) of logic and provides a detailed linguistic analysis of the word 'fā'ida'. The matn states that the benefit is 'the avoidance of error in thought'. The commentator explains why the benefit is considered a principle: studying a science without knowing its benefit is futile. Then the commentator digs into the etymology of 'fā'ida'. Two opinions are given: (1) it is derived from 'al-fayd' meaning acquisition of wealth/good, (2) it is derived from 'fu'ad' (heart) because striking the heart yields understanding; the second meaning is defended by al-Shihab al-Khafaji with a poetic verse. The commentator notes the objection that the second meaning includes evil, whereas benefit is normally good. Finally, the technical definition in common usage is given: benefit is the interest (maslaha) that results from an action, termed 'end' (ghaya) when seen as the outcome of the action, and 'purpose' (gharad) when seen as the agent's goal.

Key Terms
فائدة
مبادئ

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the commentator, why is the benefit of logic counted among the principles of the science?
A) Because it is the most important topic in logic
B) Because studying without knowing the benefit is futile and misguided
C) Because it was mentioned first in the book
D) Because it is derived from the word 'fā'ida'

Key Takeaway
Knowing the benefit of a science is itself a principle that gives the science its direction and saves the student from futility.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
State the benefit of the science of 'Uṣūl al-Ḥadīth in one sentence, then explain why knowing that benefit is necessary before studying it. Use the logic of this lesson: without it, study is 'عبث وضلال'.

Linguistic Roots and Technical Definitions of 'Fā'ida'
Author provides linguistic analysis and technical definitions of 'fā'ida'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the two proposed linguistic derivations of 'fā'ida' and explain the objection to the second derivation, as well as differentiate between fā'ida, ghāya, and gharad in technical usage.

Core Idea
Fā'ida derives either from 'fayd' (acquisition) or 'fu'ād' (heart); the latter is contested, but both point to the good that results from action.

After establishing the benefit of logic, the commentator embarks on a fascinating linguistic inquiry into the word 'fā'ida' itself. Why does this matter? Because the precise meaning of the term affects how we understand the benefit of any science. You will learn the two derivations proposed by scholars, the objection raised against the second, and the technical distinction between benefit (fā'ida), end (ghāya), and purpose (gharaḍ).

Guided Path
1
Identify the two derivations
The text presents two opinions: (1) from 'al-fayd' meaning acquisition of wealth and good; (2) from 'fa'adathu' meaning 'I struck his heart', so 'fā'ida' is a noun of agent indicating something that strikes the heart (i.e., benefits). Note that both see benefit as something good that is obtained.
The second derivation is defended by al-Shihāb al-Khafājī with a poetic verse.
2
Understand the objection to the second derivation
The objection is that 'fa'adathu' (striking the heart) can be done for evil purposes as well, whereas 'fā'ida' is exclusively good. This objection is noted but not resolved in the text; it remains a point of debate.
This shows that linguistic analysis in logic is not merely academic but has implications for precision.
3
Distinguish fā'ida, ghāya, and gharad
In common usage (al-ʿurf), fā'ida is 'the interest (maslaha) that follows an action in terms of its fruit and result'. When that interest is considered from the side of the action itself, it is called ghāya (end); when from the side of the doer, it is called gharad (purpose).
This tripartite distinction is crucial in Islamic ethics and jurisprudence for analyzing the teleology of acts.

Source Text

What is the objection raised against deriving 'fā'ida' from 'fu'ād' (heart)?
A) The derivation is grammatically impossible

?
Using the technical definition from this lesson, identify the fā'ida, ghāya, and gharad for the act of performing salat al-jama'ah (congregational prayer). First state the benefit (e.g., reward), then the end from the act's side, and the purpose from the doer's side.

Logic as a Universal Science in the Islamic Intellectual Tradition
Commentary explains the hierarchy of sciences with logic at the top

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the hierarchical relationship between logic and other Islamic sciences using the criteria of premise dependency.

Core Idea
Logic provides the universal inference principles that all Islamic sciences depend on.

In the Islamic tradition, sciences are not isolated; they form a hierarchy based on whether one science's issues are used as premises in another. This passage from al-Bajūrī's commentary on al-Bannānī explains why logic is considered a universal (kullī) science relative to other sciences like kalām, grammar (naḥw), rhetoric (bayān), and exegesis (tafsīr). Understanding this hierarchy clarifies the foundational role of logic in the Islamic sciences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the key claim
Find the statement that logic is 'universal relative to all sciences'. What does 'universal' mean in this context?
The term kullī here refers not to a universal term but to a science whose principles are universally applied.
2
Extract the criterion for 'higher' and 'lower'
The commentator gives a criterion: if science A's issues are taken as given (musallama) in science B, then A is higher and universal relative to B, and B is lower and particular.
This is a dependency relation, not a value judgment.
3
Apply the criterion to the given examples
Trace the examples: logic → kalām, grammar → rhetoric, rhetoric → tafsīr. Explain why each dependency holds based on the passage.
For instance, kalām uses logic to structure its arguments; rhetoric uses grammar for correct expression.
4
Recognise the broader implication
Note that logic is not just a tool for philosophy; it underlies the highest religious science (tawḥīd/kalām) and indirectly all others.
The passage states that kalām is the highest religious science, yet it branches from logic.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَأَمَّا نِسْبَتُهُ لِغَيْرِهِ مِنَ العُلُومِ، فَهِيَ أَنَّ المَنْطِقَ كُلّيُّ بِالنِّسْبَةِ إِلَى سَائِرِ العُلُومِ؛ لِأَنَّ أَعْلَى العُلُومِ الشَّرْعِيَّةِ عِلْمُ التَّوْحِيدِ ، وَهُوَ مُفَرَّعٌ عَنْ عِلْمٍ المَنْطِقِ؛ إِذْ حَاصِلُ عِلم الكَلَامِ اسْتِدْلَال خَاصٌ ، وَعِلْمُ المَنْطِقِ يَبْحَثُ عَنْ مُطْلَقِ الِاسْتِدْلَالِ، فَصَارَ أَعَمَّ. قوله : (كُلِّي بِالنِّسْبَةِ إِلَى سَائِرِ العُلُومِ) وذلك : أنَّ كلَّ علم كانت مسائله المطلوبة فيه تؤخذ في علم آخر مسلمةٌ؛ بحيث يتوقف الثَّاني على الأوَّل؛ سمِّي الأوَّل: «أعلى» و: «كليا للثاني»، والثَّاني : أسفل» و : جزئيا للأول»؛ كـ: المنطق مع الكلام فإنَّ مسائل المنطق تؤخذ في الكلام مسلمة، وتبنى عليها مسائل الكلام، وكـ علم النحو مع البيان، فإنَّ مسائل النحو تؤخذ في البيان مسلَّمةً وتبنى عليها مسائل البيان، وكذا البيان مع التفسير. فيكون المنطق كلّيًّا بالنسبة للكلام، والكلام كلّيّا بالنسبة لِمَا عداه من سائر العلوم الدينيَّة، والنَّحو كلّيّا بالنسبة للبيان والبيان كليًّا بالنسبة للتفسير. قوله : (خَاصٌ) أي بالله تعالى ورسله عليهم الصَّلاة والسَّلام.
As for its relationship to other sciences: logic is universal relative to all sciences, because the highest of the religious sciences is the science of tawḥīd (monotheism), and it is branched from the science of logic; since the product of kalām is specific inference, while logic investigates inference in absolute terms, so it became more general. [Commentary:] His saying: 'universal relative to all sciences' means: each science whose sought-after issues are taken as accepted in another science such that the second depends on the first – the first is called 'higher' and 'universal' for the second, and the second is called 'lower' and 'particular' for the first. For example: logic with kalām (theology), for the issues of logic are taken as accepted in kalām and the issues of kalām are built upon them; and the science of grammar with rhetoric, for the issues of grammar are taken as accepted in rhetoric and the issues of rhetoric are built upon them; and likewise rhetoric with tafsīr (exegesis). So logic is universal relative to kalām, and kalām is universal relative to the rest of the religious sciences, and grammar is universal relative to rhetoric, and rhetoric is universal relative to tafsīr. His saying: 'specific' means: related to Allah Almighty and His Messengers, peace be upon them.
Source pages p. 410

Commentary
This passage defines the relationship of logic to other sciences. The commentator begins by stating that logic is universal (kullī) relative to all sciences. He explains that the highest religious science is tawḥīd, which itself branches from logic because the product of kalām is a specific type of inference (istidlāl khāṣṣ), while logic studies inference in absolute terms (muṭlaq al-istidlāl). Thus logic is more general. Then the commentator expands on the term 'universal' by providing a definition: when a science's issues are taken as premises in another science, the first is called 'higher' (aʿlā) and 'universal' (kullī) for the second, and the second is 'lower' (asfal) and 'particular' (juzʾī) for the first. He gives examples: logic and kalām, grammar (naḥw) and rhetoric (bayān), and rhetoric and exegesis (tafsīr). Finally, he explains the word 'specific' (khāṣṣ) in the matn as referring to topics concerning Allah and His messengers.

Key Terms
كُلّي
أعلى
أسفل
جُزْئِي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is considered the highest religious science?
A) Logic
B) Tafsīr
C) Kalām (tawḥīd)
D) Grammar

Key Takeaway
Logic is universal because its principles are used as premises in all other Islamic sciences, making it the most general science in the hierarchy.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Identify a pair of Islamic sciences not mentioned in the passage (e.g., uṣūl al-fiqh and fiqh) and determine which is higher and which is lower using the criterion that the higher science's issues are taken as premises in the lower.
?
Explain why the passage calls kalām 'the highest of the religious sciences' and yet says it branches from logic. Does this create a contradiction? How does the distinction between 'specific inference' and 'absolute inference' resolve it?

The Technical Meaning of Fā'ida and Its Three Perspectives
Commentary defines fā'ida and unpacks its three perspectives.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between ghāya, gharaḍ, and ʿilla ghāʾiyya as three perspectives of fā'ida and apply this distinction to theological arguments about divine actions.

Core Idea
One interest (fā'ida) can be viewed as end, purpose, or final cause depending on perspective.

In this passage from the commentary on logic's benefit, the author unpacks the term fā'ida with precision. You will see that a single interest (maṣlaḥa) can be called ghāya (end), gharaḍ (purpose), or ʿilla ghāʾiyya (final cause) depending on how it relates to the action and the agent. This distinction is not merely semantic; it has profound implications for how we understand divine actions, as the Ashʿarīs and philosophers used it to affirm God's wisdom without attributing neediness to Him. By mastering this conceptual tool, you will be able to analyze similar distinctions in other Islamic sciences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the technical definition of fā'ida
Locate the 'urf definition: fā'ida is the maslaha attached to an action in terms of its fruit and result. Ensure you see that the genus is 'maslaha' and the differentia is 'attached to an action in terms of outcome'.
This is the core definition from which the perspectives branch.
2
Extract the three perspectives of the same interest
Notice how the same interest is called ghāya when considered as the side of the action, gharaḍ as sought by the agent, and ʿilla ghāʾiyya as motivating the agent. Verify that each term picks out the same real thing but from a different angle.
This shows that multiple terms in logic can differ in consideration but agree in essence.
3
Apply the distinction to divine actions
Read the discussion on Ashʿarī and philosopher view: God's actions have ghāyāt (ends) but not aghrāḍ (purposes) or ʿilal ghāʾiyya that would imply deficiency. Identify why they make this move: purpose implies need, which is impossible for God.
This application demonstrates the real theological stakes of the terminological distinction.
4
Test your understanding by classifying a new example
Given a concrete scenario from fiqh (e.g., the prohibition of riba is meant to prevent injustice), classify the interest (preventing injustice) as ghāya, gharaḍ, or ʿilla ghāʾiyya from the perspective of the Lawgiver.
This step forces you to apply the three perspectives to an Islamic ruling.

قوله : (وَأَمَّا فَائِدَتُهُ) إِنَّما عدُّوها مِنَ المبادئ ؛ لأنَّ البحث مع جهلها عبث وضلال. والفائدة في اللغة: «ما حصل من علم أو مال». مشتقة مِنَ «الفيد»؛ بمعنى : استحداث المال والخير. وقيل : اسم فاعل من «فأدته»: أصبتُ فؤاده، واعترض هذا بأنَّه شامل للشَّرِّ، مع أنَّها خاصة بالخير. وعلى المعنى الثَّاني مشى الشَّهاب الخفاجي، فقال: [من الرجز] مِنَ الفُؤَادِ اشْتَقَتِ الفَائِدَه وَالنَّفْسُ يَا صَاحِ بِذَا شَاهِدَه لِذَا تَرَى أَفْئِدَةُ النَّاسِ قَدْ مَالَتْ لِمَن فِي قُرْبِهِ فَائِدَه وفي العرف هي : المصلحة المرتبة على فعل من حيث ثمرته ونتيجته»؛ وتلك المصلحة : من حيث إنَّها في طرف الفعل؛ تسمّى : «غاية له». - ومن حيث إنّها مطلوبة للفاعل بالفعل ؛ تسمى: «غرضاً». ومن حيث إنَّها باعثةٌ للفاعل على الإقدام على الفعل ؛ تسمّى: «عِلَّةٌ غائيَّةٌ». فالفائدة والغاية متحدان بالذات مختلفان بالاعتبار، كما أنَّ الغَرَض والعِلَّة الغائيَّة كذلك . فأفعال الله تعالى يترتب عليها حِكَمٌ ومصالح لا تحصى، فذهب الأشاعرة والحكماء إلى أد تلك المصالح غايات لأفعاله تعالى ومنافعها راجعةٌ إلى المخلوقات وليس شيء منها غرضاً له وعِلَّةٌ غائيَّةٌ لفعله؛ لأنَّ الغرض يؤدّي إلى نُقصانه سبحانه تعالى، وهو محال، وما ورد من الأحاديث والآيات الموهمة لكون أفعاله تعالى معللة بالأغراض، فهي محمولةٌ على الغايات المرتبة عليها، وليس شيءٌ مِن أفعاله خالياً المصلحة عن
His saying: 'As for its benefit': Indeed they counted it among the principles, because research while ignorant of it is futile and misguided. The benefit in language is 'what is obtained of knowledge or wealth.' It is derived from 'al-fayd' meaning the acquisition of wealth and good. And it is said it is an active participle from 'fa'adathu': I struck his heart, and this was objected to because it includes evil, whereas benefit is specifically good. The second meaning was followed by al-Shihāb al-Khafājī who said: [in rajaz] 'From the heart derived the benefit, and the soul, O friend, is a witness to that. Thus you see the hearts of people incline to one near whom is benefit.' In custom (ʿurf) it is the interest (maṣlaḥa) that is attached to an action in terms of its fruit and result. That interest: from the perspective that it is on the side of the action, it is called 'ghāya' (end) for it; from the perspective that it is sought by the agent through the action, it is called 'gharaḍ' (purpose); from the perspective that it is motivating the agent to undertake the action, it is called 'ʿilla ghāʾiyya' (final cause). So benefit and end (ghāya) are identical in essence but differ in consideration, just as purpose (gharaḍ) and final cause (ʿilla ghāʾiyya) are identical in essence but differ in consideration. The actions of Allah Almighty entail wisdoms and interests that cannot be counted. The Ashʿarīs and philosophers held that those interests are ends (ghāyāt) for His actions, and their benefits return to creation; none of them is a purpose (gharaḍ) for Him or a final cause for His action, because purpose leads to deficiency in Him, which is impossible. Whatever traditions and verses that may suggest that His actions are motivated by purposes are interpreted as referring to the ends (ghāyāt) that come about. None of His actions is devoid of interest.
Source pages p. 410

Commentary
This passage explains the benefit (fā'ida) of logic. The commentator begins by noting that the benefit is considered a principle (mabdaʾ) of the science, since studying it without knowing its benefit is futile. He then provides the linguistic definition of fā'ida as what is obtained of knowledge or wealth. Two etymologies are discussed: one from 'fayd' (acquisition) and another from 'faʾd' (heart), which was objected to for including evil. Al-Khafājī supported the heart etymology with a poetic verse. Then the technical definition: fā'ida is the interest (maṣlaḥa) attached to an action in terms of its outcome. This interest, depending on perspective, is called 'ghāya' (end when considered on the side of the action), 'gharaḍ' (purpose when sought by the agent), and 'ʿilla ghāʾiyya' (final cause when it motivates the agent). These terms are identical in essence but differ in consideration. The passage then discusses divine actions: they have ends (ghāyāt) but no purposes (aghraḍ) in the sense of something that would imply deficiency in God. Ashʿarīs and philosophers agree that God's actions have wisdoms that benefit creation, but He is not motivated by them in a way that implies needs.

Key Terms
فائدة
غاية
غرض
علة غائية

Key Takeaway
The benefit (fā'ida) is one interest that can be viewed as end (ghāya), purpose (gharaḍ), or final cause (ʿilla ghāʾiyya), each giving a different perspective on the same reality.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

Contingent Knowledge: The Logician's Broad Definition
Author defines contingent knowledge and clarifies its application with commentary.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define contingent knowledge (al-ilm al-hadith) as per the logicians and identify what it includes and excludes based on the commentary.

Core Idea
Contingent knowledge is any mental representation, not just true belief.

Logic is the study of how to move from known knowledge to unknown knowledge. But what counts as 'knowledge' in logic? This passage from Bajuri's commentary on Bannani establishes that contingent knowledge is defined broadly to include any mental representation, whether true or false. Understanding this definition is crucial because it sets the boundaries of logic itself.

Guided Path
1
Identify the term being defined
The passage defines 'contingent knowledge' (العلم الحادث). Note it is called 'contingent' to distinguish it from God's eternal knowledge, which is one and indivisible.
The mention of 'types' already excludes eternal knowledge, so the word 'contingent' is for extra clarity.
2
Extract the core definition
The definition given is: 'the attainment of the form of a thing in the intellect' (حصول صورة الشيء في العقل). This is based on the theory of mental existence.
This definition is technical and differs from everyday usage.
3
Understand the scope of 'thing'
The word 'thing' is used in its linguistic sense, not the theological sense. Therefore it applies to existent and non-existent, singular terms and relations, and to representations that correspond to reality or not.
Theologians restrict 'thing' to existent entities, but logicians use the broader linguistic sense.
4
Identify what the definition includes
Because of this broad scope, the definition covers true knowledge, opinion (ظن), compound ignorance (جهل مركب), blind imitation (تقليد), and even illusion and fancy (شل ووهم).
Calling these 'knowledge' contradicts common language and Islamic law but is acceptable as a technical term.
5
Recognize the theological background
The author comments on the Mu'tazila view that non-existent possibles have fixed essences. The verifying theologians deny this, hence they do not call non-existents 'things'.
This clarifies why the definition uses the linguistic sense to remain neutral on theological disputes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(أَنْوَاعُ العِلْمِ الحَادِثِ)
وَصْفُهُ العِلْمَ بـ "الحَادِثِ" ; لِزِيَادَةِ البَيَانِ، وَإِلَّا فَذِكْرُ الأَنْوَاعِ يُخْرِجُ : العِلْمَ القَدِيمَ ; لأَنَّهُ وَاحِدٌ لَا تَعَدُّدَ لَهُ عَلَى الصَّحِيح عِنْدَ الجُمْهُورِ مِنْ أَهْلِ السُّنَّةِ.
وَالعِلْمُ الحَادِثُ عِنْدَ القَوْمِ هُوَ : "حُصُولُ صُورَةِ الشَّيْء فِي العَقْلِ". وَالشَّيْءُ هُنَا بِالمَعْنَى اللُّغَوِيِّ، فَيَصْدُقُ بِالمُوجُودِ وَالمَعْدُومِ، وَبِالمُفْرَدِ وَالنِّسْبَةِ ; مُطَابِقَةٌ لِلْوَاقِعِ وَغَيْرَ مُطَابِقَةٍ.
قوله : (لِزِيَادَةِ البَيَانِ) فيه تنكيتُ على مَن يقول : إنَّه لإخراج علم الله تعالى القديم، ووجه الرَّدُّ : ما أشار له الشَّارح مِن أنَّ العلم القديم خرج بذكر "الأنواع" أوَّلاً .
قوله : ( عِنْدَ القَوْم ) المراد بهم : الحكماء، وهذا التّعريف مبني على الوجود الذهني، ويتناول: الظَّنَّ ، والجهل المركَّب، والتَّقليد، بل الشَّلَّ والوهم وتسميتها : عِلْماً" مخالف للغة والعرف العام والشَّرع، لكن لا مشاحة في الاصطلاح.
قوله : (وَالشَّيْءُ هُنَا بِالمَعْنَى اللُّغَوِيٌّ ) أي : لا بالمعنى المصطلح عليه عند محققي المتكلمين؛ لأنَّ المعدوم عندهم ليس بشيء، ومرادهم: نفي تقرر الذوات في الخارج بدون الـوجـود ردا على المعتزلة، وذلك أنَّ أكثر المعتزلة قالوا : المعدوم الممكن قبل وجوده شيءٌ وذوات ثابتة متقرّرة في نفسها في الخارج ; إلَّا أنَّ الممكنات قبل أن تكسى بنور الوجود كأشياء مخبوءة في بيتٍ مظلم، ثمَّ يفيض الله تعالى على من شاء منها نور الوجود، فيبرز للعيان، فالفاعل المختارُ إِنَّما فعل عندهم الوجود لا الذوات .
(Types of Contingent Knowledge) He describes knowledge with 'contingent' for additional clarification; otherwise, the mention of 'types' excludes eternal knowledge, because it is one, having no multiplicity according to the correct view of the Sunni majority. Contingent knowledge according to the [logicians] is: 'the attainment of the form of a thing in the intellect.' And 'thing' here in the linguistic sense, so it applies to existent and non-existent, and to the single term and the relation, [whether] corresponding to reality or not. His statement: 'for additional clarification' is a subtle criticism of those who say it is to exclude God's eternal knowledge; the response is what the commentator indicated: that eternal knowledge is already excluded by the mention of 'types' in the first place. His statement: 'according to the [logicians]' — by them is meant the philosophers. This definition is based on mental existence, and it includes opinion, compound ignorance, and blind following, even illusion and fancy. Calling these 'knowledge' contradicts language, common custom, and the Law, but there is no harm in terminological convention. His statement: 'and 'thing' here in the linguistic sense' — meaning not in the technical sense of the verifying theologians, because non-existence for them is not a thing. Their intent is to deny the establishment of essences in external reality without existence, as a refutation of the Mu'tazila. Indeed, most Mu'tazila said that possible non-existents before their existence are things having fixed essences established in themselves in the external world; except that possibilities before being clothed with the light of existence are like objects hidden in a dark chamber, then God Almighty pours the light of existence on whomever He wills from among them, so they emerge into sight. Thus, according to them, the free agent only creates existence, not the essences.
Source pages p. 419

Commentary
This passage defines contingent knowledge (al-ilm al-hadith) as the first step in logic, since logic is concerned with the method of arriving at unknown knowledge from known knowledge. The author begins by noting the term 'contingent' is added for clarification, because simply saying 'types of knowledge' would already exclude God's eternal knowledge, which is one and indivisible according to Sunni doctrine. He then gives the definition of contingent knowledge according to the philosophers (al-hukama'): 'the attainment of the form of a thing in the intellect.' This definition is based on the theory of mental existence (al-wujud al-dhihni). Importantly, the word 'thing' here is taken in its linguistic sense, not the technical sense used by theologians. In the linguistic sense, 'thing' applies to both existent and non-existent, to a single term (mufrad) and a relation (nisba), and to representations that correspond to reality or not. Thus, the definition covers knowledge that is true (corresponding to reality) as well as opinion, compound ignorance, and blind imitation, even illusions and fancies. The commentator notes that calling these 'knowledge' contradicts everyday language and Islamic law, but it is acceptable as a technical term. The author also clarifies the theological disagreement about 'thing': the verifying theologians (muhaqqiqun) from the Ash'aris and Maturidis deny that non-existent possibles are 'things' in external reality, against the Mu'tazila who held that possibles have fixed essences (dhawat) before existence. According to the Mu'tazila, these essences are like hidden objects that God then brings into existence. The passage thus sets the scope of 'knowledge' in logic as broad and neutral, including any mental representation, and warns against reading theological commitments into the definition.

Key Terms
العلم الحادث
حصول صورة الشيء في العقل
الشيء بالمعنى اللغوي
الوجود الذهني

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) To clarify that eternal knowledge is excluded by the mention of 'types'
B) To align with the Mu'tazila view of non-existents
C) To limit knowledge to true statements only
D) To refer to the divine knowledge

Key Takeaway
Contingent knowledge in logic is any mental representation, defined as the attainment of the form of a thing in the intellect, covering true and false beliefs, opinions, and even ignorance.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Determine whether each of the following is an instance of contingent knowledge according to the logicians' definition: (a) 'The earth is flat' (a false belief held by some), (b) 'God is one' (a true belief), (c) 'I have no idea whether rain will fall today' (ignorance). Explain your reasoning using the elements of the definition.
?
Examine the definition: 'Contingent knowledge is the attainment of the form of a thing in the intellect.' Identify the genus and differentia. Then, using the commentary, explain why the word 'thing' is taken in its linguistic sense and what difference that makes for including non-existent entities.

Critique of Two Definitions of Knowledge
Author critiques definitions of knowledge

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate two definitions of 'ilm by identifying which individuals they exclude and whether they are suitable for logicians or usuliyyun.

Core Idea
A definition that excludes genuine instances is corrupt; both criticized definitions fail.

In this passage, the commentator critiques two definitions of knowledge (al-ilm). The first, 'knowledge of the known', departs from the logicians' broad usage to the usuli narrow one. The second, 'judgment of the mind, decisive, corresponding to a cause', is even more restrictive. Understanding these critiques sharpens your ability to evaluate definitions in Islamic sciences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two definitions
Find the definitions: (1) 'knowledge of the known' and (2) 'judgment of the mind, decisive, corresponding to a cause'.
These are distinct attempts to define 'ilm.
2
Analyze the first definition
The first definition is criticized for excluding opinion (zann) and false belief (i'tiqad fasad) because it departs from logicians' terminology. Why are these excluded? Because 'ilm for logicians includes these, but the definition uses a more restrictive sense.
This shows the importance of context-specific definitions.
3
Analyze the second definition
Break down each qualifier: 'judgment' excludes concepts (tasawwurat); 'decisive' excludes opinion; 'corresponding' excludes false belief; 'to a cause' excludes correct belief. All these are legitimate individuals of 'ilm for logicians.
Hence this definition is even more corrupt.
4
Assess the overall critique
The author highlights that definitions must be comprehensive (including all intended individuals) and exclusive (excluding non-intended). Both definitions fail the comprehensiveness test for the logicians' usage.
Compare with usuli definition that limits 'ilm to certainty.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كَمَا لِبَعْضِ الشُّرَّاحِ، فَقَدْ خَرَجَ عَنْ مُصْطَلَحِ القَوْمِ إِلَى مُصْطَلَحِ الأُصُولِ، وَلَزِمَهُ فَسَادُ العَكْسِ بِخُرُوجِ (١) : الظَّنِّ وَالِاعْتِقَادِ الفَاسِدِ، مَعَ أَنَّهُمَا مِنْ أَفْرَادِ الْمُعَرَّفِ هُنَا . وَأَكْثَرُ مِنْهُ فَسَاداً تَعْرِيفُ مَنْ عَرَّفَهُ بـ: «حُكْمُ الذَّهْنِ الجَازِمُ المُطَابِقُ لِمُوجِب»؛ لِزِيَادَتِهِ عَلَى مَا قَبْلَهُ بِخُرُوجِ : الِاعْتِقَادِ الصَّحِيحِ وَجَمِيعِ التَّصَوُّرَاتِ ؛ ذَكَرَهُ بَعْضُ الْمُحَقِّقِينَ، وَهُوَ وَاضِحٌ.
وَالدَّورُ الَّذِي أَوْرَدُوهُ عَلَى تَعْرِيفِهِ بـ : «أَنَّهُ مَعْرِفَةُ المَعْلُومِ»، الحَقُّ فِي الجَوَابِ عَنْهُ : أَنَّ المُرَادَ بِـ «المَعْلُومِ : ذَاتُهُ لَا بِقَيْدِ وَصْفُهُ العُنْوَانِي الَّذِي هُوَ العِلْمُ .
قوله : كَمَا لِبَعْضِ الشُّرَّاحِ هو سيدي سعيد، فإنَّه قال: والمختار قول القاضي : أنَّه معرفة المعلوم» (٢) .
قوله : (وَلَزِمَهُ فَسَادُ العَكْسِ قال شيخنا اليازغي: هذا هو وجه خروجه عن مصطلح القوم لا شيء زائد عليه فصوابُ العبارة إذاً : فقد خرج عن مصطلح القوم إلى مصطلح الأصوليين؛ لأنَّ العلم عند المناطقة شامل للظَّنِّ وللاعتقاد الفاسد، وهما خارجان عن هذا الحد، وعند الأصوليين خاص باليقين.
قوله : (وَأَكْثَرُ مِنْهُ فَسَاداً تَعْرِيفُ مَنْ عَرَّفَهُ بـ: حُكْمُ الذَّهْنِ... إلخ) فقوله: حكم الذهن مخرج لجميع التَّصورات ؛ إذ لا حكم فيها ، و : «الجازم» مخرج للظَّنّ، وقد كان خرج عن التعريف قبله و: «المطابق» مخرج للفاسد وقد خرج أيضاً عن التعريف قبله، و: «الموجب مخرج للاعتقاد الصحيح، فقدِ اتَّضح زيادة فساد هذا على ما قبله وممَّن عرَّف العلم هنا بهذا التعريف الشيخ عبد اللطيف.
قوله : ( وَالدَّورُ الَّذِي أَوْرَدُوهُ) بيانُهُ : أنَّ «المعلوم» اسم مفعول مشتق من العلم الذي هو المصدر، ومعرفةُ المشتق متوقفةٌ على معرفة المشتق منه، فآل الأمرُ إلى أنَّ العلم توقف على معرفة المعلوم، ومعرفة المعلوم توقفت على العِلم، وهذا عين الدور.
قوله : (أَنَّ المُرَادَ بِـ «المَعْلُومِ : ذَاتُهُ ... إلخ) اعلم : أنَّ الوصف يُراد منه تارة الذات والمعنى معاً، وتارة الذات فقط كـ «ضارب»، فأطلق المعلوم هنا وأريد الشَّيء؛ إذ لفظ «المعلوم» يدلُّ على شيءٍ متّصف بالمعلوميَّة، فألغي ذلك الوصف العنوانيُّ الَّذي هو المعلوميَّة، ورُوعي الشَّيء فقط .
قوله : (بِالْفِكَاكِ الجِهَةِ) يعني: أنَّ توقُّف العِلم على المعلوم من جهة التّصور، وتوقف المعلوم على العلم من جهة الاشتقاق.
قوله : (أَوْ بِأَنَّ الدَّوْرَ مَعِيُّ الدَّورُ المعيُّ : أن يتوقف وجود كلِّ مِن الأمرين في الخارج أو الذهن على مصاحبة الآخر»، كما في الجوهر والعرض، والأبوة والبنوة؛ المثال الأول للخارج، والثَّاني للذهن، وهذا لا استحالة فيه، بل هو واجب.
قوله : (إِدْرَاكُ مُفْرَدٍ) أي: إدراك العقل المعنى المفرد ؛ أي: وصول النَّفس إلى المعنى بتمامه : :كـ إدراك معنى الإنسان) وهي : الحَيَوَانيَّة والنَّاطقيَّة يسمَّى في الاصطلاح «تصوراً».
Like one of the commentators, he has departed from the terminology of the [logician] people to the terminology of the usuliyyun, and it entailed the corruption of the converse by the exclusion of opinion and false belief, even though they are among the individuals of the definition here. And more corrupt than it is the definition of one who defined it as: 'The judgment of the mind, decisive, corresponding to a cause'; because of its addition over what preceded it by the exclusion of correct belief and all concepts; some of the verifying scholars mentioned it, and it is clear. And the circularity they advanced against its definition as 'it is knowledge of the known' — the correct answer to it is that what is meant by 'the known' is its essence, not restricted to its attributive description which is knowledge. His statement: 'Like one of the commentators' — he is Sayyid Sa'id, for he said: The chosen is the judge's statement: it is knowledge of the known. His statement: 'And it entailed the corruption of the converse' — our shaykh al-Yazghi said: This is the aspect of his departure from the terminology of the people, nothing else added, so the correct expression therefore is: he has departed from the terminology of the people to the terminology of the usuliyyun; because knowledge according to the logicians includes opinion and false belief, and both are excluded from this definition, and according to the usuliyyun it is specific to certainty. His statement: 'And more corrupt than it is the definition of one who defined it as: The judgment of the mind... etc.' — his statement: 'judgment of the mind' excludes all concepts, since there is no judgment in them; and 'decisive' excludes opinion, and it had been excluded from the previous definition; and 'corresponding' excludes the false, and it also had been excluded from the previous definition; and 'to a cause' excludes correct belief; so the increase in corruption of this over the previous has become clear. And among those who defined knowledge here with this definition is Shaykh 'Abd al-Latif. His statement: 'And the circularity they advanced' — its explanation: that 'the known' is a passive participle derived from knowledge which is the infinitive, and knowledge of the derivative is dependent on knowledge of the derivative from it, so the matter ends up that knowledge is dependent on knowledge of the known, and knowledge of the known is dependent on knowledge — this is clear circularity. His statement: 'That what is meant by the known is its essence... etc.' — know: that the description is sometimes used for the essence and meaning together, and sometimes for the essence only like 'striker'; so 'the known' was used here and the thing is intended; for the term 'the known' indicates a thing qualified by being known, so that attributive description which is being known was disregarded, and only the thing was considered. His statement: 'By the separation of aspect' — means: that the dependence of knowledge on the known is from the aspect of conception, and the dependence of the known on knowledge is from the aspect of derivation. His statement: 'Or that the circularity is concurrent' — the concurrent circularity: that the existence of each of the two matters in the external or the mind depends on the accompaniment of the other, as in substance and accident, and fatherhood and sonship; the first example is for the external, and the second for the mind, and there is no impossibility in it, rather it is necessary. His statement: 'Perception of a single expression' — i.e., the mind's perception of the single meaning; i.e., the soul's reaching the meaning in its entirety: like perception of the meaning of 'human' — which are animality and rationality — is called in terminology 'concept'.
Source pages p. 421

Commentary
This passage is a critical commentary on definitions of knowledge (علم) from a hashiya on al-Sullam al-Murawniq. The author first critiques a definition given by some commentator, saying it departs from the logicians' terminology to that of the usuliyyun (principles of jurisprudence scholars), which causes the converse to be corrupted because it excludes opinion and false belief, even though these are included in the definiendum according to logicians. Then he critiques another definition: 'the judgment of the mind, decisive, corresponding to a cause'. This definition is even worse because it additionally excludes correct belief and all concepts (tasawwurat), which are still part of knowledge. The author then addresses the circularity objection (دور) to the definition 'knowledge of the known' (معرفة المعلوم). He explains the proper answer: by 'the known' is meant the thing itself, not its attribute of being known. The commentary then quotes remarks by al-Yazghi and others. The author explains the circularity: 'the known' is derived from 'knowledge', so knowing the derivative requires knowing the source, creating a circle. Some respond by saying the circle is only concurrent (معي), not sequential (سبقي), but the author refutes this by stating that the dependence of a derivative on its source is sequential, not concurrent. He gives examples: substance/accident and fatherhood/sonship are concurrent, but here it's sequential because knowing the meaning of 'derived from knowledge' requires prior knowledge of knowledge. Finally, the author gives an alternative gloss: perception of a single meaning (إدراك مفرد) is called 'concept' (تصور).

Key Terms
العلم
الظن
الاعتقاد الفاسد
التصور
العكس

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Both definitions
D) Neither definition

Key Takeaway
A valid definition must include all intended individuals; the critique shows how definitions fail by exclusion.

What Is Mantiq?
intermediate
7 min
Circularity in Definitions: The Dawr Objection and Its Resolution
Author addresses circularity in definition of knowledge

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify a circular definition (dawr) and distinguish between concurrent and sequential circularity.

Core Idea
Circularity arises when the definiens uses a term derived from the definiendum; the solution is to reinterpret the term as referring to the thing itself.

The definition 'knowledge is knowledge of the known' appears straightforward, but logicians pointed out it leads to a vicious circle: 'the known' derives from 'knowledge', so knowing the known presupposes knowledge. The commentator provides a sophisticated response, distinguishing between concurrent and sequential circularity, and offers a resolution by taking 'the known' to mean the thing itself.

Guided Path
1
Identify the circular definition
The definition 'knowledge is knowledge of the known' – note that 'the known' (al-ma'lum) is a passive participle derived from 'ilm.
Derivation creates a dependency.
2
Understand the circularity
If 'ilm is defined using 'ma'lum', and 'ma'lum' is known only through 'ilm, then we have a circle: each depends on the other.
This is the classic dawr.
3
Distinguish types of circularity
Concurrent circularity (dawr ma'i) involves mutual dependence in existence, like substance and accident. Sequential circularity (dawr sabqi) involves a temporal or conceptual priority. Here it is sequential because derivation requires prior knowledge of the root.
The author mentions that some claim it is concurrent, but he refutes that.
4
Learn the resolution
The commentator says that by 'the known' they mean the thing itself, not the attribute of being known. So the definition becomes 'knowledge of the thing', which is not circular.
This is achieved by disregarding the derivative sense and focusing on the essence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كَمَا لِبَعْضِ الشُّرَّاحِ، فَقَدْ خَرَجَ عَنْ مُصْطَلَحِ القَوْمِ إِلَى مُصْطَلَحِ الأُصُولِ، وَلَزِمَهُ فَسَادُ العَكْسِ بِخُرُوجِ (١) : الظَّنِّ وَالِاعْتِقَادِ الفَاسِدِ، مَعَ أَنَّهُمَا مِنْ أَفْرَادِ الْمُعَرَّفِ هُنَا . وَأَكْثَرُ مِنْهُ فَسَاداً تَعْرِيفُ مَنْ عَرَّفَهُ بـ: «حُكْمُ الذَّهْنِ الجَازِمُ المُطَابِقُ لِمُوجِب»؛ لِزِيَادَتِهِ عَلَى مَا قَبْلَهُ بِخُرُوجِ : الِاعْتِقَادِ الصَّحِيحِ وَجَمِيعِ التَّصَوُّرَاتِ ؛ ذَكَرَهُ بَعْضُ الْمُحَقِّقِينَ، وَهُوَ وَاضِحٌ.
وَالدَّورُ الَّذِي أَوْرَدُوهُ عَلَى تَعْرِيفِهِ بـ : «أَنَّهُ مَعْرِفَةُ المَعْلُومِ»، الحَقُّ فِي الجَوَابِ عَنْهُ : أَنَّ المُرَادَ بِـ «المَعْلُومِ : ذَاتُهُ لَا بِقَيْدِ وَصْفُهُ العُنْوَانِي الَّذِي هُوَ العِلْمُ .
قوله : كَمَا لِبَعْضِ الشُّرَّاحِ هو سيدي سعيد، فإنَّه قال: والمختار قول القاضي : أنَّه معرفة المعلوم» (٢) .
قوله : (وَلَزِمَهُ فَسَادُ العَكْسِ قال شيخنا اليازغي: هذا هو وجه خروجه عن مصطلح القوم لا شيء زائد عليه فصوابُ العبارة إذاً : فقد خرج عن مصطلح القوم إلى مصطلح الأصوليين؛ لأنَّ العلم عند المناطقة شامل للظَّنِّ وللاعتقاد الفاسد، وهما خارجان عن هذا الحد، وعند الأصوليين خاص باليقين.
قوله : (وَأَكْثَرُ مِنْهُ فَسَاداً تَعْرِيفُ مَنْ عَرَّفَهُ بـ: حُكْمُ الذَّهْنِ... إلخ) فقوله: حكم الذهن مخرج لجميع التَّصورات ؛ إذ لا حكم فيها ، و : «الجازم» مخرج للظَّنّ، وقد كان خرج عن التعريف قبله و: «المطابق» مخرج للفاسد وقد خرج أيضاً عن التعريف قبله، و: «الموجب مخرج للاعتقاد الصحيح، فقدِ اتَّضح زيادة فساد هذا على ما قبله وممَّن عرَّف العلم هنا بهذا التعريف الشيخ عبد اللطيف.
قوله : ( وَالدَّورُ الَّذِي أَوْرَدُوهُ) بيانُهُ : أنَّ «المعلوم» اسم مفعول مشتق من العلم الذي هو المصدر، ومعرفةُ المشتق متوقفةٌ على معرفة المشتق منه، فآل الأمرُ إلى أنَّ العلم توقف على معرفة المعلوم، ومعرفة المعلوم توقفت على العِلم، وهذا عين الدور.
قوله : (أَنَّ المُرَادَ بِـ «المَعْلُومِ : ذَاتُهُ ... إلخ) اعلم : أنَّ الوصف يُراد منه تارة الذات والمعنى معاً، وتارة الذات فقط كـ «ضارب»، فأطلق المعلوم هنا وأريد الشَّيء؛ إذ لفظ «المعلوم» يدلُّ على شيءٍ متّصف بالمعلوميَّة، فألغي ذلك الوصف العنوانيُّ الَّذي هو المعلوميَّة، ورُوعي الشَّيء فقط .
قوله : (بِالْفِكَاكِ الجِهَةِ) يعني: أنَّ توقُّف العِلم على المعلوم من جهة التّصور، وتوقف المعلوم على العلم من جهة الاشتقاق.
قوله : (أَوْ بِأَنَّ الدَّوْرَ مَعِيُّ الدَّورُ المعيُّ : أن يتوقف وجود كلِّ مِن الأمرين في الخارج أو الذهن على مصاحبة الآخر»، كما في الجوهر والعرض، والأبوة والبنوة؛ المثال الأول للخارج، والثَّاني للذهن، وهذا لا استحالة فيه، بل هو واجب.
قوله : (إِدْرَاكُ مُفْرَدٍ) أي: إدراك العقل المعنى المفرد ؛ أي: وصول النَّفس إلى المعنى بتمامه : :كـ إدراك معنى الإنسان) وهي : الحَيَوَانيَّة والنَّاطقيَّة يسمَّى في الاصطلاح «تصوراً».

What Is Mantiq?
beginner

Defining Tasawwur: Perception of a Single Meaning
Author defines tasawwur as perception of a single meaning

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define 'tasawwur' and distinguish it from 'tasdiq' based on its definition as perception of a single meaning.

Core Idea
Tasawwur is the perception of a single meaning without judgment; it is the foundation of all conceptual knowledge.

At the end of the passage, the commentator clarifies that 'perception of a single expression' (إدراك مفرد) is called a concept (tasawwur). This is a key definition in logic, as it distinguishes mere grasping of concepts from making judgments (tasdiq). Understanding tasawwur is essential for building definitions and arguments.

Guided Path
1
Locate the definition of tasawwur
Find the phrase 'إدراك مفرد' (perception of a single meaning) in the passage.
This is the commentator's gloss.
2
Understand 'single meaning'
A single meaning is a unified mental content, like the concept of 'human' which includes animality and rationality as a whole.
It is not a simple atom but a composite grasped as one.
3
Contrast with tasdiq
Tasdiq involves judgment that combines concepts, e.g., 'Zayd is standing'. Tasawwur is just the concepts themselves.
This distinction is fundamental in Islamic logic.
4
Apply to other terms
Practice defining other concepts like 'ilm itself as a tasawwur: it is the perception of the meaning of knowledge.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

قوله : (أَنَّ المُرَادَ بِـ «المَعْلُومِ : ذَاتُهُ ... إلخ) اعلم : أنَّ الوصف يُراد منه تارة الذات والمعنى معاً، وتارة الذات فقط كـ «ضارب»، فأطلق المعلوم هنا وأريد الشَّيء؛ إذ لفظ «المعلوم» يدلُّ على شيءٍ متّصف بالمعلوميَّة، فألغي ذلك الوصف العنوانيُّ الَّذي هو المعلوميَّة، ورُوعي الشَّيء فقط .
قوله : (بِالْفِكَاكِ الجِهَةِ) يعني: أنَّ توقُّف العِلم على المعلوم من جهة التّصور، وتوقف المعلوم على العلم من جهة الاشتقاق.
قوله : (أَوْ بِأَنَّ الدَّوْرَ مَعِيُّ الدَّورُ المعيُّ : أن يتوقف وجود كلِّ مِن الأمرين في الخارج أو الذهن على مصاحبة الآخر»، كما في الجوهر والعرض، والأبوة والبنوة؛ المثال الأول للخارج، والثَّاني للذهن، وهذا لا استحالة فيه، بل هو واجب.
قوله : (إِدْرَاكُ مُفْرَدٍ) أي: إدراك العقل المعنى المفرد ؛ أي: وصول النَّفس إلى المعنى بتمامه : :كـ إدراك معنى الإنسان) وهي : الحَيَوَانيَّة والنَّاطقيَّة يسمَّى في الاصطلاح «تصوراً».
Like one of the commentators, he has departed from the terminology of the [logician] people to the terminology of the usuliyyun, and it entailed the corruption of the converse by the exclusion of opinion and false belief, even though they are among the individuals of the definition here. And more corrupt than it is the definition of one who defined it as: 'The judgment of the mind, decisive, corresponding to a cause'; because of its addition over what preceded it by the exclusion of correct belief and all concepts; some of the verifying scholars mentioned it, and it is clear. And the circularity they advanced against its definition as 'it is knowledge of the known' — the correct answer to it is that what is meant by 'the known' is its essence, not restricted to its attributive description which is knowledge. His statement: 'Like one of the commentators' — he is Sayyid Sa'id, for he said: The chosen is the judge's statement: it is knowledge of the known. His statement: 'And it entailed the corruption of the converse' — our shaykh al-Yazghi said: This is the aspect of his departure from the terminology of the people, nothing else added, so the correct expression therefore is: he has departed from the terminology of the people to the terminology of the usuliyyun; because knowledge according to the logicians includes opinion and false belief, and both are excluded from this definition, and according to the usuliyyun it is specific to certainty. His statement: 'And more corrupt than it is the definition of one who defined it as: The judgment of the mind... etc.' — his statement: 'judgment of the mind' excludes all concepts, since there is no judgment in them; and 'decisive' excludes opinion, and it had been excluded from the previous definition; and 'corresponding' excludes the false, and it also had been excluded from the previous definition; and 'to a cause' excludes correct belief; so the increase in corruption of this over the previous has become clear. And among those who defined knowledge here with this definition is Shaykh 'Abd al-Latif. His statement: 'And the circularity they advanced' — its explanation: that 'the known' is a passive participle derived from knowledge which is the infinitive, and knowledge of the derivative is dependent on knowledge of the derivative from it, so the matter ends up that knowledge is dependent on knowledge of the known, and knowledge of the known is dependent on knowledge — this is clear circularity. His statement: 'That what is meant by the known is its essence... etc.' — know: that the description is sometimes used for the essence and meaning together, and sometimes for the essence only like 'striker'; so 'the known' was used here and the thing is intended; for the term 'the known' indicates a thing qualified by being known, so that attributive description which is being known was disregarded, and only the thing was considered. His statement: 'By the separation of aspect' — means: that the dependence of knowledge on the known is from the aspect of conception, and the dependence of the known on knowledge is from the aspect of derivation. His statement: 'Or that the circularity is concurrent' — the concurrent circularity: that the existence of each of the two matters in the external or the mind depends on the accompaniment of the other, as in substance and accident, and fatherhood and sonship; the first example is for the external, and the second for the mind, and there is no impossibility in it, rather it is necessary. His statement: 'Perception of a single expression' — i.e., the mind's perception of the single meaning; i.e., the soul's reaching the meaning in its entirety: like perception of the meaning of 'human' — which are animality and rationality — is called in terminology 'concept'.
Source pages p. 421

Commentary
This passage is a critical commentary on definitions of knowledge (علم) from a hashiya on al-Sullam al-Murawniq. The author first critiques a definition given by some commentator, saying it departs from the logicians' terminology to that of the usuliyyun (principles of jurisprudence scholars), which causes the converse to be corrupted because it excludes opinion and false belief, even though these are included in the definiendum according to logicians. Then he critiques another definition: 'the judgment of the mind, decisive, corresponding to a cause'. This definition is even worse because it additionally excludes correct belief and all concepts (tasawwurat), which are still part of knowledge. The author then addresses the circularity objection (دور) to the definition 'knowledge of the known' (معرفة المعلوم). He explains the proper answer: by 'the known' is meant the thing itself, not its attribute of being known. The commentary then quotes remarks by al-Yazghi and others. The author explains the circularity: 'the known' is derived from 'knowledge', so knowing the derivative requires knowing the source, creating a circle. Some respond by saying the circle is only concurrent (معي), not sequential (سبقي), but the author refutes this by stating that the dependence of a derivative on its source is sequential, not concurrent. He gives examples: substance/accident and fatherhood/sonship are concurrent, but here it's sequential because knowing the meaning of 'derived from knowledge' requires prior knowledge of knowledge. Finally, the author gives an alternative gloss: perception of a single meaning (إدراك مفرد) is called 'concept' (تصور).

Key Terms
التصور
الإدراك
المفرد
المعنى

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) meaning
D) None

Key Takeaway
Tasawwur is the mental grasping of a single concept, the building block of all knowledge.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Define 'iman' as a tasawwur: articulate its single meaning (belief in the heart) without including the judgment of its truth. Then write a tasdiq statement about iman, such as 'Iman is required for salvation'.

What Is Mantiq?

The Scope of Tasawwur: Included Relations
Author defines tasawwur by enumerating the types of relations that fall under it.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to enumerate the types of relations that constitute tasawwur and justify why each falls under conception rather than judgment.

Core Idea
Tasawwur encompasses all mental perceptions of relations that stop short of truth-value.

The author broadens the concept of tasawwur by specifying that it includes not only simple concepts but also various relational perceptions. Whether it is the relation in a proposition (without judging it), the grammatical relations of idafa and na't, performative utterances, or even unintended relational contexts, as long as the mind does not commit to truth or falsehood, it remains in the realm of tasawwur. This lesson unpacks each category.

Guided Path
1
Identify the baseline definition
Recall that tasawwur is the perception of a thing without judgment (tasdiq). This passage extends that definition by listing which perceptions qualify.
2
Extract the six types from the passage
From the Arabic, list: (a) nisba hukmiyya without actually judging (as from a doubter), (b) nisba naqisa (idafa and na't), (c) nisba insha'iyya, (d) nisba mashkul fiha 'ala al-sawa', (e) nisba ghayr maqsuda (clause as sila or khabar).
The fourth type is later criticized by the commentator as redundant.
3
Explain the absence of judgment for each type
For (a), the doubter conceives the subject, predicate, and relation but does not affirm or deny. For (b), incomplete relations like idafa are not propositions, so no truth value. For (c), performatives have no truth value. For (d) and (e), the relation is not the intended subject of judgment.
The commentator explains the doubter's case in detail.
4
Note the commentator's critique
The commentator criticizes the inclusion of 'nisba mashkul fiha 'ala al-sawa'' as a repetition of (a), since the doubter already involves equal doubt.
This shows the scholarly rigor in refining definitions.
5
Summarize the overall scope
Tasawwur includes any perception of a relation—whether propositional, grammatical, performative, or incidental—provided no truth-evaluation occurs.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
- وَتَدْخُلُ فِيهِ : النِّسْبَةُ الحُكْمِيَّةُ الَّتِي هِيَ مَوْرِدُ الإِيجَابِ وَالسَّلْبِ مِنْ غَيْرِ اعْتِبَارِ الحُكْمِ، كَمَا يَقَعُ مِنَ الشَّاكِّ .
- وَتَدْخُلُ فِيهِ أَيْضاً : النِّسْبَةُ النَّاقِصَةُ كَنِسْبَةِ المُضَافِ إِلَى المُضَافِ إِلَيْهِ، وَالنَّعْتِ إِلَى المَنْعُوتِ، وَالنِّسْبَةُ الإِنْشَائِيَّةُ وَالمَشْكُولُ فِيهَا عَلَى السَّوَاءِ، وَغَيْرُ المَقْصُودَةِ كَنِسْبَةِ الجُمْلَةِ الوَاقِعَةِ صِلَةً أَوْ خَبَراً، فَإِدْرَاكُ [٧/١] كُلِّ مِنْ هَذِهِ الأَشْيَاءِ تَصَوُّرٌ.
قوله : (كَمَا يَقَعُ مِنَ الشَّاكِّ) أي : يتصوّر المحكوم عليه والمحكوم به ومعنى النسبة، ويشكُ في وقوعها أو لا وقوعها، فلو لم يتصور النِّسبة لم يمكنه أن يشكّ فيها هل هي واقعة أو ليست بواقعة؟
قوله : ( وَالنِّسْبَةُ الإِنْشَائِيَّةُ ) أي : لأنَّها لا تحتمل صدقاً ولا كذباً.
قوله : (وَالمَشْكُولُ فِيهَا عَلَى السَّوَاءِ) تبع في هذا الهلالي، وفيه نظر؛ إذ هو مكرَّر مع قوله قبل : وَتَدْخُلُ فِيهِ النِّسْبَةُ الحُكْمِيَّةُ ... كَمَا يَقَعُ مِنَ الشَّاكِّ.
And there enters into it: the relational judgment that is the locus of affirmation and negation without considering the judgment, as occurs from the doubter. And there also enters into it: the incomplete relation, like the relation of the genitive to the genitive, and the adjective to the described, and the performative relation, and the relation that is equally doubted, and the unintended relation like the relation of a clause that is a relative clause or a predicate. So the perception of each of these things is a conception. His statement: (as occurs from the doubter) means: he conceives the subject and predicate and the meaning of the relation, but doubts its occurrence or non-occurrence, for if he did not conceive the relation, he could not doubt whether it occurs or not. His statement: (the performative relation) means: because it admits neither truth nor falsehood. His statement: (the relation that is equally doubted) he followed al-Hilali in this, but there is consideration in it; for it is a repetition with his previous statement: 'and there enters into it the relational judgment... as occurs from the doubter.'
Source pages p. 423

Commentary
This passage is a definitional expansion of the concept of tasawwur (conception). The author, commenting on a matn, clarifies what types of perceptions fall under tasawwur. He states that tasawwur includes the perception of a relational judgment (al-nisba al-hukmiyya) that is the subject of affirmation or negation, but without actually making a judgment. An example is a doubter who conceives the subject, predicate, and relation but does not affirm or deny. This shows that mere conception of a proposition's components is tasawwur. Next, he lists other types: incomplete relations like the grammatical idafa (genitive) and na't (adjective), performative relations (like commands or questions which have no truth value), relations that are equally doubted (redundant as he criticizes), and unintended relations such as the relation of a relative clause or predicate clause which are not the focus of judgment. The commentary explains each: for the doubter, he must at least conceive the relation to be in doubt; the performative relation has no truth value; the 'equally doubted' is criticized as a repetition. Thus, tasawwur encompasses a wide range of mental perceptions beyond simple concepts.

Key Terms
تَصَوُّر (tasawwur): Perception of a thing without judgment; includes conception of concepts and relations as long as no truth evaluation occurs. [Note: No significant shift; stable across the tradition.]
النِّسْبَةُ الحُكْمِيَّةُ (al-nisba al-hukmiyya): The relational aspect of a proposition that is the locus of affirmation or negation, apart from the act of judging. [Note: In later texts, this term may refer specifically to the relation in a categorical proposition.]

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Knowing that Zayd is standing.
B) Conception of the relation 'son of' without judging whether it exists.
C) Doubting whether the world is created.
D) Believing that prayer is obligatory.

Key Takeaway
Tasawwur is not limited to simple concepts; it includes the perception of all types of relations as long as no truth-value judgment is made.

What Is Mantiq?

7 min
Definition of Tasdiq: Perception with Judgment
Author defines tasdiq as perception of a relation with judgment, clarifying its scope and nature.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define tasdiq, identify its essential components (perception and judgment), and determine which mental states qualify as tasdiq according to the logicians.

Core Idea
Tasdiq is not mere perception—it requires a judgment of truth or falsity, and even opinion counts, but not doubt.

After learning about tasawwur (concept formation), we now turn to the second main cognitive act: tasdiq (assent). This lesson unpacks the precise definition of tasdiq as 'perception of the relation with a judgment.' We will see why this definition necessarily includes opinion (zann) but excludes doubt (shakk) and bare illusion (wahm). Understanding this definition is crucial for distinguishing genuine theological and legal reasoning from mere speculation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the term being defined (tasdiq)
The passage defines tasdiq as 'perception of the relation' but immediately clarifies that by 'relation' the author means 'judgment' (hukm). This is because the philosophers define tasdiq as perception of the occurrence or non-occurrence of a relation. Note the shift: tasdiq is not just perceiving a relation; it is perceiving it with a judgment of its truth value.
The term 'nisba' (relation) is used metaphorically for 'hukm'.
2
Extract the genus and differentia
The genus (jins) is 'perception' (idrak). The differentia (fasl) is 'with a judgment' — specifically, knowledge or belief that the relation holds or does not hold. This makes tasdiq a kind of perception that includes a truth claim.
The differentia is the judgment aspect, which distinguishes tasdiq from mere concept formation (tasawwur).
3
Determine the scope: what counts as tasdiq
The commentator explicitly states that opinion (zann) qualifies as tasdiq because it involves belief (i'tiqad), though not certain. Doubt (shakk) and illusion (wahm) are excluded because they lack belief altogether. Thus, any mental state that affirms or denies a relation, even with probability, is a tasdiq.
This is a key clarification: tasdiq does not require certainty.
4
Extend to conditional propositions
The definition also covers conjunctive and disjunctive propositions (shartiyyat). The perception of the content of such propositions—whether the relation is affirmative or negative—is also tasdiq, as long as it involves a judgment.
The commentator notes that this extension adds little new, because the relation concept already applies to categorical and conditional statements alike.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَأَمَّا التَّصْدِيقُ فَفَسَّرَهُ بِـ : «أَنَّهُ إِدْرَاكُ النِّسْبَةِ»، وَأَرَادَ بِهَا : الحُكْمَ؛ لِيُطَابِقَ قَوْلَ جُمْهُورِ الحُكَمَاءِ : أَنَّ التَّصْدِيقَ هُوَ : إِدْرَاكُ وُقُوع النِّسْبَةِ أَوْ لَا وُقُوعِهَا»، وَهُوَ مُرَادِفٌ لِلْحُكْمِ ; أَي : العِلْمُ بِتُبُوتِ أَمْرٍ لِأَمْرِ أَوِ انْتِفَاءِ أَمْرٍ عَنْ أَمْرِ.
قوله : (وَأَرَادَ بِهَا : الحُكْمَ) أي : فهو من باب استعمال اللفظ في غير ما وُضِعَ له وحمله على هذا التّجوز عدم وجدان قول بكون مسمى التصديق النسبة فقط .
قوله : (هُوَ : إِدْرَاكُ وُقُوع النِّسْبَةِ) معنى قولهم : إدراك وقوع النسبة... إلخ؛ أي: العلم بوقوعها أو لا ; أي: اعتقاد أنَّها واقعة أو ليست بواقعة؛ سواء كان ذلك الاعتقاد جازماً أم لا، فيدخل : الظَّنُّ ، دون الشَّكِّ والوَهم؛ إذ لا اعتقاد فيهما . وهذا المعنى الَّذي فسَّر به التصديق هو معنى الحكم عند المناطقة، كما أشار إليه الشارح بقوله : «وهو مرادف للحكم ; أي: العلم بثبوت ... إلخ » هذا هو الحكم أيضاً عند المتكلمين . وحاصله : أنَّ التصديق مرادفٌ للحكم عند المناطقة، والحكم عند المناطقة يرادف الحكم عند المتكلمين، بل هو بعينه ، ثمَّ إِنَّ قولهم: وقوع النسبة أو لا وقوعها» يُوهم - كما قال شيخنا سيدي الطَّيِّب - أن لا نسبة في السَّلب، وليس كذلك، ولكنَّهم أرادوا النِّسبة الثبوتية.
(۱) في (ج) : «بِقَوْلِهِ : إِنَّهُ» بدلاً من بـ: أَنَّهُ».
أَوْ بِوُقُوع النِّسْبَةِ الاتِّصَالِيَّةِ وَالانْفِصَالِيَّةِ، فَإِدْرَاكُ مَضْمُونِ ذَلِكَ كُلُّهُ تَصْدِيقٌ ; سَوَاءٌ كَانَ جَازِماً أَمَّ لَا، مُطَابِقاً لِلْوَاقِعِ أَمْ لَا .
قوله : (الاتِّصَالِيَّةِ وَالِانْفِصَالِيَّةِ) على حذف موصوف; أي: في القضيَّة الاتصالية، أو في القضيَّة الانفصالية، لكن ليس فيه كبير فائدة; إذ النِّسبة لا تختلفُ ثبوتاً وانتفاء باعتبار الحمليّات والشَّرطيات .
قوله : (أَمْ لَا يدخل فيه - كما تقدَّم - : الظَّنُّ فقط، دون الشَّلِّ والوهم; إذ لا حكم فيهما.
As for tasdiq, he interpreted it as: 'It is the perception of the relation,' and he intended by it: the judgment; to match the statement of the majority of philosophers: that tasdiq is the perception of the occurrence of the relation or its non-occurrence, and it is synonymous with judgment; i.e., knowledge of the establishment of a thing for a thing or the negation of a thing from a thing. His statement: ('and he intended by it: the judgment') means: this is from the category of using a word in other than what it was coined for, and his interpretation of it as this figurative usage is due to not finding a statement that the meaning of tasdiq is only the relation. His statement: ('it is the perception of the occurrence of the relation') the meaning of their statement 'perception of the occurrence of the relation... etc.' i.e., knowledge of its occurrence or not; i.e., belief that it occurs or does not occur; whether that belief is certain or not, so opinion enters into it, but not doubt and illusion, for there is no belief in them. And this meaning with which he interpreted tasdiq is the meaning of judgment according to the logicians, as the commentator indicated by his statement: 'and it is synonymous with judgment; i.e., knowledge of the establishment... etc.' This is also the judgment according to the theologians. The summary is: that tasdiq is synonymous with judgment according to the logicians, and judgment according to the logicians is synonymous with judgment according to the theologians, indeed it is the same. Then, their statement 'the occurrence of the relation or its non-occurrence' suggests - as our teacher Sayyidi al-Tayyib said - that there is no relation in negation, but it is not so; rather they intended the affirmative relation. (1) In (j): 'by his statement: that it' instead of 'by: that it'. Or by the occurrence of the conjunctive or disjunctive relation, so the perception of the content of all of that is assent; whether it is certain or not, corresponding to reality or not. His statement: (the conjunctive and disjunctive) is with an omitted described; i.e., in the conjunctive proposition or in the disjunctive proposition, but there is no great benefit in it; for the relation does not differ in terms of existence and non-existence with regard to categorical and conditional [propositions]. His statement: (or not) - it includes in it - as previously - only opinion, not doubt and illusion; for there is no judgment in them.
Source pages p. 423

Commentary
This passage is a definitional expansion of tasdiq (assent). The author begins with the matn definition: tasdiq is the perception of the relation (nisba), but clarifies that the intended meaning is the judgment (hukm) to align with the philosophers who define it as perception of the occurrence or non-occurrence of a relation. This judgment is synonymous with knowledge of a thing's establishment for another or its negation. The commentary then explains that the word 'nisba' is used metaphorically for 'hukm' because no authority defined tasdiq solely as perception of the relation. Next, the commentator expands on the phrase 'perception of the occurrence of the relation': it means belief that the relation holds or does not hold, whether certain or merely opinion (zann), so opinion qualifies as tasdiq, but doubt and illusion do not because they lack belief. This meaning of tasdiq is identical to the logicians' concept of judgment, which is also what the theologians call judgment. Then a subtle point: the phrase 'occurrence or non-occurrence of the relation' might imply that negative propositions have no relation, but the intended meaning is the affirmative relation (i.e., the relation of a predicate to a subject, even in negatives it is considered a relation). Finally, the definition is extended to conditional propositions (conjunctive and disjunctive): the perception of their content is also tasdiq, regardless of certainty or correspondence to reality. The commentary notes that the mention of conjunctive/disjunctive is redundant because the relation does not differ between categorical and conditional propositions. It also reiterates that only opinion is included, not doubt or illusion.

Key Terms
تَصْدِيق (tasdiq): Perception of a relation with a judgment of its occurrence or non-occurrence; synonymous with hukm (judgment). [Note: No significant shift; stable across the tradition, though some earlier philosophers may have emphasized certainty.]
حُكْم (hukm): The mental act of affirming or denying something of something; equivalent to tasdiq in this context. [Note: In usul al-fiqh, hukm often means a legal ruling; here it is used epistemologically.]

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is considered a tasdiq?
A) Doubting whether the world is eternal.
B) Believing that Zayd's standing is probable.
C) Imagining a flying horse.
D) Understanding the meaning of 'book' without judgment.

Key Takeaway
Tasdiq is defined as perception of a relation with a judgment, and it includes opinion but excludes doubt and illusion.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Consider the following mental states and determine, based on the definition in this lesson, whether each qualifies as tasdiq: (a) A mufti is 70% sure that a particular transaction is riba, but not certain. (b) A student hears the phrase 'God is one' and understands its meaning but does not yet believe it. (c) Someone imagines a flying horse but knows it is not real. Explain your reasoning for each.
?
Construct your own definition of tasdiq in Arabic following the pattern: 'tasdiq is the perception of ... with ...' and test whether it includes opinion and excludes doubt, as required by the logicians.

Al-Razi's Composite Definition of Tasdiq
Imam al-Razi defines tasdiq as four perceptions, with a biographical sketch of the scholar.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the four components of tasdiq according to Imam al-Razi and compare his definition with the standard two-component definition.

Core Idea
Tasdiq is not a single judgment but a composite of four distinct perceptions.

Most logicians define tasdiq as the perception of a relation with a judgment, but Imam al-Razi offers a more detailed analysis. In this passage, we see his unique view that tasdiq comprises four perceptions: the subject, predicate, relational judgment, and the judgment of occurrence. Understanding this expansion helps us appreciate the complexity of mental acts in Islamic logic.

Guided Path
1
Identify the term being defined
The definiendum is 'tasdiq' (تصديق). Note that this is a key term in logic, often contrasted with 'tasawwur' (concept).
Al-Razi's definition is more detailed than the usual one.
2
List the four perceptions
Al-Razi specifies: (1) perception of the subject (المحكوم عليه), (2) perception of the predicate (المحكوم به), (3) perception of the relational judgment (النسبة الحكمية), (4) perception that this relation occurs or does not occur (أنها واقعة أو ليست بواقعة).
The fourth perception is the actual judgment or assent.
3
Understand the function of each component
Each perception is a distinct mental act. The first two grasp the terms, the third grasps the connection, and the fourth adds the claim that the connection holds in reality (or not).
Without the fourth, you only have a concept of the relation, not assent.
4
Compare with the standard definition
Most logicians (e.g., al-Bajuri) define tasdiq as simply two perceptions: the relational judgment and the judgment of occurrence. Al-Razi splits the terms as well, making it four.
This shows al-Razi's expansionist approach.
5
Apply to an example from kalam
Take the proposition 'The world is temporally originated.' The four perceptions are: perception of 'world', perception of 'temporally originated', perception of the subject-predicate relation, and perception that this relation actually holds.
This breakdown clarifies the mental steps in affirming a proposition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَعِنْدَ الإِمَامِ الرَّازِيِّ : التَّصْدِيقُ عِبَارَةٌ عَنْ مَجْمُوعِ أَرْبَعَةِ إِدْرَاكَاتٍ : إِدْرَاكِ المَحْكُومِ عَلَيْهِ ، وَإِدْرَاكُ المَحْكُومِ بِهِ ، وَإِدْرَاكِ النِّسْبَةِ الحُكْمِيَّةِ ، وَإِدْرَاكِ أَنَّهَا رَاقِعَةٌ أَوْ لَيْسَتْ وَاقِعَةً؛
قوله : (وَإِدْرَاكِ أَنَّهَا رَاقِعَةٌ) أي: الحكم بذلك .
قوله : (وَعِنْدَ الإِمَامِ الرَّازِيِّ) وهو الملقَّب بـ «الفخر» أيضاً، وهو الإمام أبو عبد الله محمد بن عمر بن الحسين البكري الطبرستاني الأصل الرَّازي المولد ، المعروف بابن الخطيب . ((فاق أهل زمانه في علم الكلام وعلم الأوائل، وله التّصانيف العجيبة والاختراعات الغريبة، ومناقبه أكثر من أن تُحصى، حكى شرف الدين بن عنين : أنَّه حضر درسه يوماً بخوارزم، وكان اليوم شاتياً وقد سقط ثلج كثير، وخوارزم بردها في غاية الشِّدَّة، فسقطت بالقرب منه حمامة وقد طردها بعض الجوارح، فلما وقعت لم تقدر على الطيران من شدة البرد والخوف، فلما قام الإمام مِنَ الدرس وقف عليها، وأخذها فأنشده ابن عنين في الحال من أبياتٍ من الكامل] مَنْ نَبَّأَ الوَرْقَاءَ أَنَّ مَحَلَّكُمْ حَرَمُ، وَأَنَّكَ مَلْجَأَ لِلْخَائِف؟ وَفَدَتْ عَلَيْكَ وَقَدْ تَدَانَى حَنْفُهَا فَحَيَوْتَهَا بِبَقَائِهَا المُسْتَانَفِ توفي كلته بالرّي يوم الاثنين عيد الفطر سنة ست وست مئة بمدينة هراة، وهو ابن ثلاث وستين ومن نظمه : [من الطويل] نِهَايَةُ أَقْدَامِ العُقُولِ عِقَالُ وَأَكْثَرُ سَعْيِ العَالِمِينَ ضَلَالُ وَلَمْ نَسْتَفِدْ مِنْ بَحْثِنَا طُوْلَ عُمْرِنَا سِوَى أَنْ جَمَعْنَا فِيْهِ قِيلَ وَقَالُوا وَأَرْوَاحُنَا فِي وَحْشَةٍ مِنْ جُسُومِنَا وَحَاصِلُ دُنْيَانَا أَذًى وَوَبَالُ
And according to Imam al-Razi: tasdiq is an expression for a total of four perceptions: the perception of the subject, the perception of the predicate, the perception of the relational judgment, and the perception that it occurs or does not occur. His statement: (and the perception that it occurs) i.e., the judgment of that. His statement: (and according to Imam al-Razi) and he is also nicknamed 'al-Fakhr', and he is Imam Abu Abdullah Muhammad ibn Umar ibn al-Husayn al-Bakri al-Tabaristani by origin, al-Razi by birth, known as Ibn al-Khatib. He surpassed the scholars of his time in kalam and the sciences of the ancients, and he has amazing compositions and strange inventions, and his merits are too many to be counted. Sharf al-Din ibn 'Unayn narrated: that he attended his lesson one day in Khwarazm, and it was a wintry day and a lot of snow had fallen, and Khwarazm's cold is extremely severe. A pigeon fell near him, chased by some birds of prey. When it fell, it could not fly due to the intense cold and fear. When the Imam stood up from the lesson, he stopped by it and took it. Ibn 'Unayn immediately recited to him from verses of the Kamil meter: 'Who told the pigeon that your place is a sanctuary, and that you are a refuge for the frightened? It came to you when its death drew near, and you revived it with its renewed existence.' He died, may Allah have mercy on him, in Rayy on Monday, the day of Fitr, the year 606 [AH] in the city of Herat, and he was sixty-three years old. And from his poetry: [Tawil meter] 'The limit of the feet of intellects is a shackle, and most of the striving of scholars is misguidance. We have not gained from our research over our long lives except that we collected in it 'they said' and 'they spoke'. And our souls are in loneliness from our bodies, and the sum of our world is harm and calamity.'
Source pages p. 424

Commentary
This passage presents a definition of tasdiq from Imam Fakhr al-Din al-Razi and includes a biographical sketch. Al-Razi's definition is distinctive: tasdiq consists of four perceptions combined: the perception of the subject (mahkum 'alayh), the perception of the predicate (mahkum bihi), the perception of the relational judgment (al-nisba al-hukmiyya), and the perception that this relation occurs or does not occur (i.e., the judgment itself). The commentator clarifies that the fourth is the judgment. Thus, al-Razi considers tasdiq to be a composite of these four cognitive acts. The commentary then provides a biography of al-Razi, noting his title 'al-Fakhr', his full name, and his excellence in kalam and ancient sciences. A story is told about his compassion: during a snowstorm, a pigeon fell near him, and he saved it, prompting a spontaneous poetic verse from a student. The passage ends with al-Razi's death details and two lines of his poetry reflecting on the limitations of human intellect and the futility of worldly pursuits.

إدراك
محكوم عليه
محكوم به
نسبة حكمية

Key Takeaway
Al-Razi expands the standard two-perception definition of tasdiq to four, emphasizing the distinct mental acts of grasping subject, predicate, relation, and assent.
