The Dispute over Tasdiq: Simple or Composite?
Author presents the majority view that tasdiq is simple and al-Sayyid's justification.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the majority view that tasdiq is simple from the Imam's view that it is composite of four perceptions, and identify the status of the three preliminary perceptions under each view.

Core Idea
The debate about tasdiq's structure is not semantic but methodological.

In this passage, the author presents two competing positions on the internal composition of tasdiq (assent). The majority of logicians hold that tasdiq is simple, while Imam Fakhr al-Din al-Razi argues it is composed of four parts. The three preliminary perceptions—conception, judgment?—are considered conditions for tasdiq by the majority, but parts of it by the Imam. Understanding this dispute is crucial because it affects how we define the subject matter of logic and the methods of acquiring knowledge.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two views on tasdiq
Find where the author states the majority (jumhūr) view that tasdiq is simple and the Imam's view that it is composite. Note the Arabic phrases: 'عند الجمهور بسيط' and 'عند الإمام مركب من أربعة أجزاء'.
2
Determine the status of the three perceptions
The passage says that the first three perceptions are 'shurut' (conditions) for tasdiq according to the majority, but 'ajza' (parts) according to the Imam. Understand the difference: conditions are external prerequisites, parts are internal constituents.
3
Recognize al-Sayyid's vindication of the majority
Al-Sayyid al-Sharif al-Jurjani supports the majority using a methodological argument. Identify his key point: the division of knowledge is based on distinct methods, and grouping the three perceptions with judgment would not yield a new method.
This sets the stage for the next lesson.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فَهُوَ عِنْدَ الجُمْهُورِ بَسِيطٌ ، وَعِنْدَ الإِمَامِ مُرَكَّبٌ مِنْ أَرْبَعَةِ أَجْزَاءٍ، وَالإِدْرَاكَاتُ [ب/ ٦] الثَّلَاثَةُ الأُولُ عِنْدَهُمْ : شُرُوطٌ لَهُ، وَعِنْدَهُ : أَجْزَاءٌ لَهُ. وَرَبَّحَ السَّيِّدُ مَذْهَبَ الجُمْهُورِ بِأَنَّ تَقْسِيمَ العِلْمِ إِلَى هَذَيْنِ القِسْمَيْنِ إِنَّمَا هُوَ لِامْتِيَازِ كُلِّ مِنْهُمَا عَنِ الآخَرِ بِطَرِيقٍ يُسْتَحْصَلُ بِهِ، وَقَدِ اخْتُصَّ الإِدْرَاكُ المُسَمَّى بِالحُكْمِ بِطَرِيق وَاحِدٍ وَهُوَ الحُجَّةُ، وَمَا عَدَاهُ مِنْ سَائِرِ الإِدْرَاكَاتِ لَهُ طَرِيقٌ آخَرُ هُوَ القَوْلُ الشَّارِحُ، فَلَا فَائِدَةَ فِي ضَمِّ الإِدْرَاكَاتِ الثَّلَاثَةِ إِلَى الحُكْمِ مَعَ مُشَارَكَتِهَا لِسَائِرِ التَّصَوُّرَاتِ فِي طَرِيقِهَا ؛ إِذْ لَمْ يَجْعَلُوا لِهَذَا المَجْمُوعِ طَرِيقاً يَخُصُّهُ ، فَمَنْ لَاحَظَ مَقْصُودَ هَذَا الفَنِّ وَهُوَ بَيَانُ الطَّرِيقِ المُوَصِّلِ إِلَى العِلْمِ لَمْ يَلْتَبِسْ عَلَيْهِ أَنَّ الوَاجِبَ فِي تَقْسِيمِهِ مُلَاحَظَةُ الامْتِيَازِ فِي الطَّرِيقِ . اهـ
Thus, according to the majority (al-jumhūr), it (tasdīq) is simple, while according to the Imam (Fakhr al-Dīn al-Rāzī), it is composed of four parts. The first three perceptions according to them (the majority) are conditions for it, and according to him (the Imam) they are parts of it. Al-Sayyid (al-Sharīf al-Jurjānī) vindicated the doctrine of the majority by [arguing that] the division of knowledge into these two divisions is only for the distinction of each from the other by a method by which it is obtained. The perception called judgment (ḥukm) has been singled out by one method, namely the proof (al-ḥujja), while the rest of the perceptions have another method, namely the explicatory statement (al-qawl al-shāriḥ). There is no benefit in attaching the three perceptions to judgment, given their sharing with the rest of the concepts (taṣawwurāt) in their method, since they did not assign to this aggregate a method that is specific to it. So whoever considers the purpose of this art, which is the exposition of the method that leads to knowledge, will not be confused that what is required in its division is the observation of distinction in method. End.
Source pages p. 425

Commentary
This passage is a commentary that presents the differing views on the composition of tasdīq (assent). The majority (jumhūr) hold that tasdīq is a simple entity, while the Imam (Fakhr al-Dīn al-Rāzī) holds it is composed of four parts: the three perceptions (conception, judgment, and something else?) actually the text refers to the three perceptions (idrākāt) as conditions for the fourth (judgment) according to the majority, and as parts according to the Imam. Al-Sayyid al-Sharīf al-Jurjānī then supports the majority view with a methodological argument: The division of knowledge into tasawwur (conception) and tasdīq (assent) is based on the distinct methods by which each is obtained. Judgment (ḥukm) has its own unique method—the proof (ḥujja). All other perceptions (including the three preliminary ones) share the method of explicatory statement (qawl shāriḥ). Therefore, attaching those three perceptions to judgment to form a composite tasdīq would not create a new method, defeating the purpose of the division. The commentator concludes that observance of distinction in method is the correct criterion for dividing knowledge.

التصديق
الحكم
الطريق

Key Takeaway
The dispute over tasdiq's composition is not merely verbal; it reflects different views on whether tasdiq has internal parts or is a simple entity, with implications for the method of logic.

Al-Sayyid's Methodological Criterion for Dividing Knowledge
Author presents the majority view that tasdiq is simple and al-Sayyid's justification.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply al-Sayyid al-Sharif's criterion that the division of knowledge must be based on distinct methods to evaluate the soundness of a proposed division.

Core Idea
Division of knowledge by method reveals that tasdiq must be simple.

Al-Sayyid al-Sharif al-Jurjani provides a powerful justification for the majority view by appealing to the very purpose of logic: exposition of the method leading to knowledge. He argues that if we divide knowledge into conception and assent, we must do so based on distinct methods. Judgment has a unique method—the proof—while all other perceptions share the method of explicatory statement. Therefore, combining the three perceptions with judgment would not yield a new method, rendering a composite tasdiq pointless. This lesson unpacks that argument and shows how to use the criterion.

Guided Path
1
Extract al-Sayyid's central criterion
Identify the sentence: 'the division of knowledge into these two divisions is only for the distinction of each from the other by a method by which it is obtained.' This means that the basis for dividing knowledge into conception and assent must be that each has a unique method (ṭarīq).
2
Determine the method of judgment (ḥukm)
Al-Sayyid says: 'The perception called judgment has been singled out by one method, namely the proof (al-ḥujja).' Therefore, the defining method of judgment, and thus of assent, is argumentation.
3
Determine the method of the other three perceptions
He says: 'the rest of the perceptions have another method, namely the explicatory statement (al-qawl al-shāriḥ).' This includes the three preliminary perceptions and all conceptions. Their method is definition and explanation.
4
Evaluate why composite tasdiq fails the criterion
If we group the three perceptions with judgment to form a composite tasdiq, the composite would not have a unique method because the three perceptions already share the method of conceptions. Thus, the composite would not be distinguished from conception by method, defeating the purpose of division.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فَهُوَ عِنْدَ الجُمْهُورِ بَسِيطٌ ، وَعِنْدَ الإِمَامِ مُرَكَّبٌ مِنْ أَرْبَعَةِ أَجْزَاءٍ، وَالإِدْرَاكَاتُ [ب/ ٦] الثَّلَاثَةُ الأُولُ عِنْدَهُمْ : شُرُوطٌ لَهُ، وَعِنْدَهُ : أَجْزَاءٌ لَهُ. وَرَبَّحَ السَّيِّدُ مَذْهَبَ الجُمْهُورِ بِأَنَّ تَقْسِيمَ العِلْمِ إِلَى هَذَيْنِ القِسْمَيْنِ إِنَّمَا هُوَ لِامْتِيَازِ كُلِّ مِنْهُمَا عَنِ الآخَرِ بِطَرِيقٍ يُسْتَحْصَلُ بِهِ، وَقَدِ اخْتُصَّ الإِدْرَاكُ المُسَمَّى بِالحُكْمِ بِطَرِيق وَاحِدٍ وَهُوَ الحُجَّةُ، وَمَا عَدَاهُ مِنْ سَائِرِ الإِدْرَاكَاتِ لَهُ طَرِيقٌ آخَرُ هُوَ القَوْلُ الشَّارِحُ، فَلَا فَائِدَةَ فِي ضَمِّ الإِدْرَاكَاتِ الثَّلَاثَةِ إِلَى الحُكْمِ مَعَ مُشَارَكَتِهَا لِسَائِرِ التَّصَوُّرَاتِ فِي طَرِيقِهَا ؛ إِذْ لَمْ يَجْعَلُوا لِهَذَا المَجْمُوعِ طَرِيقاً يَخُصُّهُ ، فَمَنْ لَاحَظَ مَقْصُودَ هَذَا الفَنِّ وَهُوَ بَيَانُ الطَّرِيقِ المُوَصِّلِ إِلَى العِلْمِ لَمْ يَلْتَبِسْ عَلَيْهِ أَنَّ الوَاجِبَ فِي تَقْسِيمِهِ مُلَاحَظَةُ الامْتِيَازِ فِي الطَّرِيقِ . اهـ
Thus, according to the majority (al-jumhūr), it (tasdīq) is simple, while according to the Imam (Fakhr al-Dīn al-Rāzī), it is composed of four parts. The first three perceptions according to them (the majority) are conditions for it, and according to him (the Imam) they are parts of it. Al-Sayyid (al-Sharīf al-Jurjānī) vindicated the doctrine of the majority by [arguing that] the division of knowledge into these two divisions is only for the distinction of each from the other by a method by which it is obtained. D) Because the majority never intended a composite.

Key Takeaway
Al-Sayyid's criterion that divisions of knowledge must be based on distinct methods is a powerful tool for evaluating classifications in logic and other Islamic sciences.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Consider a proposal to divide knowledge into 'intellectual' (ʿaqlī) and 'transmitted' (naqlī) based on source. Apply al-Sayyid's method-based criterion: Do they have distinct methods of acquisition? Explain why or why not.
?
In usul al-fiqh, knowledge is often divided into 'daruri' (necessary) and 'nazari' (theoretical). Evaluate this division using al-Sayyid's criterion. Are the methods distinct?

Definitions of Judgment and Their Implications for Assent
Author enumerates definitions of hukm and derives consequences for tasdiq.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the three definitions of hukm (judgment) and explain why each prevents defining tasdiq (assent) as hukm.

Core Idea
If judgment is an act or passion, it cannot be assent, because assent is a quality.

In the previous lesson, we learned that knowledge is divided into concept (tasawwur) and assent (tasdiq). But what exactly is assent? Many logicians define it as judgment (hukm). However, as this passage shows, there is disagreement about the nature of judgment itself. Understanding these definitions is crucial because they determine whether tasdiq can be equated with hukm at all.

Guided Path
1
List the three definitions of hukm
From the Arabic passage, extract the three views: hukm as an act of the soul, as speech of the soul (also an act), and as a passion.
Note that the second is a refinement of the first.
2
Identify the common category
All three definitions place hukm either in the category of action (fi'l) or passion (infi'al). Recognize that the author groups them as such.
This is crucial for the argument.
3
Recall the category of knowledge
Knowledge (including tasdiq) belongs to the category of quality (kayf). The passage states this explicitly.
Quality is distinct from action and passion.
4
Apply the category distinction
Since tasdiq is a quality, it cannot be identical to something that is an action or passion. Therefore, defining tasdiq as hukm is invalid if hukm is an act or passion.
This refutes both the majority view and the Imam's view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَاعْلَمْ أَنَّهُ اخْتُلِفَ فِي الحُكْمِ : فَقِيلَ: «هُوَ : فِعْلُ لِلْنَّفْسِ زَائِدٌ عَلَى العِلْمِ». وَقِيلَ: «هُوَ حَدِيثُ النَّفْسِ التَّابِعُ لِلْعِلْمِ، وَهَذَا أَيْضاً فِعْلٌ، فَلَا يُنَافِي الأَوَّلَ». وَقِيلَ: «هُوَ : انْفِعَالٌ، وَهُوَ : تَأثِيرُ النَّفْسِ النَّاشِيُّ عَنِ العِلْمِ، وَعَلَيْهِمَا لَا يَصِحُ تَفْسِيرُ التَّصْدِيقِ بِالحُكْمِ كَمَا عِنْدَ الجُمْهُورِ، وَلَا بِمَجْمُوعِ الإِدْرَاكَاتِ الَّتِي رَابِعُهَا الحُكْمُ كَمَا عِنْدَ الإِمَامِ؛ لِأَنَّ التَّصْدِيقَ قِسْمٌ مِنَ العِلْمِ، وَالعِلْمُ مِنْ مَقُولَةِ الكَيْفِ مُبَايِنُ لِلْفِعْلِ وَالانْفِعَالِ.
And know that there is disagreement concerning judgment (al-ḥukm). For it was said: 'It is an act of the soul (fiʿl li-l-nafs) additional to knowledge.' And it was said: 'It is a speech of the soul (ḥadīth al-nafs) following knowledge, and this too is an act, so it does not contradict the first.' And it was said: 'It is a passion (infiʿāl), and it is the impression of the soul (taʾthīr al-nafs) arising from knowledge.' And according to both [views that it is act or passion], it is not valid to interpret tasdīq as judgment as according to the majority, nor as the aggregate of perceptions whose fourth is judgment as according to the Imam, because tasdīq is a division of knowledge, and knowledge belongs to the category of quality (kayf), which is distinct from act and passion.
Source pages p. 425

Commentary
This passage is a critical exposition of the different definitions of judgment (ḥukm) and their consequences for the definition of tasdīq (assent). The commentator lists three opinions: (1) judgment is an act of the soul additional to knowledge, (2) it is a speech of the soul (ḥadīth al-nafs) that follows knowledge, which is also an act, (3) it is a passion (infiʿāl), i.e., an impression of the soul arising from knowledge. The crucial point is that both views (judgment as act or passion) have the implication that it is incorrect to define tasdīq either as judgment (the majority view) or as the aggregate of perceptions whose fourth is judgment (the Imam's view). The reason given is that tasdīq is a division of knowledge, and knowledge belongs to the category of quality (kayf). Quality is distinct from both action (fiʿl) and passion (infiʿāl) as categories of accident. Therefore, if judgment is an act or passion, it cannot be the same as tasdīq, since they belong to different Aristotelian categories. This undermines the standard definitions of tasdīq.

Key Terms
الحكم
التصديق
الكيف

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the commentator argue that tasdiq cannot be defined as judgment (hukm) according to those who say hukm is an act or passion?
A) Because tasdiq is a quality (kayf), while act and passion are different categories.
B) Because tasdiq is a composite of four parts.
C) Because judgment is only a condition for tasdiq.
D) Because the majority and Imam agree on the definition of tasdiq.

Key Takeaway
The definition of judgment (hukm) as act or passion prevents it from being identical to assent (tasdiq), because assent belongs to the category of quality.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

Three Types of Relational Attributes: Where Does Dalala Belong?
Author classifies relational attributes to refine the definition of dalala

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify a relational attribute into one of three types and determine whether it applies to the utterance or the hearer.

Core Idea
Dalala is a property of the utterance, not of understanding — like fatherhood, not brotherhood.

This passage from Bannani’s matn and Bajuri’s commentary refines the definition of dalala (signification). The author distinguishes three ways a relational attribute can subsist between two things. Understanding (fahm) is a relation between hearer, meaning, and utterance, but signification is a property of the utterance alone. This distinction is foundational for logic: the subject matter of logic is utterances insofar as they signify. Grasping this classification prevents conflating the act of understanding with the signifying property of the utterance.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three types of relational attributes
The author lists three kinds: (1) subsisting in each relatum (e.g., brotherhood between two people); (2) subsisting in one relatum and connected to the other (e.g., fatherhood in the father, connected to the son); (3) subsisting in the totality of both (e.g., resemblance). Note where the attribute inheres in each case.
Arabic terms: al-ukhuwwa (brotherhood), al-ubuwwa (fatherhood), al-tashabuh (resemblance).
2
Map understanding (fahm) and signification (dalala) to a type
Understanding subsists in the hearer and is connected to both meaning and utterance — it belongs to type 2 but inheres in the hearer. Signification subsists in the utterance and is connected to the meaning — also type 2, but inheres in the utterance. Neither is type 1 because both do not inhere in both relata equally.
The author explicitly says dalala is from the same category as fatherhood.
3
Examine the grammatical evidence for understanding's connection
The author points to the preposition 'min' in 'fahima al-sami‘ al-ma‘na min al-lafz' (the hearer understood the meaning from the utterance). The preposition shows that the utterance is the source, not the subject, of understanding. Thus, the utterance acquires the attribute of being 'that from which the meaning is understood' — which is precisely signification.
This grammatical analysis confirms that signification is a property of the utterance, not of the hearer.
4
Apply the classification to an Islamic science example
Consider the term 'hukm' (ruling) in usul al-fiqh. Does it subsist in the Lawgiver, the act, or both? Using the three-type classification, argue that hukm is like fatherhood: it subsists in the Lawgiver and is connected to the act. This clarifies that the act itself does not 'have' a ruling inherently; the ruling is an attribute of the Lawgiver's address.
This shows the practical value of the classification in avoiding conceptual confusion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
نَعَمْ ؛ يُفْهَمُ مِنْ تَعَلَّقِهِ بِاللَّفْظِ صِفَةٌ لَهُ هِيَ كَوْنُهُ مَنْهُوماً مِنْهُ المَعْنَى . وَحَاصِلُ مَا ذَكَرَهُ أَنَّ كَوْنَ الفَهْمِ نِسْبَةً بَيْنَ السَّامِعِ وَالمَعْنَى، وَاللَّفْظُ لَا يَسْتَلْزِمُ أَنْ يَكُونَ صِفَةً حَقِيقِيَّةً لِكُلٍّ مِنْهَا، وَذَلِكَ لِأَنَّ مِنَ المَعَانِي النِّسْبِيَّةِ : - مَا هُوَ قَائِمٌ بِكُلٍّ مِنَ المُنْتَسِبَيْنِ، فَيُوصَفُ بِهَا كُلٌّ مِنْهُمَا كَـ: الْأُخُوَّةِ الَّتِي بَيْنَ زَيْدٍ وَعَمْرٍو، وَالشَّرِكَةِ الَّتِي بَيْنَهُمَا . - وَمِنْهَا مَا هُوَ قَائِمٌ بِأَحَدِهِمَا مُتَعَلِّقٌ بِالْآخَرِ، فَيُوصَفُ بِهَا مَنْ قَامَتْ بِهِ، لَا مَنْ تَعَلَّقَتْ بِهِ كَـ: الْأُبُوَّةِ، فَإِنَّهَا قَائِمَةٌ بِالْأَبِ مُتَعَلِّقَةٌ بِالِابْنِ، فَلَا يَصِحُّ وَصْفُ الِابْنِ بِهَا، وَمِنْ هَذَا القَبِيلِ الفَهْمُ وَالدَّلَالَةُ كَمَا يَشْهَدُ بِهِ الِاشْتِقَاقُ، فَلَا يَصِحُّ وَصْفُ اللَّفْظِ بِالفَهْمِ حَقِيقَةً، وَإِنَّمَا يَصِحُّ وَصْفُهُ بِكَوْنِهِ مَفْهُوماً مِنْهُ . - وَمِنْهَا مَا هُوَ قَائِمٌ بِمَجْمُوعِ المُنْتَسِبَيْنِ فَلَا يُوصَفُ بِهَا أَحَدُهُمَا، بَلْ مَجْمُوعُهُمَا كَ: التَّشَابُهِ؛ فَيُقَالُ : زَيْدٌ وَعَمْرٌو مُتَشَابِهَانِ . قَوْلُهُ : (نَعَمْ؛ يُفْهَمُ مِنْ تَعَلُّقِهِ بِاللَّفْظِ) أَيْ: بِوَاسِطَةِ حَرْفِ الْجَرِّ. وَأَشَارَ إِلَى أَنَّ الفَهْمَ وَإِنْ كَانَ صِفَةً قَائِمَةً بِالسَّامِعِ فَقَطْ، لَكِنَّهُ مُتَعَلِّقٌ بِالمَعْنَى بِغَيْرِ وَاسِطَةٍ، وَبِاللَّفْظِ بِوَاسِطَةِ حَرْفِ الْجَرِّ؛ كَمَا يَدُلُّ عَلَيْهِ قَوْلُكَ: «فَهِمَ السَّامِعُ المَعْنَى مِنَ اللَّفْظِ»، فَهُنَاكَ ثَلَاثَةُ أَشْيَاءَ: الفَهْمُ، وَتَعَلُّقُهُ بِالمَعْنَى، وَتَعَلُّقُهُ بِاللَّفْظِ؛ فَالْأَوَّلُ: صِفَةٌ لِلسَّامِعِ، وَالْآخِرَانِ: صِفَةٌ لِلْفَهْمِ، وَإِذَا تَبَيَّنَ أَنَّ الفَهْمَ لَهُ تَعَلُّقٌ بِاللَّفْظِ، فَيُوصَفُ اللَّفْظُ بِالحَالَةِ الَّتِي حَصَلَتْ لَهُ مِنْ تَعَلُّقِ فَهْمِ السَّامِعِ بِهِ، وَهِيَ كَوْنُهُ مَفْهُوماً مِنْهُ المَعْنَى.
Yes; it is understood from its connection with the utterance a description for it, which is its being that from which the meaning is understood. The gist of what he mentioned is that the fact that understanding is a relation between the hearer and the meaning, and the utterance does not necessitate that it be a real description for each of them. That is because among relational meanings: (1) What subsists in each of the two relata, so each is described by it, like brotherhood between Zayd and 'Amr, and partnership between them. (2) Among them is what subsists in one of them and is connected to the other, so one in whom it subsists is described by it, not the one to which it is connected, like fatherhood; for it subsists in the father and is connected to the son, so it is not correct to describe the son with it. From this category are understanding and signification, as derivation witnesses, so it is not correct to describe the utterance with understanding in reality; rather it is correct to describe it with its being that from which it is understood. (3) Among them is what subsists in the totality of the two relata, so neither is described by it individually, but rather their totality, like resemblance; so it is said: Zayd and 'Amr resemble each other. His statement: 'Yes; it is understood from its connection with the utterance' i.e., by means of the preposition. He indicated that understanding, although it is a description subsisting in the hearer only, is connected to the meaning without mediation, and to the utterance by means of the preposition, as indicated by your saying: 'The hearer understood the meaning from the utterance.' So there are three things: the understanding, its connection with the meaning, and its connection with the utterance. The first is a description of the hearer; the last two are descriptions of the understanding. When it is clear that understanding has a connection with the utterance, then the utterance is described by the state that it acquired from the connection of the hearer's understanding with it, which is its being that from which the meaning is understood.
Source pages p. 435

Commentary
This passage defines the nature of signification (dalala) as a property of the utterance, not of the understanding. The author classifies relational attributes into three categories to show that understanding (fahm) is a property of the hearer, but signification (dalala) is a property of the utterance, analogous to fatherhood (ubuvwa) rather than brotherhood. In brotherhood, both brothers share the relation; in fatherhood, the father alone has the attribute, while the son is merely the object of the relation. Similarly, understanding belongs to the hearer, while the utterance is described as 'that from which the meaning is understood' (مفهوم منه المعنى). The author then explains the grammatical connection: the preposition 'min' in 'fahima al-sami' al-ma'na min al-lafz' indicates that the understanding is connected to the utterance indirectly, via the preposition. Thus, the utterance acquires the property of being a source of understanding, which is exactly what signification is. This refines the definition of dalala: it is not the act of understanding itself, but the attribute of the utterance that makes it conducive to understanding.

Key Terms
دلالة
فهم
نسبة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is signification (dalala) like fatherhood (al-ubuwwa) rather than brotherhood (al-ukhuwwa)?
A) Because both the utterance and the meaning share the attribute equally.
B) Because the attribute subsists in the utterance alone and is connected to the meaning.
C) Because the attribute subsists in the totality of utterance and meaning.
D) Because the utterance and the meaning are identical.

Key Takeaway
Signification is a property of the utterance, not of the hearer, and belongs to the second type of relational attribute where the attribute subsists in one relatum and is connected to the other.

Defining Dalala as Understanding: Refuting Objections
Author refutes three objections regarding the definition of dalala as fahm.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain how the definition of dalala (signification) as fahm (understanding) is defended against three objections using metaphorical interpretation (majaz mursal).

Core Idea
The definition of dalala as 'fahm' is saved by metaphorical transference from hearer to utterance.

In defining dalala (signification), earlier logicians described it as 'fahm' (understanding). This raised three objections: fahm is a property of the hearer, not the utterance; it leads to circularity; and it requires dalala to precede understanding. In this passage, the commentator shows how each objection is answered by recognizing that 'fahm' is used metaphorically (majaz mursal) to refer to the utterance's property of being understood from it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three objections
Read the passage and extract the three objections against defining dalala as fahm. They relate to: (1) fahm as a property of the hearer, (2) circularity if the property of being understood is identical to dalala, (3) temporal priority of dalala over understanding.
2
Extract the answers for each objection
For each objection, find how the commentator resolves it. Note that each answer relies on the idea that 'fahm' is used metaphorically (majaz mursal) to mean the necessary consequence—the utterance's property of being understood.
The key insight: the necessitating term (fahm) is used for the necessary consequence (kawnuhu mafhuman minhu).
3
Understand majaz mursal in this context
Majaz mursal is a metaphorical transfer where the cause stands for the effect, or vice versa. Here, fahm (the act of understanding in the hearer) is used to denote the utterance's property that necessitates understanding. This allows the definition to avoid attributing a hearer's act to the utterance literally.
This solves the first objection (property of hearer vs. utterance) and the third (temporal priority) because the property of being understood is not temporally prior; it is potential until understanding occurs.
4
Verify the resolution of each objection
Check that each objection is neutralized: (1) fahm now refers to a property of the utterance, (2) the circularity is avoided because the property is not explained by a separate cause but is itself dalala, (3) the description of the utterance as 'indicating' before understanding is metaphorical, based on potential, so no temporal priority issue.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَوْلُهُ : (وَأَجَابَ) يَعْنِي: عَنِ الاعْتِرَاضِ السَّابِقِ؛ أَيْ: حَيْثُ تَعَقَّبَ السَّيِّدُ هَذَا الجَوَابَ؛ أَيْ: الَّذِي أَجَابَ بِهِ السَّعْدُ وَغَيْرُهُ فَالْجَوَابُ عَنِ الاعْتِرَاضِ الوَارِدِ مَا ذَكَرَهُ. قَوْلُهُ : (وَمُرَادُهُمْ لَازِمُ ذَلِكَ) يَعْنِي: أَنَّ القَوْمَ أَطْلَقُوا المَلْزُومَ الَّذِي هُوَ الفَهْمُ، وَلَمْ يَقْصِدُوا بِهِ مَعْنَاهُ الصَّرِيحَ، بَلْ مَا يُفْهَمُ مِنْهُ مِمَّا هُوَ صِفَةُ اللَّفْظِ؛ أَعْنِي: كَوْنَهُ مَفْهُوماً مِنْهُ المَعْنَى، وَلَمَّا كَانَ هَذَا مِنْ قَبِيلِ المَجَازِ أَشَارَ إِلَى قَرِينَتِهِ بِقَوْلِهِ: «وَاتَّكَلُوا». قَوْلُهُ : (وَأَنَّ الفَهْمَ لَيْسَ صِفَةٌ لَهُ) أَيْ: فَلَا بُدَّ إِذَنْ أَنْ يَقْصِدُوا بِالفَهْمِ الَّذِي ذَكَرُوهُ فِي تَعْرِيفِهِمَا مَعْنًى هُوَ صِفَةٌ لَهُ، وَلَيْسَ ذَلِكَ إِلَّا كَوْنَهُ مَفْهُوماً مِنْهُ المَعْنَى. قَوْلُهُ : (وَأُجِيبَ عَنِ الثَّانِي) حَاصِلُ الجَوَابِ: أَنَّ الصِّفَةَ المَفْهُومَةَ مِنْ تَعَلُّقِ الفَهْمِ بِاللَّفْظِ وَهُوَ: كَوْنُ اللَّفْظِ ... إِلَخْ» عَيْنُ الدَّلَالَةِ، فَلَا يَصِحُّ تَعْلِيلُهَا بِالدَّلَالَةِ، فَلَا تَقُولُ: «كَوْنُ اللَّفْظِ مَفْهُوماً مِنْهُ المَعْنَى لِلدَّلَالَةِ»؛ لِأَنَّ الكَوْنَ هُوَ عَيْنُ الدَّلَالَةِ، وَحِينَئِذٍ فَمَعْنَى قَوْلِكَ: فَهِمْتُ كَذَا مِنَ اللَّفْظِ؛ لِأَنَّهُ دَلَّنِي عَلَيْهِ: أَنَّكَ اتَّصَفْتَ بِالفَاهِمِيَّةِ مِنَ اللَّفْظِ؛ لِكَوْنِ اللَّفْظِ مُنْشَأً لِفَهْمِهِ، وَلَا مِرْيَةَ أَنَّ هَذَا السُّؤَالَ لَا يَرِدُ عَلَى مَا مَرَّ عَنِ السَّيِّدِ، فَلَا يَحْتَاجُ إِلَى الجَوَابِ. فَإِنْ قِيلَ: يَرِدُ عَلَى قَوْلِهِمْ: «فَهِمَ السَّامِعُ المَعْنَى مِنَ اللَّفْظِ لِدَلَالَتِهِ عَلَيْهِ»: أَنَّ الدَّلَالَةَ سَابِقَةٌ عَلَى الفَهْمِ؛ لِأَنَّ العِلَّةَ سَابِقَةٌ عَلَى المَعْلُولِ. أُجِيبَ: بِأَنَّ المَعْنَى: أَنَّ السَّامِعَ اتَّصَفَ بِالفَاهِمِيَّةِ مِنَ اللَّفْظِ لِكَوْنِ اللَّفْظِ صَالِحاً لِأَنْ يَدُلَّ عَلَى فَهْمِهِ؛ إِذْ لَمْ تُوجَدِ الدَّلَالَةُ بِالفِعْلِ؛ لِأَنَّهَا لُغَةً: الإِرْشَادُ، وَمَا لَمْ يَحْصُلْ فَهْمٌ بِالفِعْلِ لَمْ يَتَحَقَّقْ إِرْشَادٌ، فَلَمْ تَتَقَدَّمِ الدَّلَالَةُ حِينَئِذٍ. قَوْلُهُ : (بَلْ مَجَازاً حَاصِلُهُ: أَنَّ اعْتِرَاضَهُمْ مَبْنِيٌّ عَلَى أَنَّ وَصْفَ الدَّالِّ بِالدَّلَالَةِ قَبْلَ الفَهْمِ حَقِيقَةً، فَيُنَافِي تَفْسِيرَهَا بِالعِلْمِ، وَلَيْسَ الأَمْرُ كَذَلِكَ، بَلْ مَجَازاً مُرْسَلاً، فَبَطَلَتْ حِينَئِذٍ المُنَافَاةُ وَصَحَّ تَفْسِيرُ الدَّلَالَةِ بِالفَهْمِ.
His statement: 'And he answered' means: concerning the preceding objection; that is, where al-Sayyid followed up this answer, i.e., the answer that al-Sa'd and others gave. So the answer to the objection that occurred is what he mentioned. His statement: 'And they intended the necessary consequence of that' means that the people (the scholars) used the necessitating term which is 'understanding', and they did not intend its literal meaning, but rather what is understood from it that is a description of the utterance, i.e., its being that from which the meaning is understood. Since this is a type of metaphor, he indicated its contextual clue by his statement: 'and they relied'. His statement: 'And that understanding is not a description for it' i.e., so necessarily, then, they intended by 'understanding' which they mentioned in their definition a meaning that is a description for it (the utterance), and that is nothing other than its being that from which the meaning is understood. His statement: 'And the second was answered' the gist of the answer is that the description understood from the connection of understanding with the utterance, which is: 'the utterance being... etc.' is identically signification, so it is not correct to make it dependent on signification. So you do not say: 'The utterance being understood from it the meaning is because of signification'; because the being is identical to signification. Then the meaning of your saying: 'I understood such-and-such from the utterance because it indicated it to me' is that you were described with the state of understanding from the utterance because the utterance was the source of understanding it. There is no doubt that this question does not apply to what was mentioned earlier from al-Sayyid, so it does not need an answer. If it is said: There applies to their statement: 'The hearer understood the meaning from the utterance because of its indication of it' that signification precedes understanding because the cause precedes the effect. It is answered: That the meaning is that the hearer was described with the state of understanding from the utterance because the utterance is suitable to indicate his understanding, since signification does not exist in actuality; because it is, in language, guidance. And unless understanding actually occurs, guidance is not realized, so signification does not precede in that case. His statement: 'But metaphorically' its gist is that their objection is based on the fact that describing the indicator with signification before understanding is real, so it contradicts interpreting it as knowledge; but it is not so, rather it is a metaphorical usage (majaz mursal), so the contradiction is nullified and interpreting signification as understanding is correct.
Source pages p. 435

Commentary
This passage presents the answers to three objections against defining dalala as 'fahm' (understanding). The first objection is that 'fahm' is a property of the hearer, not of the utterance. The answer is that when earlier scholars used 'fahm' in the definition, they did not intend its literal meaning (the act of understanding) but rather its necessary consequence—namely, that the utterance is such that understanding is derived from it. This is a metaphorical usage (majaz mursal) where the necessitating term is used for the necessary consequence. The second objection is that the effect of dalala is the understanding as a property of the hearer, but what we call dalala is the property of the utterance; if we say 'the utterance is such that understanding is derived from it because of its dalala', we are explaining the same thing by itself. The answer is that the property of being understood from (kawnuhu mafhuman minhu) is exactly what dalala is; it is not a separate attribute that can be a cause. So the statement 'I understood because it indicated' means that the hearer attained understanding because the utterance was a source of that understanding, not that there is a separate cause called dalala. The third objection is that if dalala is the cause of understanding, it must precede the understanding, yet the definition includes understanding. The answer is that the description of the utterance as 'indicator' before actual understanding is metaphorical (majaz mursal), based on the potentiality of the utterance. In reality, dalala (as actual guidance) does not occur until understanding happens. Thus, the apparent contradiction is resolved, and the definition of dalala as 'fahm' (understood metaphorically) stands correct.

فهم
مجاز مرسل

Checkpoint
How is the second objection (circularity) against defining dalala as fahm answered?
A) By denying that the property of being understood is identical to dalala.
B) By stating that the property of being understood is the effect of dalala, not the cause.
C) By explaining that the statement 'I understood because it indicated' means the utterance is the source of understanding, not that a separate cause called dalala exists.
D) By redefining understanding as a separate entity from dalala.

Key Takeaway
The definition of dalala as 'fahm' is retained by interpreting 'fahm' metaphorically as the utterance's property of being understood from it, resolving objections about the subject of predication, circularity, and temporal priority.

Defending the Definition of Dalalah as Fahm
Author presents and refutes objections to defining dalalah as fahm.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to defend the definition of dalalah as fahm against the three objections raised, using the concept of majaz mursal and the distinction between attribute of the word and attribute of the understanding subject.

Core Idea
Dalalah as fahm is not circular because 'fahm' refers to the word's property, not the act of understanding.

The definition of dalalah (indication) as fahm (understanding) was the position of earlier scholars, but it faced objections about circularity and temporal priority. In this passage, the commentator systematically answers each objection, clarifying that the term 'fahm' is used metaphorically to denote the word's attribute of being understood, not the actually occurring understanding. This lesson walks you through the objections and their resolutions, equipping you with the tools to navigate similar definitional debates in Islamic logic.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three objections
Read the passage and the translation. Look for the three objections: (1) that applying 'fahm' to dalal is metaphorical and not literal, (2) that defining dalalah by fahm leads to circularity, and (3) that dalalah as cause must precede understanding as effect, but the definition conflates them.
2
Understand the metaphorical transfer
The commentator explains that the earlier scholars used 'fahm' metaphorically (majaz mursal) by applying the term for the necessary condition (malzum) to the necessary consequence (lazim). The 'fahm' they intend is not the act of understanding but the property of the word that it is understood from it the meaning. The contextual indicator (qarina) is intellectual, showing it is not literal.
This resolves the first objection: the definition is not literal but metaphorical, which is acceptable.
3
Analyze the second answer: avoiding circularity
The second objection claimed that if dalalah equals fahm, then saying 'the word is understood because of its indication' is circular. The answer distinguishes: the effect of dalalah is understanding as an attribute of the understander, while the meaning of dalalah is understanding as an attribute of the word. These are different, so no circularity. The word's being understood is exactly the indication, not caused by it.
This shows precise conceptual differentiation.
4
Resolve temporal priority in the third answer
The third objection asserted that dalalah must precede fahm as cause precedes effect. The answer: the word's suitability (salihiyya) to indicate, not actual indication, is what causes understanding. Actual indication requires actual understanding, so priority is not temporal but conceptual. The description of the word as 'indicating' before understanding is metaphorical (naming by what it will become).
This preserves the causal relation without temporal paradox.
5
Reflect on the role of majaz in logical definitions
Note that the commentator uses majaz mursal (allegorical metaphor) to defend the definition. This illustrates that definitions in logic can employ metaphorical language, as long as the intended meaning is clear. The intellectual qarina prevents confusion.
This is a methodological point: definitions are not always literal.

وَأَنَّ الفَهْمَ لَيْسَ صِفَةٌ لَهُ، فَإِطْلَاقُ الفَهْم عَلَى الكَوْنِ المَذْكُورِ مَجَازٌ مُرْسَلٌ ، مِنْ إِطْلَاقِ المَلْزُوم عَلَى اللَّازِم ، وَالقَرِينَةُ عَقْلِيَّةٌ كَمَا ذَكَرَهُ، وَهُوَ ظَاهِرٌ. وَأُجِيبَ عَنِ الثَّانِي : بِأَنَّ المَعْلُولَ بِالدَّلَالَةِ إِنَّمَا هُوَ الفَهْمُ بِاعْتِبارِ كَوْنِهِ صِفَةٌ لِلْفَاهِم، وَلَيْسَ هُوَ مَعْنَى الدَّلَالَةِ، وَإِنَّمَا مَعْنَاهَا كَمَا سَلَفَ : الفَهْمُ بِاعْتِبارِ كَوْنِهِ صِفَةٌ لِلْمَفْهُومِ مِنْهُ، وَهُوَ لَا يَصِحُ تَعْلِيلُهُ بِالدَّلَالَةِ. وَأُجِيبَ عَنِ الثَّالِثِ : بِأَنَّ الدَّالَ لا يُوصَفُ بِالدَّلَالَةِ قَبْلَ الفَهْمِ حَقِيقَةٌ، بَلْ مَجَازاً مُرْسَلاً مِنْ تَسْمِيَةِ الشَّيْء بِاسْمِ مَا يَؤولُ هُوَ إِلَيْهِ. قصارة - معناه الصّريح، بل ما يفهم منه مما هو صفة اللفظ ؛ أعني : كونه مفهوماً منه المعنى، ولما كان هذا من قبيل المجاز أشار إلى قرينته بقوله : «وَاتَّكَلُوا». قوله : (وَأَنَّ الفَهْمَ لَيْسَ صِفَةٌ لَهُ) أي: فلا بدَّ إذن أن يقصدوا بالفهم الذي ذكروه في تعريفهما معنى هو صفةٌ له، وليس ذلك إلَّا كونه مفهوماً منه المعنى . قوله : ( وَأُجِيبَ عَن الثَّانِي) حاصل الجواب: أنَّ الصفة المفهومة من تعلق الفهم باللفظ وهو : كون اللفظ ... إلخ» عين الدَّلالة، فلا يصح تعليلها بالدَّلالة، فلا تقول: «كون اللفظ مفهوماً المعنى للدَّلالة» ؛ لأنَّ الكون هو عين الدَّلالة، وحينئذ فمعنى قولك : فهمت كذا مِن اللَّفظ ؛ لأنَّه دلني عليه : أنَّك اتَّصفت بالفاهميَّة مِنَ اللَّفظ ؛ لكون اللفظ منشأ لفهمه، ولا مرية أنَّ هذا السُّؤال لا يرد على ما مرَّ عنِ السَّيِّد، فلا يحتاج إلى الجواب. فإن قيل: يرد على قولهم: «فهم السَّامع المعنى مِنَ اللَّفظ لدلالته عليه»: أنَّ الدَّلالة سابقة على الفهم؛ لأنَّ العلة سابقة على المعلول. أجيب : بأنَّ المعنى: أنَّ السَّامع اتّصف بالفاهميَّة مِنَ اللفظ لكون اللفظ صالحاً لأنْ يدل على فهمه ؛ إذ لم توجد الدلالة بالفعل ؛ لأنَّها لغةٌ : الإرشاد، وما لم يحصل فهم بالفعل لم يتحقق إرشاد، فلم تتقدم الدلالة حينئذ . قوله : (بَلْ مَجَازاً حاصلُهُ : أنَّ اعتراضهم مبني على أنَّ وصف الدَّالّ بالدَّلالة قبل الفهم حقيقة، فينافي تفسيرها بالعلم، وليس الأمر كذلك، بل مجازاً مرسلاً، فبطلت حينئذ المنافاة وصح تفسير الدلالة بالفهم.
And that understanding [fahm] is not an attribute of it [the dalal], so the application of 'understanding' to the aforementioned state is a metaphorical transfer (majaz mursal), from applying the necessary condition (malzum) to the necessary consequence (lazim), and the contextual indicator (qarina) is intellectual, as he mentioned, and it is evident. And the second objection is answered: that the effect of indication is only understanding in terms of it being an attribute of the one who understands, and it is not the meaning of indication; rather its meaning, as previously mentioned, is understanding in terms of it being an attribute of what is understood from it, and it is not valid to explain that by indication. And the third objection is answered: that the indicator (dal) is not described with indication before understanding truly, but rather metaphorically (majaz mursal) by naming a thing with the name of what it will eventually become. Qasara: Its explicit meaning, rather what is understood from it that is an attribute of the word, i.e., being understood from it the meaning. And since this is of the category of metaphor, he indicated its contextual indicator by his saying: 'and they relied'. His saying: 'And that understanding is not an attribute of it' means: Then necessarily what they mean by 'understanding' in their definition is a meaning that is an attribute of it, and that is nothing but being understood from it the meaning. His saying: 'And the second is answered'—the gist of the answer: that the attribute understood from the attachment of understanding to the word, i.e., the word being ... etc., is exactly indication, so it is not valid to explain it by indication. So you do not say: 'The word being understood from it the meaning is because of indication' because that being is exactly indication. Then the meaning of your saying: 'I understood such-and-such from the word because it indicated it to me' is that you are described with understanding from the word by virtue of the word being the source of his understanding. And there is no doubt that this objection does not apply to what has passed from al-Sayyid, so it does not need an answer. If it is said: It applies to their saying: 'The hearer understands the meaning from the word because of its indication of it' that indication precedes understanding, because the cause precedes the effect. It is answered: The meaning is that the hearer is described with understanding from the word by virtue of the word being suitable to indicate his understanding, since indication does not actually exist, because it is linguistically guidance, and as long as no actual understanding occurs, no guidance is realized, so indication does not precede then. His saying: 'Rather metaphorically'—its gist: that their objection is based on describing the indicator with indication before understanding truly, which contradicts its interpretation as knowledge, but it is not so; rather it is metaphorically (majaz mursal), so the contradiction is invalidated and the interpretation of indication as understanding is valid.

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) responding to objections against the definition of dalalah (indication) as fahm (understanding). The author first clarifies that when the earlier scholars defined dalalah as fahm, they did not mean understanding as an attribute of the person who understands (the fahim), but rather understanding as an attribute of the word itself—specifically, that the word is understood from it the meaning. This is a metaphorical usage (majaz mursal) of the term fahm, applying the necessary condition (malzum) to the necessary consequence (lazim). The intellectual contextual indicator (qarina 'aqliyya) shows this is not literal. Then the second objection is answered: the effect of dalalah is understanding in the sense of the attribute of the fahim, but that is not the meaning of dalalah; the meaning is understanding as an attribute of the word. Therefore, one cannot explain that attribute by dalalah itself, as it would be circular. The third objection is about describing the dal (indicator) with dalalah before understanding occurs. The response is that this description is not true (haqiqa) but metaphorical (majaz mursal), naming a thing for what it will become. The commentator (Qasara) adds an explanation: the literal meaning of dalalah is not fahm itself but the property of being understood from it. The objection that dalalah must precede understanding because it is the cause is refuted: the relationship is not temporal; the word's suitability for indication (salihiyya) is what causes understanding, not an actual indication before understanding. Thus, the earlier definition is defended, and the apparent contradiction is resolved.

Key Takeaway
The definition of dalalah as fahm is defended by distinguishing between fahm as the act of the understander and fahm as the word's property of being understood, and by using majaz mursal to explain temporal expressions.

Reconciling the Two Definitions of Dalalah: Haythiyyah vs. Fahm
Author explains the later view that dalalah is haythiyyah and reconciles it with the earlier definition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain how the later definition of dalalah as haythiyyah is consistent with the earlier definition as fahm, and identify the root of the apparent disagreement.

Core Idea
The later definition of dalalah as haythiyyah does not contradict the earlier; both describe the same reality — the word's suitability to convey meaning.

In this lesson, we explore a classic point of debate in Islamic logic: the definition of dalalah (indication). The earlier scholars defined it as fahm (understanding), while the later scholars defined it as haythiyyah (a property of leading to understanding). At first glance, these seem different, but the author argues they are equivalent. We will see how the apparent disagreement arises from a misunderstanding and how it is resolved.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two definitions
Locate in the Arabic passage the definitions given by the earlier scholars (al-mutaqaddimun) and the later scholars (al-muta'akhkhirun). The earlier defined dalalah as fahm, the later as haythiyyah.
2
Analyze the later definition
Understand that haythiyyah means the word being a locus (mahall) for the attachment of understanding, not mere potentiality. The later scholars did not mean simple suitability but actual attachment of understanding to the word.
The commentator emphasizes that the later scholars' definition is not just 'potential understanding' but the word as the place where understanding occurs.
3
Reconcile the views
Notice how the earlier scholars' 'fahm' refers to the attribute of the word that leads to understanding, which is exactly what the later scholars mean by haythiyyah. The apparent disagreement is due to focusing on wording rather than meaning.
The author cites al-Ghazali's principle: one should seek meanings, not just words.

أنواع الدلالة الوضعية. وَذَهَبَ المُتَأخّرُونَ إِلَى أَنَّ الدَّلَالَةَ هِيَ الحَيثِيَّةُ ; أَي : كَوْنُ أَمْرِ بِحَيْثُ يَصِحُ أَنْ يُفْهَمَ مِنْهُ أَمْرُ ; سَوَاءٌ فُهِمَ أَوْ لَمْ يُفْهَمْ، وَبِعِبَارَةٍ أُخْرَى : كَوْنُ أَمْرٍ بِحَيْثُ يَلْزَمُ مِنَ العِلْمِ بِهِ العِلْمُ بِأَمْرِ آخَرَ، وَعَلَيْهِ : يَكُونُ وَصْفُ الدَّالَ بِالدَّلَالَةِ قَبْلَ الفَهْم حَقِيقَةٌ . فَإِنْ قُلْتَ : يَلْزَمُ عَلَى مَذْهَبِ الأَقْدَمِينَ حُدُوتُ دَلَالَةِ كَلَامِ اللَّهِ تَعَالَى القَدِيمِ؛ لِعَدَمِ الفَاهِمِ فِي الأَزَلِ، وَيَلْزَمُ مِنْ حُدُوثِهَا حُدُوثُ مَوْصُوفِهَا. قصارة. قوله : (سَوَاءٌ فُهِمَ أَوْ لَمْ يُفْهَمْ هذه الزِّيادة وقعت للشَّيخ السَّنوسي، وتبعه عليها جمع، وليست في كلام المتأخرين، فهذه زيادة من عنده ; بناءً على فهمه - كجماعة الخلاف بين الفريقين. والحقُ : أنَّه لا خلاف بينهما، فالمتأخّرون قائلون بأنَّ الدَّالَ لا يُوصَفُ بالدَّلالة حقيقةٌ إلَّا بعد الفهم، ولم يريدوا بالحيثيَّة مجرَّد المصاحبة للفهم، وإنَّما أرادوا : أَنَّ الدَّلالة هي كون اللفظ محله لتعلق الفهم به . وحاصلُهُ : أَنَّ الأقدمين وإن عرَّفوا الدَّلالة بالفهم، فمرادهم : ما يُفهم منه مما هو صفةٌ للفظ؛ أعني : كونه بحيث يفهم منه المعنى، كما تقدَّم عنِ السَّيِّد، والمتأخّرون لم يقصدوا بقولهم : كون أمر بحيث يصح أن يفهم ... إلخ » مجرَّد الصَّلاحِيَّة للفهم، بل قصدوا كون اللفظ محلا لتعلُّق الفهم به، وهذا هو معنى كلام المتقدمين، فرجع الخلاف إلى وفاق ولم يبق بين الفريقين شقاق. وتوهم جماعة الخلاف مبني على تحكيم الألفاظ، مع الغفلة عن المراد، وتقدم قول الغزالي : من طلب المعاني ... إلخ». قوله : (وَبِعِبَارَةِ أُخْرَى) أشار بهذا الرَّفع توهم مباينة هذا التّعريف لِمَا قبله . قوله : (وَعَلَيْهِ : يَكُونُ أي : على ما ذهب إليه المتأخّرون، وهو مبني على فهمه مخالفة هذا التّعريف لتعريف الأقدمين، وقد علمت ما فيه. قوله : (فَإِنْ قُلْتَ: يَلْزَمُ تبع في هذا السُّؤال الهلالي، وهو معترض من وجوه: الأول : أنَّه كان من حقه أن لو أتى به من جملة الاعتراضات ويجيب عنه، لكن الهلالي أتى به سؤالاً فتبعه .
Types of conventional indication. And the later scholars (muta'akhkhirun) held that indication (dalalah) is haythiyyah, i.e., a thing being such that it is valid for another thing to be understood from it, whether understood or not understood. In another expression: a thing being such that knowledge of it necessitates knowledge of another thing. And accordingly, describing the indicator (dal) with indication before understanding is true (haqiqa). If you say: It follows from the doctrine of the earlier scholars (mutaqaddimun) that the indication of the eternal speech of Allah (ta'ala) occurs in time (hadith) because there is no understander in eternity, and from its temporal origination follows the temporal origination of its described entity. Qasara: His saying: 'whether understood or not understood'—this addition was made by Shaykh al-Sanusi, and a group followed him, and it is not found in the speech of the later scholars. So this is an addition from him based on his understanding—like a group—of a disagreement between the two parties. But the truth is that there is no disagreement between them. For the later scholars say that the indicator is not described with indication truly except after understanding, and they did not mean by haythiyyah mere accompaniment of understanding, but rather they meant that indication is the word being a locus for the attachment of understanding to it. The gist is that the earlier scholars, although they defined indication as understanding, their intended meaning is what is understood from it that is an attribute of the word, i.e., its being such that the meaning is understood from it, as has passed from al-Sayyid. And the later scholars did not intend by their saying 'a thing being such that it is valid to understand...' mere potential for understanding, but rather they intended the word being a locus for the attachment of understanding to it. And this is the meaning of the speech of the earlier scholars. So the disagreement returns to agreement, and no schism remains between the two groups. The illusion of disagreement among a group is based on prioritizing wording, with heedlessness of the intended meaning. And the saying of al-Ghazali has preceded: 'Whoever seeks meanings...' etc. His saying: 'In another expression'—he indicated by this the removal of the illusion that this definition is different from what preceded. His saying: 'And accordingly, it is' i.e., based on what the later scholars held, and it is based on his understanding that this definition contradicts the definition of the earlier scholars, and you have already learned what is in it. His saying: 'If you say: it follows'—he followed al-Hilali in this question, and he is an objector in several ways: first, that it would have been proper for him to bring it as part of the objections and answer it, but al-Hilali brought it as a question so he followed him.
Source pages p. 437

Commentary
This passage presents the later scholars' definition of dalalah (indication) as haythiyyah—a property of an entity such that it can validly lead to understanding another thing, regardless of whether understanding actually occurs. This definition is contrasted with the earlier scholars' definition as fahm (understanding). The author explains that the apparent conflict is resolved by noting that the later scholars' haythiyyah is not mere potentiality but the word being a 'locus' (mahall) for understanding, which is equivalent to the earlier view that understanding is an attribute of the word (i.e., its being understood-from-it the meaning). The commentator (Qasara) criticizes an addition by al-Sanusi ('whether understood or not understood') as misrepresenting the later view. The truth is that both schools agree that description with indication as true (haqiqa) occurs only after understanding; the difference is terminological. The passage also mentions an objection by al-Hilali regarding the eternal speech of Allah: if dalalah is dependent on understanding, then Allah's speech would have had no indication in eternity, implying its temporal origination, which is problematic. However, the commentator notes that this objection is misplaced because the later view does not require actual understanding for the word to be described as indicative in a true sense—it is based on its suitability, which is eternal. The objection is thus answered implicitly. The author stresses that the disagreement is illusory, arising from a focus on wording rather than intended meaning, citing al-Ghazali's principle that meanings matter more than expressions.

Key Terms
الحَيْثِيَّة
الأَقْدَمُونَ
المُتَأَخْرُونَ
المَحَلّ

Checkpoint
What does the author identify as the root of the illusion of disagreement between the earlier and later definitions of dalalah?
A) A genuine difference in the understanding of the nature of indication.
B) The later scholars' rejection of the earlier definition entirely.
C) A focus on wording over intended meaning, and heedlessness of the actual intent.
D) The addition of the phrase 'whether understood or not understood' by al-Sanusi.

Key Takeaway
The apparent disagreement between the earlier and later definitions of dalalah is resolved once we realize they are describing the same reality from different perspectives: the earlier focusing on the effect (understanding), the later on the property (suitability as a locus).

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
1. Identify the definition of dalalah as used by a later scholar like al-Taftazani in his commentary on al-Tahdhib, and show how it aligns with the earlier definition.
?
2. Using a concrete example from the Quran, explain how the ayah 'Establish prayer' (أَقِيمُوا الصَّلَاةَ) has dalalah (indication) according to both the earlier and later definitions, demonstrating their equivalence.

The Nature of Indication and Its Primary Division
Author clarifies nature of dalaala and divides into verbal/non-verbal.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish dalaala as a mere relation from a real attribute and classify any indication as verbal or non-verbal.

Core Idea
Indication is not a real attribute but an accidental relation.

Before the author classifies indication into types, he clarifies a crucial point: dalaala is not a real attribute of its subject. This distinction prevents a logical fallacy. Then he divides indication into verbal and non-verbal based on the nature of the indicator.

Guided Path
1
Understand the distinction between real attribute and mere relation
The author argues that a real attribute's occurrence necessitates the occurrence of its subject. Dalaala is only a relation accidental to the indicator, so its occurrence does not necessitate the temporal origination of the indicator itself, like the temporal connection of God's power is not an attribute of power.
This avoids the fallacy that dalaala would make the indicator created.
2
Identify the criterion for verbal vs non-verbal indication
If the indicator (dāl) is a word (lafẓ), the indication is verbal (lafẓiyya); otherwise it is non-verbal (ghayr lafẓiyya). This is the primary division.
Examples: 'lion' is verbal; smoke indicating fire is non-verbal.
3
Apply the division to real-world examples from Islamic sciences
In Usul al-Fiqh, the word 'command' (amr) is a verbal indication for obligation. The sight of a minaret indicates the direction of prayer non-verbally.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قلت : أجيب بأن الصفة التي يلزم من حدوثها حدوث موصوفها هي الصفة الحقيقية، والدلالة إنما هي مجرد نسبة عارضة للدال، فلا يلزم من حدوثها حدوثه، كما أن التعلق التنجيزي للقدرة حادث، وهي قديمة بلا مرية. ثم الدال إن كان لفظا فالدلالة لفظية، وإلا فغير لفظية، وكل منهما ينقسم إلى ثلاثة أقسام: وضعية، وعقلية، وطبيعية؛ لأن الدلالة إن كانت اختيارية فهي الوضعية، وإلا فإن أمكن تخلفها فهي الطبيعية، وإلا فهي العقلية، فصارت الدلالة ستة أقسام: فدلالة اللفظ الوضعية كدلالة لفظ "الأسد" على السبع المعروف حقيقة، أو على الرجل الشجاع مجازا؛
I said: It is answered that the attribute from whose occurrence the occurrence of its subject necessarily follows is the real attribute, but indication is only a mere relation accidental to the indicator, so its occurrence does not necessitate his occurrence, just as the immediate connection of power is temporal and it is eternal without doubt. Then if the indicator is a word, the indication is verbal, otherwise it is non-verbal, and each of them divides into three divisions: conventional, rational, and natural; because if the indication is voluntary, it is conventional, otherwise if it is possible for it to lag, it is natural, otherwise it is rational; so indication becomes six divisions: the verbal conventional indication is like the indication of the word 'lion' to the known beast in reality, or to the courageous man metaphorically.
Source pages p. 438

Commentary
This passage defines and classifies dalaala (indication). It begins by clarifying a previous point: the attribute whose occurrence necessitates the occurrence of its subject is a real attribute. Dalaala, however, is merely a relation that is accidental to the indicator (the thing that indicates). Therefore, the occurrence of this relation does not imply the temporal origination of the indicator itself, just as the immediate connection (ta'alluq tanzīzī) of God's power is temporal while the power itself is eternal. Then the author proceeds to the classification: dalaala is divided based on whether the indicator (dāl) is a word (lafẓ) or not. If it is a word, the indication is verbal (lafẓiyya); otherwise it is non-verbal (ghayr lafẓiyya). Each of these two types is further divided into three: conventional (waḍ'iyya), rational ('aqliyya), and natural (ṭabī'iyya). The criterion for this division is: if the indication is voluntary (ikhtiyāriyya) – that is, based on a deliberate choice – it is conventional. If it is not voluntary, then if it is possible for the indication to lag behind its cause (i.e., the indicator exists but the indication may not occur), it is natural, otherwise it is rational. Thus there are six types of indication in total. An example given is the conventional verbal indication of the word 'lion' referring either to the well-known beast in its literal sense (ḥaqīqa) or to a courageous man in a metaphorical sense (majāz). This classification is foundational for understanding how meanings are conveyed in Islamic logic and jurisprudence.

Key Terms
الدلالة
الصفة الحقيقية
النسبة العارضة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what distinguishes dalaala from a real attribute?
A) A real attribute necessitates the existence of its subject, while dalaala does not.
B) Dalaala is eternal, while real attributes are temporal.
C) Real attributes are always verbal, while dalaala is non-verbal.
D) Dalaala is a relation that causes the indicator to exist.

Key Takeaway
Dalaala is not a real attribute but an accidental relation; it is divided into verbal and non-verbal based on the indicator.

The Three Types of Indication: Conventional, Rational, and Natural
Author subdivides each primary type into three based on voluntariness and lag.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify any indication as conventional, rational, or natural using the criteria of voluntariness and possibility of lag.

Core Idea
Indication is classified by whether it is voluntary and whether it can lag.

The author further subdivides both verbal and non-verbal indication into three types based on two criteria: whether the indication is voluntary (ikhtiyāriyya) and, if not voluntary, whether it can possibly lag behind its cause (i.e., the indicator exists but the indication does not occur). This yields conventional, rational, and natural indication.

Guided Path
1
Learn the first criterion: voluntary vs involuntary
If the indication is based on deliberate choice (ikhtiyār), it is conventional (waḍ'iyya). This includes linguistic conventions where a speaker intentionally assigns a meaning to a word.
Voluntary means the connection is established by conscious agreement.
2
Apply the second criterion: possibility of lag
For involuntary indications, check if it is possible for the indication to be absent while the cause is present. If it can lag (e.g., redness may not always accompany shame), it is natural (ṭabī'iyya). If it cannot lag (e.g., smoke always indicates fire), it is rational ('aqliyya).
Lag means the indication fails to occur even though the indicator is present.
3
Classify the example given in the passage
The word 'lion' used literally indicates the beast by linguistic convention (voluntary). So it is conventional verbal indication. When used metaphorically for a brave man, it is also conventional (based on a secondary convention).
The example shows that conventional indication can be either literal or metaphorical.
4
Apply to new examples from Islamic sciences
In Kalam, the occurrence of a miracle at the hands of a prophet is a rational indication of prophethood because it cannot lag (the miracle necessarily indicates truthfulness). In medicine, fever indicates illness naturally (it can lag or be absent).

Source Text

The Five Types of Indication (al-Dalalah)
Author classifies indication into five types with examples

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify each of the five types of indication (dalalah) and give an Islamic example for each.

Core Idea
Indication is not only conventional; it is also rational and natural, and applies to both words and non-words.

In Islamic logic, understanding how signs convey meaning is fundamental. The author classifies indication into five types based on the nature of the indicator (word or non-word) and the basis of the relation (convention, reason, or nature). This lesson unpacks each type with examples from Quranic language, natural human reactions, and rational inference to the Creator.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish linguistic vs. non-linguistic indicators
Notice the division: indication can be by a word (lafz) or by a non-word (ghayr lafz). This is the first branching point in the classification.
2
For each category, identify the basis of indication
For both linguistic and non-linguistic, there are three bases: wad'iyya (conventional assignment), 'aqliyya (rational inference), and tabi'iyya (natural instinct). Write them in a 2x3 grid.
Natural indication only occurs for linguistic indicators in this passage; non-linguistic natural indication is not mentioned.
3
Match the examples from the passage
For conventional linguistic: Quranic words indicating individual and compound meanings. For rational linguistic: a word indicating its speaker (since a word is an accident requiring a substance). For natural linguistic: 'Ah' indicating pain. For conventional non-linguistic: writing indicating speech, gesture indicating 'yes'/'no'. For rational non-linguistic: change indicating origination, origination indicating the Creator.
4
Verify completeness
Ask: are there any types of indication not covered? The author implies these five are exhaustive. Consider: custom (urf) might be a type? But here custom can be subsumed under conventional (wad'iyya).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بِنَاءً عَلَى أَنَّ المَجَازَ مَوْضُوعٌ بِالنَّوْع، وَمِنْ ذَلِكَ : دَلَالَهُ أَلْفَاظِ القُرْآنِ عَلَى مَعَانِيهِ الإِفْرَادِيَّةِ، وَكَذَا التَّرْكِيبِيَّةِ؛ لأَنَّ التَّحْقِيقَ أَنَّ دَلَالَةَ المُرَكَّب وَضْعِيَّةٌ، لَا عَقْلِيَّةٌ.
(٢) - وَدَلَالَةُ اللَّفْظِ العَقْلِيَّةُ كَدَلَالَةِ اللَّفْظِ عَلَى لَافِظٍ يَقُومُ هُوَ بِهِ، وَهِيَ الأَلْفَاظِ؛ لِأَنَّ اللَّفْظَ عَرَضْ يَسْتَحِيلُ أَنْ يَقُومَ بِنَفْسِهِ.
(۳) - وَدَلَالَةُ اللَّفْظِ الطَّبِيعِيَّةُ كَدَلَالَةِ «أَحْ» عَلَى الوَجَعِ، وَالصُّرَاخِ الضَّرُورِيِّ عَلَى مُصِيبَةٍ نَزَلَتْ بِالصَّارِخِ.
(٤) - وَدَلَالَةُ غَيْرِ اللَّفْظِ الوَضْعِيَّةُ كَدَلَالَةِ الكِتَابَةِ عَلَى الأَلْفَاظِ، وَدَلَالَةِ الإِشَارَةِ عَلَى مَعْنَى «نَعَمْ» أَوْ «لَا».
(٥) - وَدَلَالَةُ غَيْرِ اللَّفْظِ العَقْلِيَّةُ كَدَلَالَةِ التَّغَيُّرِ عَلَى الحُدُوثِ، وَدَلَالَةِ الحُدُوثِ عَلَى وُجُودِ الخَالِقِ، وَمِنْ هَذَا القِسْمِ: دَلَالَةُ كَلَامِ اللهِ تَعَالَى القَدِيمِ ـ أَعْنِي : المَعْنَى القَائِمَ بِالذَّاتِ العَلِيَّةِ - عَلَى مُتَعَلَّقَاتِهِ : أَمَّا أَنَّهَا غَيْرُ لَفْظِيَّةٍ فَظَاهِرٌ؛ لِأَنَّ كَلَامَهُ تَعَالَى بِالمَعْنَى المَذْكُورِ لَيْسَ بِحَرْفٍ وَلَا صَوْتٍ. وَأَمَّا أَنَّهَا عَقْلِيَّةٌ : فَلِأَنَّ تَعَلَّقَ الكَلَام - وَهُوَ دَلَالَتُهُ - نَفْسِيٌّ لَهُ كَتَعَلُّقِ غَيْرِهِ مِنَ الصِّفَاتِ، وَالنَّفْسِيُّ لَا يَتَغَيَّرُ وَلَا يَتَخَلَّفُ، وَالوَضْعِيَّةُ وَالطَّبْعِيَّةُ يَصِحُ تَغَيُّرُهُمَا كَمَا تَقَدَّمَ، وَأَيْضاً : تَعَلُّقُ الكَلَامِ قَدِيمٌ كَالكَلَامِ، وَالوَضْعِيَّةُ وَالطَّبْعِيَّةُ حَادِثَتَانِ
Based on the view that metaphor is conventionally assigned by type. Among that is the indication of the words of the Quran upon its individual meanings, and likewise compound meanings; because verification is that the indication of a compound is conventional, not rational. (2) The rational indication of a word, like the indication of a word upon a speaker who performs it; and that is for words, because the word is an accident, impossible to subsist by itself. (3) The natural indication of a word, like the indication of 'Ah' upon pain, and the involuntary scream upon a calamity that has befallen the screamer. (4) The conventional indication of a non-word, like the indication of writing upon words, and the indication of a gesture upon the meaning of 'yes' or 'no'. (5) The rational indication of a non-word, like the indication of change upon origination, and the indication of origination upon the existence of the Creator. And from this division is the indication of the eternal speech of God Almighty—meaning the meaning subsisting in the Exalted Essence—upon its objects. As for it being non-linguistic, it is obvious, because His speech in the mentioned meaning is not a letter nor a sound. And as for it being rational: because the dependency of speech—which is its indication—is essential to it like the dependency of other attributes, and what is essential does not change nor fail, while conventional and natural indications can change as was mentioned previously; and also, the dependency of speech is eternal like the speech, while conventional and natural indications are originated.
Source pages p. 440

Commentary
This passage is a classification of types of indication (dalalah). It begins by affirming that metaphorical use is a conventional indication by type (naw'), and gives the example of Quranic words indicating their meanings—both individual and compound—arguing that compound indication is conventional, not rational. Then it enumerates five types: (1) conventional linguistic indication (not fully listed in this excerpt), (2) rational linguistic indication: when a word indicates its speaker, because a word is an accident and cannot subsist by itself, so its existence necessarily points to a substance that bears it. (3) natural linguistic indication: like the utterance 'Ah' naturally indicating pain, or an involuntary scream indicating a sudden calamity. (4) conventional non-linguistic indication: such as writing indicating spoken words, or a gesture indicating 'yes' or 'no'. (5) rational non-linguistic indication: like change (taghayyur) indicating temporal origination (huduth), and huduth indicating the existence of the Creator. The author then elaborates on the divine attribute of speech (kalam Allah al-qadim) as a rational non-linguistic indication: the eternal meaning subsisting in God's essence indicates His commands and prohibitions (muta'allaqat). It is non-linguistic because it is not composed of letters or sounds, and it is rational because its dependency (ta'alluq)—i.e., its indication—is essential (nafsi) and therefore immutable and eternal, unlike conventional and natural indications which can change and are temporal. This shows the unique status of divine speech as an object of rational inference.

وضعية
عقلية
طبيعية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

D) Smoke indicates fire.

Key Takeaway
The five types of indication (conventional, rational, natural for both words and non-words) form a complete classification that clarifies how signs convey meaning in language, theology, and daily life.

What Is Mantiq?

Indication of Divine Speech as Rational Non-Linguistic
Author argues divine speech indication is rational non-linguistic

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the eternal divine speech (kalam nafsi) is classified as a rational non-linguistic indication and why it cannot be conventional or natural.

Core Idea
God's eternal speech indicates rationally because its connection is essential and immutable, unlike temporal conventional or natural signs.

The passage applies the classification of indication to a key theological issue: the nature of God's speech. In Islamic kalam, God's speech is an eternal attribute (kalam nafsi) which indicates His commands and prohibitions. The author argues that this indication is rational non-linguistic because it is essential to His essence, not a convention or natural phenomenon.

Guided Path
1
Confirm divine speech is non-linguistic
The passage states: 'His speech in the mentioned meaning is not a letter nor a sound.' So it is not composed of words or sounds; thus it cannot be a linguistic indicator.
2
Identify the argument for its rationality
The author gives two reasons: (a) the dependency (ta'alluq) of speech—its indication—is nafsi (essential) for God, like other attributes. What is essential does not change or fail. (b) The dependency is eternal, like the speech itself. Conventional and natural indications are originated and changeable.
3
Apply the definition of rational indication
Rational indication is based on inference from cause to effect or from necessary connection. Here, because the attribute of speech necessarily indicates its objects (e.g., command to pray) by virtue of its essence, it is a rational inference for those who understand God's essence.
4
Contrast with conventional and natural
Conventional indication relies on arbitrary assignment and can change (e.g., a word can be reassigned). Natural indication is instinctive and not essential. Divine speech's indication is unchanging and essential, so it must be rational.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بِنَاءً عَلَى أَنَّ المَجَازَ مَوْضُوعٌ بِالنَّوْع، وَمِنْ ذَلِكَ : دَلَالَهُ أَلْفَاظِ القُرْآنِ عَلَى مَعَانِيهِ الإِفْرَادِيَّةِ، وَكَذَا التَّرْكِيبِيَّةِ؛ لأَنَّ التَّحْقِيقَ أَنَّ دَلَالَةَ المُرَكَّب وَضْعِيَّةٌ، لَا عَقْلِيَّةٌ.
(٢) - وَدَلَالَةُ اللَّفْظِ العَقْلِيَّةُ كَدَلَالَةِ اللَّفْظِ عَلَى لَافِظٍ يَقُومُ هُوَ بِهِ، وَهِيَ الأَلْفَاظِ؛ لِأَنَّ اللَّفْظَ عَرَضْ يَسْتَحِيلُ أَنْ يَقُومَ بِنَفْسِهِ.
(۳) - وَدَلَالَةُ اللَّفْظِ الطَّبِيعِيَّةُ كَدَلَالَةِ «أَحْ» عَلَى الوَجَعِ، وَالصُّرَاخِ الضَّرُورِيِّ عَلَى مُصِيبَةٍ نَزَلَتْ بِالصَّارِخِ.

(٥) - وَدَلَالَةُ غَيْرِ اللَّفْظِ العَقْلِيَّةُ كَدَلَالَةِ التَّغَيُّرِ عَلَى الحُدُوثِ، وَدَلَالَةِ الحُدُوثِ عَلَى وُجُودِ الخَالِقِ، وَمِنْ هَذَا القِسْمِ: دَلَالَةُ كَلَامِ اللهِ تَعَالَى القَدِيمِ ـ أَعْنِي : المَعْنَى القَائِمَ بِالذَّاتِ العَلِيَّةِ - عَلَى مُتَعَلَّقَاتِهِ : أَمَّا أَنَّهَا غَيْرُ لَفْظِيَّةٍ فَظَاهِرٌ؛ لِأَنَّ كَلَامَهُ تَعَالَى بِالمَعْنَى المَذْكُورِ لَيْسَ بِحَرْفٍ وَلَا صَوْتٍ. وَأَمَّا أَنَّهَا عَقْلِيَّةٌ : فَلِأَنَّ تَعَلَّقَ الكَلَام - وَهُوَ دَلَالَتُهُ - نَفْسِيٌّ لَهُ كَتَعَلُّقِ غَيْرِهِ مِنَ الصِّفَاتِ، وَالنَّفْسِيُّ لَا يَتَغَيَّرُ وَلَا يَتَخَلَّفُ، وَالوَضْعِيَّةُ وَالطَّبْعِيَّةُ يَصِحُ تَغَيُّرُهُمَا كَمَا تَقَدَّمَ، وَأَيْضاً : تَعَلُّقُ الكَلَامِ قَدِيمٌ كَالكَلَامِ، وَالوَضْعِيَّةُ وَالطَّبْعِيَّةُ حَادِثَتَانِ

Types of Non-Verbal Indication and Their Logical Relevance
Author enumerates three types of non-verbal indication and states that only verbal conventional indication is considered in logic.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the three types of non-verbal indication (conventional, rational, natural) and explain why only verbal conventional indication is the subject of logic.

Core Idea
Logic studies only verbal conventional indication because it is precise, general, and independent of individual variation.

In this passage, the author categorises non-verbal indication into three types: conventional, rational, and natural. After defining each, he asserts that logicians only consider the first type—verbal conventional indication. This lesson will help you parse these categories and understand the rationale for limiting logic's scope.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three categories
List the three types of non-verbal indication mentioned: conventional (وضعية), rational (عقلية), and natural (طبيعية). Note the examples given for each.
2
Examine the rational indication subcase
The author includes God's eternal speech as a special case of non-verbal rational indication. Understand why it is non-verbal (not letters/sound) and why rational (intrinsic, unchanging relation).
3
Compare the properties
Note that conventional and natural indications admit change and are temporal, while rational indication (especially divine speech relation) is intrinsic and eternal.
4
Determine the scope of logic
Why does the author say only the first type is considered? Because verbal conventional indication has precision and general benefit, as earlier in the source (not included here) but stated in the commentary.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(٤) - وَدَلَالَةُ غَيْرِ اللَّفْظِ الوَضْعِيَّةُ كَدَلَالَةِ الكِتَابَةِ عَلَى الأَلْفَاظِ، وَدَلَالَةِ الإِشَارَةِ عَلَى مَعْنَى «نَعَمْ» أَوْ «لَا». وَلَحِقَتِ التَّاء؛ لِأَنَّ المنسوب مُؤَنَّثُ وَهُوَ «دلالة». وَهَلِ المُرَادُ طَبْعُ اللفظ أَوْ طَبْعُ اللافظ؟ صَرَّحَ القطب بالثاني، فإنه لما مثل بـ«أح» قال: فإنَّ طبع اللافظ يقتضي التلفظ به عند عروض المعنى له.
(٥) - وَدَلَالَةُ غَيْرِ اللَّفْظِ العَقْلِيَّةُ كَدَلَالَةِ التَّغَيُّرِ عَلَى الحُدُوثِ، وَدَلَالَةِ الحُدُوثِ عَلَى وُجُودِ الخَالِقِ، وَمِنْ هَذَا القِسْمِ: دَلَالَةُ كَلَامِ اللهِ تَعَالَى القَدِيمِ ـ أَعْنِي: المَعْنَى القَائِمَ بِالذَّاتِ العَلِيَّةِ - عَلَى مُتَعَلَّقَاتِهِ: أَمَّا أَنَّهَا غَيْرُ لَفْظِيَّةٍ فَظَاهِرٌ؛ لِأَنَّ كَلَامَهُ تَعَالَى بِالمَعْنَى المَذْكُورِ لَيْسَ بِحَرْفٍ وَلَا صَوْتٍ. وَأَمَّا أَنَّهَا عَقْلِيَّةٌ: فَلِأَنَّ تَعَلَّقَ الكَلَامِ - وَهُوَ دَلَالَتُهُ - نَفْسِيٌّ لَهُ كَتَعَلُّقِ غَيْرِهِ مِنَ الصِّفَاتِ، وَالنَّفْسِيُّ لَا يَتَغَيَّرُ وَلَا يَتَخَلَّفُ، وَالوَضْعِيَّةُ وَالطَّبْعِيَّةُ يَصِحُ تَغَيُّرُهُمَا كَمَا تَقَدَّمَ، وَأَيْضاً: تَعَلُّقُ الكَلَامِ قَدِيمٌ كَالكَلَامِ، وَالوَضْعِيَّةُ وَالطَّبْعِيَّةُ حَادِثَتَانِ. قوله: (كَمَوْصُوفِهِمَا) أي: الموضوع والمطبوع.
(٦) - وَدَلَالَهُ غَيْرِ اللَّفْظِ الطَّبِيعِيَّةُ كَدَلَالَةِ حُمْرَةِ الوَجْهِ عَلَى الخَجَلِ، وَصُفْرَتِهِ عَلَى الوَجَلِ، وَجَمِيعُ مَا يَسْتَدِلُ بِهِ الأَطِبَاءُ عَلَى المَرَضِ مِنْ هَذَا النَّوْعِ. وَالمُعْتَبَرُ عِنْدَ القَوْمِ مِنْ هَذِهِ الأَقْسَام: القِسْمُ الأَوَّلُ فَقَط وَهُوَ دَلَالَةُ اللَّفْظِ الوَضْعِيَّةُ، وَلَهَا تَرْجَمَ النَّاظِمُ، إِلَّا أَنَّهُ تَرَكَ مِنْهَا وَصْفاً ذَكَرَهُ فِي أَوَّلِ البَيْتِ وَهُوَ: كَوْنُ الدَّلَالَةِ لَفْظِيَّةٌ.
(4) - And the conventional indication of the non-word, like the indication of writing upon words, and the indication of pointing to the meaning of 'yes' or 'no'. And the ta' was attached because the relative adjective is feminine, namely 'indication'. And is what is meant the nature of the word or the nature of the speaker? Al-Qutb explicitly stated the second; when he gave the example of 'Akh', he said: 'Indeed, the nature of the speaker necessitates uttering it when the meaning occurs to him.' (5) - And the rational indication of the non-word, like the indication of change upon temporal origination, and the indication of temporal origination upon the existence of the Creator. And from this category is the indication of the eternal speech of Allah Almighty – I mean the meaning subsisting in the exalted Self – upon its objects. As for it being non-verbal, it is apparent, because His speech in the mentioned meaning is not a letter or a sound. And as for it being rational: because the relation of speech – which is its indication – is intrinsic to it like the relation of other attributes, and the intrinsic does not change nor lag, whereas conventional and natural indication admit change as previously mentioned. Also, the relation of speech is eternal like the speech, whereas conventional and natural indication are temporal. His saying: ('like their described ones') means the subject and the natural. (6) - And the natural indication of the non-word, like the indication of redness of the face upon shame, and its pallor upon fear, and all that physicians use as evidence for illness falls under this type. And what is considered by the scholars among these categories is only the first category, which is the conventional indication of the word, and for it the poet gave a translation, except that he omitted from it a description which he mentioned at the beginning of the verse, namely: that the indication is verbal.
Source pages p. 441

Commentary
This passage is definitional, enumerating three types of non-verbal indication and concluding that only the first type (verbal conventional indication) is relevant in logic. The author first defines non-verbal conventional indication (دلالة غير اللفظ الوضعية) with examples: writing indicates spoken words, and pointing indicates 'yes' or 'no'. A gloss clarifies the feminine form 'دلالة' and a debate about whether 'nature' refers to the word's nature or the speaker's nature, citing al-Qutb who opts for the speaker's nature with the example of 'Akh' as a natural utterance of pain. Next, rational indication (دلالة غير اللفظ العقلية) is defined with examples: change indicates temporal origination, and temporal origination indicates the Creator. A special case is the indication of God's eternal speech (the meaning subsisting in His essence) upon its objects. The author argues this indication is non-verbal because God's speech is not a letter or sound, and rational because the relation of speech to its objects is intrinsic and unchanging, unlike conventional and natural indications which admit change and are temporal. The gloss 'like their described ones' refers to the conventional and natural categories. Third, natural indication (دلالة غير اللفظ الطبيعية) is defined with examples: redness of face indicates shame, pallor indicates fear, and medical symptoms indicate illness. Finally, the author states that logicians only consider the first category—verbal conventional indication—and notes that the poet omitted the qualifier 'verbal' from the verse, though it is understood from context. The logical teaching is that the precision and general benefit of conventional verbal indication make it the sole subject of logic, as it does not vary between individuals and covers both existent and non-existent things.

Key Terms
دلالة غير اللفظ الوضعية
دلالة غير اللفظ العقلية
دلالة غير اللفظ الطبيعية
تعلق الكلام
