مُنْفَرِدُ المنفرد مقابل المشترك، ولم يشر المصنف إليه هنا، وتكلّم عليه صاحب المختصر حيث قال : وهو مشترك إن تعدّد مسماه كـ: «عين»، ومنفرد إنِ اتَّحد كـ: «إنسان، ورجل»، فنحو: «إنسان ورجل متواطئ باعتبار، ومنفرد باعتبار آخر.
The third division of the four divisions according to the author: that the word is one and its meaning is multiple, and it is the mushtarak - with fat-ha on the ra - and it is that whose named entity is multiple; i.e., what was placed for it as a real placement, by being placed for a specific meaning, then for another specific meaning without consideration of transfer from the first meaning to the second, like 'ayn, for it is placed for the eye, and placed also for the spring, and likewise for coin, and others without consideration of transfer from one to another, and it is not placed for a single meaning that is a common core between them. And likewise 'qur'u' for purity and menstruation. Unlike e.g., 'insan', for it is mufrad (single) because its named entity is one. And the mutabayin and dhu'l-wajh... (poem). His statement: 'and its meaning is multiple' - the correct is 'its named entity', as al-Hilali expressed following al-Mukhtasar, for meaning includes metaphor, and metaphor is not considered mushtarak, even if we say it is placed, because mushtarakity is considered by the first placement, as this commentator indicated by his saying 'a real placement'. And it was said in Jam' al-Jawami': 'And its opposite if it is true in both then it is mushtarak'. By this you know what happened to Qadurah here, where he said: 'like 'ayn, for it is placed for the eye, and for spring water, and gold, and spy', so he included 'spy' here. His statement: 'then for another meaning' indicates multiple placements, and by this is excluded the definite articles other than proper names, because they, according to what al-Sayyid chose, were placed for particulars, which would require that they are of the type of mushtarak since their object is multiple, but their placement is not multiple. His statement: 'like 'ayn' - his example with 'ayn and 'qur'u' indicates that its named entities must all be common nouns; if its named entities are all proper names like a proper name with multiple bearers, or different like al-Harith as a proper name and as an attribute, or al-Fadl as a proper name and as a source, it is not called mushtarak, because mushtarakity is considered relative to one placement, and the proper name often has multiple placers; this was mentioned by al-'Abadi, and al-Yusi followed him in his notes on al-Mukhtasar, and al-Sayyid explicitly stated that all three divisions are of the type of mushtarak. His statement: 'unlike e.g., 'insan', for it is mufrad' - mufrad is the opposite of mushtarak, and the author did not point to it here, and the author of al-Mukhtasar discussed it where he said: 'It is mushtarak if its named entity is multiple like 'ayn, and mufrad if single like 'insan' and 'rajul'. So e.g., 'insan' and 'rajul' are mutawati' in one respect and mufrad in another respect.
Source pages p. 530

Commentary
This passage is a definitional exposition of the third division of the fourfold classification of words in relation to their meanings: the homonym (mushtarak). The author defines it as a single word with multiple named entities (musammayāt), each established by an independent, original linguistic placement (waḍ‘ ḥaqīqī). The example of ‘ayn (eye, spring, coin) and qur’u (menstrual purity, menstruation) illustrate that the various meanings are not derived from a single core meaning. The commentary refines this definition by clarifying that the term must have multiple original placements, not metaphorical transfers, and that the named entities must be common nouns (shā’i‘a), not proper names (which have multiple placements but are not considered mushtarak in the technical sense of logic). The passage also distinguishes mushtarak from mufrad (univocal) like insān (human), which has a single named entity. It notes that some like al-Sayyid al-Sharif consider proper names with multiple bearers to be mushtarak, but the dominant view excludes them because the placement (waḍ‘) is not multiple but rather multiple applications of the same placement.

مُنْفَرِد
وَضْع حَقِيقِيّ
مُسَمَّى

Key Takeaway
Mushtarak is a single word with multiple named entities each established by an independent original placement, excluding metaphor and proper names.

Refinements: What Counts as Mushtarak?
The author defines the mushtarak as a word with multiple meanings placed independently.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the refinements to determine whether a given word is truly mushtarak according to the logicians, distinguishing it from metaphors and proper names.

Core Idea
Only words with multiple original placements are mushtarak; metaphors and proper names with multiple bearers are not.

The commentator presents critical refinements to the definition of mushtarak. He corrects the author's phrase 'meaning' to 'named entity', excludes metaphor, and addresses proper names. He also clarifies that the named entities must be common nouns (shā’i‘a). These refinements ensure that the category remains precise and applicable in logical analysis.

Guided Path
1
Identify the corrections
The commentator says the correct phrase is 'its named entity is multiple', not 'its meaning is multiple'. This excludes metaphor, because metaphor has a transferred meaning but the original placement is only one.
Find the sentence: 'صوابُهُ : «مسمَّاه)'
2
Understand the exclusion of metaphor
Even if metaphor is considered a placement (some say it is), mushtarakity is based on the first placement (al-waḍ‘ al-awwal). Metaphor is a transfer, so it does not count as a new placement.
The commentator cites Jam' al-Jawami'.
3
Examine the proper name issue
Words like 'al-Harith' which can refer to multiple individuals are not mushtarak because the placement is not multiple; the same word is placed for a single concept (a proper name) but applies to multiple individuals accidentally. The passage mentions that al-Sayyid al-Sharif considers them mushtarak, but the dominant view is otherwise.
The requirement that the named entities be common nouns (shā’i‘a) is key.
4
Distinguish from mufrad
Mufrad (like insan) has a single named entity. The passage contrasts mushtarak with mufrad. Some words like 'insan' and 'rajul' are mutawati' (univocal) in one respect and mufrad in another, but the focus here is on the number of named entities.
This clarifies the opposite category.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

أَيْ : مَا وُضِعَ هُوَ لَهُ وَضْعاً حَقِيقِيًّا ؛ بِأَنْ وُضِعَ لِمَعْنَّى بِخُصُوصِهِ، ثُمَّ لِمَعْنَى آخَرَ بِخُصُوصِهِ مِنْ غَيْرِ اعْتِبَارِ نَقْلِهِ مِنَ الْمَعْنَى الأَوَّلِ إِلَى الثَّانِي كَـ: باعتباره، وإن قلنا : إنَّه موضوع؛ لأنَّ الاشتراك معتبر بالوضع الأوَّل، كما أشار له هذا الشارح بقوله : «وضعاً حقيقياً». وقال في جمع الجوامع : وعكسه إن كان حقيقة فيهما فمشترك»، وبه تعلم ما وقع لقدورة هنا؛ حيث قال: «كالعين، فإنَّها موضوعة للباصرة، ولعين الماء والذَّهب، والجاسوس»، فأدخل الجاسوس هنا .قوله : (ثُمَّ لِمَعْنَى آخَرَ فيه إشعار بتعدد الوضع، وبه يخرج ما عدا العلم مِنَ المعارف؛ لأنَّها على ما اختاره السَّيّد وضعت لجزئيات، فإنَّه يقتضي أنَّها مِن قبيل المشترك؛ حيث تعدّد فيها الموضوع له، لكن لم يتعدّد فيها الوضع. قوله : (گ): «عَيْنِ) تمثيله بـ «عین» و «قرء» يُشعر بأنَّ مسمياته لا تكون واحد، والعِلمُ قد تعدَّد واضعه غالباً؛ ذكره العبادي، وجرى عليه اليوسي في حواشي المختصر، وصرَّح السَّيّد بأنَّ الأقسام الثلاثة كلُّها مِن قبيل المشترك. قوله : (بِخِلَافِ نَحْوِ : «إِنْسَانِ»، فَإِنَّهُ مُنْفَرِدُ المنفرد مقابل المشترك، ولم يشر المصنف إليه هنا، وتكلّم عليه صاحب المختصر حيث قال : وهو مشترك إن تعدّد مسماه كـ: «عين»، ومنفرد إنِ اتَّحد كـ: «إنسان، ورجل»، فنحو: «إنسان ورجل متواطئ باعتبار، ومنفرد باعتبار آخر.
The third division of the four divisions according to the author: that the word is one and its meaning is multiple, and it is the mushtarak - with fat-ha on the ra - and it is that whose named entity is multiple; i.e., what was placed for it as a real placement, by being placed for a specific meaning, then for another specific meaning without consideration of transfer from the first meaning to the second, like 'ayn, for it is placed for the eye, and placed also for the spring, and likewise for coin, and others without consideration of transfer from one to another, and it is not placed for a single meaning that is a common core between them. And likewise 'qur'u' for purity and menstruation. Unlike e.g., 'insan', for it is mufrad (single) because its named entity is one. And the mutabayin and dhu'l-wajh... (poem). His statement: 'and its meaning is multiple' - the correct is 'its named entity', as al-Hilali expressed following al-Mukhtasar, for meaning includes metaphor, and metaphor is not considered mushtarak, even if we say it is placed, because mushtarakity is considered by the first placement, as this commentator indicated by his saying 'a real placement'. And it was said in Jam' al-Jawami': 'And its opposite if it is true in both then it is mushtarak'. By this you know what happened to Qadurah here, where he said: 'like 'ayn, for it is placed for the eye, and for spring water, and gold, and spy', so he included 'spy' here. His statement: 'then for another meaning' indicates multiple placements, and by this is excluded the definite articles other than proper names, because they, according to what al-Sayyid chose, were placed for particulars, which would require that they are of the type of mushtarak since their object is multiple, but their placement is not multiple. His statement: 'like 'ayn' - his example with 'ayn and 'qur'u' indicates that its named entities must all be common nouns; if its named entities are all proper names like a proper name with multiple bearers, or different like al-Harith as a proper name and as an attribute, or al-Fadl as a proper name and as a source, it is not called mushtarak, because mushtarakity is considered relative to one placement, and the proper name often has multiple placers; this was mentioned by al-'Abadi, and al-Yusi followed him in his notes on al-Mukhtasar, and al-Sayyid explicitly stated that all three divisions are of the type of mushtarak. His statement: 'unlike e.g., 'insan', for it is mufrad' - mufrad is the opposite of mushtarak, and the author did not point to it here, and the author of al-Mukhtasar discussed it where he said: 'It is mushtarak if its named entity is multiple like 'ayn, and mufrad if single like 'insan' and 'rajul'. So e.g., 'insan' and 'rajul' are mutawati' in one respect and mufrad in another respect.
Source pages p. 530

Commentary
This passage is a definitional exposition of the third division of the fourfold classification of words in relation to their meanings: the homonym (mushtarak). The author defines it as a single word with multiple named entities (musammayāt), each established by an independent, original linguistic placement (waḍ‘ ḥaqīqī). The example of ‘ayn (eye, spring, coin) and qur’u (menstrual purity, menstruation) illustrate that the various meanings are not derived from a single core meaning. The commentary refines this definition by clarifying that the term must have multiple original placements, not metaphorical transfers, and that the named entities must be common nouns (shā’i‘a), not proper names (which have multiple placements but are not considered mushtarak in the technical sense of logic). The passage also distinguishes mushtarak from mufrad (univocal) like insān (human), which has a single named entity. It notes that some like al-Sayyid al-Sharif consider proper names with multiple bearers to be mushtarak, but the dominant view excludes them because the placement (waḍ‘) is not multiple but rather multiple applications of the same placement.

مُسَمَّى

A) Because it has multiple meanings, but not all are common nouns.
B) Because it is a proper name, and its placement is not multiple; it is one word placed for a single concept that applies to multiple individuals.
C) Because it has a metaphorical meaning.
D) Because it is a common noun.

Key Takeaway
The refined definition excludes metaphors and proper names from mushtarak, reserving it for common nouns with multiple independent placements.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

Then consider 'mawlā' which can mean master, freed slave, etc. Is it mushtarak? Check if each meaning has an independent original placement.

Two Methods for Dividing Speech and the Dispute over Talab
Expansion on division of speech and talab dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two methods for dividing speech into khabar and insha' and determine where talab is classified in each.

Core Idea
Talab straddles present and future, causing a dispute over its classification.

In this passage, the commentator presents two ways to divide speech: one that places talab under insha', and another that makes it independent. By understanding the basis of the dispute—the two times of talab—you will see how logical classification depends on perspective. This lesson walks you through both division schemes and the key point of disagreement.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two division schemes
Find the two ways the passage divides speech: first method: khabar and insha', then insha' into talab and tanbih. Second method: three divisions (khabar, insha', talab).
The passage says 'the second method' but refers to a prior method in the poem.
2
Determine the basis of difference
The passage states talab has two times: present (time of request) and future (time of action). Considering the present places it in insha'; considering the future makes it separate.
3
Note the commentator's preference
The commentator says 'whoever looks at the first (present) is correct', emphasizing that the linguistic meaning is the present request, not future compliance.
He critiques the second perspective as not about the word's signification.
4
Relate to the poem
The first method is in the poem, but the word 'insha' is omitted; the commentator explains the omission and shows it is implied.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الطَّرِيقَةُ الثَّانِيَةُ : أَنَّ القِسْمَةَ تُنَائِيَّةٌ ، وَأَنَّهُ يَنْقَسِمُ إِلَى : خَبَرٍ، وَإِنْشَاء فَقَط ; ثُمَّ الإِنْشَاءُ يَنْقَسِمُ إِلَى : طَلَبٍ، وَتَنْبِيه . فَاخْتِلَافُ الطَّرِيقَتَيْنِ فِي الطَّلَبِ هَلْ هُوَ دَاخِل فِي الإِنْشَاءِ، أَوْ قِسْمٌ بِرَأْسِهِ ؟ وَوَجْهُ الخِلَافِ : أَنَّ الطَّلَبَ لَهُ زَمَنَانِ : زَمَنْ حَالِيٌّ وَهُوَ زَمَنُ الطَّلَبِ، وَاسْتِقْبَالِيٌّ وَهُوَ زَمَنُ الحَدَثِ . فَمَنْ نَظَرَ إِلَى الأَوَّلِ أَدْرَجَهُ فِي الإِنْشَاءِ، وَمَنْ نَظَرَ إِلَى الثَّانِي جَعَلَهُ قِسْماً بِرَأْسِهِ. وَالطَّرِيقَةُ الأُوْلَى هِيَ الَّتي في النَّظم، ثُمَّ الطَّلَبُ يَشْمَلُ طَلَبَ الفِعْلِ وَهُوَ الأَمْرُ، وَطَلَبَ الكَفِّ وَهُوَ النَّهِيُّ ، وَطَلَبَ العِلْمِ بِالمَاهِيَّةِ وَهُوَ الِاسْتِفْهَامُ . ما احْتَمَلَ المَيْنَ لِذَاتِهِ خَبَر قَضِيَّةٌ، وَالعَكْسُ إِنْشَاءُ ظَهَر ثمَّ الإنشاء ينقسم إلى : طلب، وتنبيه؛ وذلك : أنَّ اللفظ إن دلّ بالقصد الأوّل على طلب فعل وهو الأمر، أو كفّ وهو النَّهي، أو علم بالماهية وهو الاستفهام سمّي: «طلباً»، وإلا سمي: «تنبيها» كـ: التمني، والترجي، والنداء، والعرض، والتخصيص، والدُّعاء؛ لأنَّ دلالتها على الطلب لا بالقصد الأول. قوله : (فَمَنْ نَظَرَ إِلَى الأَوَّلِ) هذا هو الحقُّ؛ لأنَّ النَّظر الثَّاني ليس نظراً في الحقيقة في مدلول اللَّفظ ؛ لأنَّ مدلول «قم» مثلاً هو الأمر بالقيام والامتثال وعدمه خارج عن مدلول اللفظ . : وحاصلُهُ أنَّ الطَّلب له :زمنان زمنٌ مِن حيث هو إنشاء وهو حالي، وزمن حدوث الفعل وهو مستقبل؛ فطلب حدوث الحدث مِنَ المخاطب مقارن للتَّلفظ به، وحدوث ذلك مِنَ المخاطب مستقبل، ومعناه الذي وضع له هو الأوّل، والثاني متعلق معناه، وعليه : فإن أُريد تعريفه من حيث كونه إنشاء قلت: «ما قارن معناه زمان التكلم به». وإن أُريد تعريفه من حيث الخصوصيَّة التي يتميّز بها عن مطلق الإنشاء قلت: «ما تأخّر معناه عن زمان التلفظ به . قوله : (وَالطَّرِيقَةُ الأُولَى هِيَ الَّتِي فِي النَّظم أي : إلَّا أنَّه حذف لفظ «الإنشاء»، فيكون في كلامه حذف «الواو» مع ما عطفت والدليل على ذلك : ذكر النَّاظم الطلب.
The second method: that the division is binary, and that it divides only into news (khabar) and construction (insha'). Then insha' divides into request (talab) and notification (tanbih). So the difference between the two methods is whether talab is included in insha' or is an independent division. The basis of the difference: that talab has two times: a present time, which is the time of the request, and a future time, which is the time of the event. Whoever looks at the first includes it in insha', and whoever looks at the second makes it an independent division. The first method is the one in the poem. Then talab includes request for action, which is command (amr), request for cessation, which is prohibition (nahy), and request for knowledge of the quiddity, which is interrogation (istifham). [Matn:] 'What admits of falsity in itself is a proposition (qadiyya) of news (khabar), and the reverse is insha' that appears. Then insha' divides into talab and tanbih; that is: if the word indicates, with the primary intent, a request for action – which is amr, or cessation – which is nahy, or knowledge of the quiddity – which is istifham, it is called 'talab'; otherwise it is called 'tanbih', like wish, hope, calling, presenting, specifying, and supplication, because their indication of request is not with primary intent.' He said: 'So whoever looks at the first' – this is the truth, because the second look is not really a look into the signification of the word, for the signification of 'stand' for example is the command to stand, and compliance or non-compliance is outside the signification of the word. The summary: that talab has two times: a time from the aspect that it is insha', which is present, and a time of the occurrence of the action, which is future. So the request for the occurrence of the event from the addressee is concomitant with the utterance, and the occurrence from the addressee is future, and its meaning that it is placed for is the first, and the second is related to its meaning. Accordingly, if one intends to define it from the aspect that it is insha', one says: 'That whose meaning is concomitant with the time of speaking.' And if one intends to define it from the aspect of the specificity by which it is distinguished from absolute insha', one says: 'That whose meaning is delayed from the time of utterance.' He said: 'And the first method is the one in the poem' – meaning except that he omitted the word 'insha', so in his speech there is omission of the 'waw' together with what it conjoins, and the evidence for that is the mention of talab by the author.
Source pages p. 534

Commentary
This passage is a definitional and analytic discussion of the classification of speech into khabar and insha', and the dispute over whether talab is a subdivision of insha' or a separate category. The commentator presents the second method that divides speech binarily into khabar and insha', then insha' into talab and tanbih. The point of disagreement is whether talab belongs within insha' or is an independent division. The basis is that talab has two times: the present time of utterance and the future time of the action. Considering the present time makes it insha', considering the future makes it a separate division. The first method (the one in the poem) is preferred. The commentator then quotes the matn defining talab as words indicating request with primary intent, and tanbih as otherwise. He then explains that the correct view is to look at the present time, because the meaning of 'stand' is the command itself, not compliance. He defines talab generically as 'that whose meaning is concomitant with the time of speaking' (as insha') and specifically as 'that whose meaning is delayed from the time of utterance' (as opposed to other insha'). Finally, he clarifies that the poem's method omits the word 'insha' but implies it, as evidenced by the author's mention of talab.

زمنان
تنبيه
أمر

According to the commentator, what is the correct view regarding the classification of talab?
A) Talab is a separate qism from insha' because of its future time.
B) Talab is included in insha' because its present time determines its nature.
C) Talab is neither, it is a third category.
D) The dispute is unresolved.

Key Takeaway
The classification of talab depends on which of its two times (present request or future action) is taken as primary; the correct view includes it in insha'.

The Two Times of Talab and Its Definition
Analytical expansion on the two times of talab and its definitions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the present and future dimensions of talab and construct the two definitions of talab given in the passage.

Core Idea
Talab's meaning is present (request), while its fulfillment is future; definition captures this duality.

This passage delves into the nature of talab by examining its two times: the present moment of the request and the future moment of the action. The commentator uses this analysis to provide two definitions: one that defines talab as a type of insha' (present time), and another that distinguishes it from other insha' (delayed meaning). This lesson will help you understand how time is integral to the logical definition of talab.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the two times of talab
The passage explicitly states that talab has a present time (time of request) and a future time (time of the event). Note that the request itself occurs at the moment of utterance.
The present time is called 'zaman hali' and the future 'zaman istiqbali'.
2
Understand the consequence of each perspective
If you consider the present time, talab is insha' because the meaning is concurrent with speech. If you consider the future, talab seems independent because the action is not yet realized.
The commentator says considering the future is not about the linguistic meaning.
3
Extract the first definition (as insha')
The commentator says: if you want to define talab from the aspect of being insha', you say: 'That whose meaning is concomitant with the time of speaking.' This definition aligns talab with other insha'.
4
Extract the second definition (as specific)
To define talab in its specificity (distinguishing it from other insha' like tanbih), you say: 'That whose meaning is delayed from the time of utterance.' This captures the future aspect.
Other insha' (tanbih) like tamannī have their meaning present, not delayed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الطَّرِيقَةُ الثَّانِيَةُ : أَنَّ القِسْمَةَ تُنَائِيَّةٌ ، وَأَنَّهُ يَنْقَسِمُ إِلَى : خَبَرٍ، وَإِنْشَاء فَقَط ; ثُمَّ الإِنْشَاءُ يَنْقَسِمُ إِلَى : طَلَبٍ، وَتَنْبِيه . فَاخْتِلَافُ الطَّرِيقَتَيْنِ فِي الطَّلَبِ هَلْ هُوَ دَاخِل فِي الإِنْشَاءِ، أَوْ قِسْمٌ بِرَأْسِهِ ؟ وَوَجْهُ الخِلَافِ : أَنَّ الطَّلَبَ لَهُ زَمَنَانِ : زَمَنْ حَالِيٌّ وَهُوَ زَمَنُ الطَّلَبِ، وَاسْتِقْبَالِيٌّ وَهُوَ زَمَنُ الحَدَثِ . فَمَنْ نَظَرَ إِلَى الأَوَّلِ أَدْرَجَهُ فِي الإِنْشَاءِ، وَمَنْ نَظَرَ إِلَى الثَّانِي جَعَلَهُ قِسْماً بِرَأْسِهِ. وَالطَّرِيقَةُ الأُوْلَى هِيَ الَّتي في النَّظم، ثُمَّ الطَّلَبُ يَشْمَلُ طَلَبَ الفِعْلِ وَهُوَ الأَمْرُ، وَطَلَبَ الكَفِّ وَهُوَ النَّهِيُّ ، وَطَلَبَ العِلْمِ بِالمَاهِيَّةِ وَهُوَ الِاسْتِفْهَامُ . ما احْتَمَلَ المَيْنَ لِذَاتِهِ خَبَر قَضِيَّةٌ، وَالعَكْسُ إِنْشَاءُ ظَهَر ثمَّ الإنشاء ينقسم إلى : طلب، وتنبيه؛ وذلك : أنَّ اللفظ إن دلّ بالقصد الأوّل على طلب فعل وهو الأمر، أو كفّ وهو النَّهي، أو علم بالماهية وهو الاستفهام سمّي: «طلباً»، وإلا سمي: «تنبيها» كـ: التمني، والترجي، والنداء، والعرض، والتخصيص، والدُّعاء؛ لأنَّ دلالتها على الطلب لا بالقصد الأول. قوله : (فَمَنْ نَظَرَ إِلَى الأَوَّلِ) هذا هو الحقُّ؛ لأنَّ النَّظر الثَّاني ليس نظراً في الحقيقة في مدلول اللَّفظ ؛ لأنَّ مدلول «قم» مثلاً هو الأمر بالقيام والامتثال وعدمه خارج عن مدلول اللفظ . : وحاصلُهُ أنَّ الطَّلب له :زمنان زمنٌ مِن حيث هو إنشاء وهو حالي، وزمن حدوث الفعل وهو مستقبل؛ فطلب حدوث الحدث مِنَ المخاطب مقارن للتَّلفظ به، وحدوث ذلك مِنَ المخاطب مستقبل، ومعناه الذي وضع له هو الأوّل، والثاني متعلق معناه، وعليه : فإن أُريد تعريفه من حيث كونه إنشاء قلت: «ما قارن معناه زمان التكلم به». وإن أُريد تعريفه من حيث الخصوصيَّة التي يتميّز بها عن مطلق الإنشاء قلت: «ما تأخّر معناه عن زمان التلفظ به . قوله : (وَالطَّرِيقَةُ الأُولَى هِيَ الَّتِي فِي النَّظم أي : إلَّا أنَّه حذف لفظ «الإنشاء»، فيكون في كلامه حذف «الواو» مع ما عطفت والدليل على ذلك : ذكر النَّاظم الطلب.
The second method: that the division is binary, and that it divides only into news (khabar) and construction (insha'). Then insha' divides into request (talab) and notification (tanbih). So the difference between the two methods is whether talab is included in insha' or is an independent division. The basis of the difference: that talab has two times: a present time, which is the time of the request, and a future time, which is the time of the event. Whoever looks at the first includes it in insha', and whoever looks at the second makes it an independent division. The first method is the one in the poem. Then talab includes request for action, which is command (amr), request for cessation, which is prohibition (nahy), and request for knowledge of the quiddity, which is interrogation (istifham). [Matn:] 'What admits of falsity in itself is a proposition (qadiyya) of news (khabar), and the reverse is insha' that appears. Then insha' divides into talab and tanbih; that is: if the word indicates, with the primary intent, a request for action – which is amr, or cessation – which is nahy, or knowledge of the quiddity – which is istifham, it is called 'talab'; otherwise it is called 'tanbih', like wish, hope, calling, presenting, specifying, and supplication, because their indication of request is not with primary intent.' He said: 'So whoever looks at the first' – this is the truth, because the second look is not really a look into the signification of the word, for the signification of 'stand' for example is the command to stand, and compliance or non-compliance is outside the signification of the word. The summary: that talab has two times: a time from the aspect that it is insha', which is present, and a time of the occurrence of the action, which is future. So the request for the occurrence of the event from the addressee is concomitant with the utterance, and the occurrence from the addressee is future, and its meaning that it is placed for is the first, and the second is related to its meaning. Accordingly, if one intends to define it from the aspect that it is insha', one says: 'That whose meaning is concomitant with the time of speaking.' And if one intends to define it from the aspect of the specificity by which it is distinguished from absolute insha', one says: 'That whose meaning is delayed from the time of utterance.' He said: 'And the first method is the one in the poem' – meaning except that he omitted the word 'insha', so in his speech there is omission of the 'waw' together with what it conjoins, and the evidence for that is the mention of talab by the author.
Source pages p. 534

Commentary
This passage is a definitional and analytic discussion of the classification of speech into khabar and insha', and the dispute over whether talab is a subdivision of insha' or a separate category. The commentator presents the second method that divides speech binarily into khabar and insha', then insha' into talab and tanbih. The point of disagreement is whether talab belongs within insha' or is an independent division. The basis is that talab has two times: the present time of utterance and the future time of the action. Considering the present time makes it insha', considering the future makes it a separate division. The first method (the one in the poem) is preferred. The commentator then quotes the matn defining talab as words indicating request with primary intent, and tanbih as otherwise. He then explains that the correct view is to look at the present time, because the meaning of 'stand' is the command itself, not compliance. He defines talab generically as 'that whose meaning is concomitant with the time of speaking' (as insha') and specifically as 'that whose meaning is delayed from the time of utterance' (as opposed to other insha'). Finally, he clarifies that the poem's method omits the word 'insha' but implies it, as evidenced by the author's mention of talab.

زمنان
زمن حالي
زمن استقبالي

Key Takeaway
Talab is defined by its present (request) and future (action) times; its generic definition as insha' focuses on the present, while its specific definition highlights the future delay.

Subdivision of Talab into Command, Supplication, and Request
Commentator defines amr, du'a', and iltimas based on the speaker's status.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the three subtypes of talab (amr, du'a', iltimas) based on the speaker's manner (isti'la', khudū', or neutral) and distinguish amr from actual superiority.

Core Idea
Command is defined by the manner of seeking superiority, not by actual rank.

In this passage, the commentator explains how the request for action (talab al-fi'l) is subdivided into three categories based on the speaker's attitude. Understanding these distinctions is crucial for correctly interpreting commands in Arabic texts, especially in usul al-fiqh and tafsir.

Guided Path
1
Identify the divided category
The passage states that what is divided into command, supplication, and request is 'the first' (al-awwal), i.e., talab al-fi'l (request for action).
This is the category being subdivided.
2
Define amr
Amr is defined as a request made in the manner of seeking superiority (isti'la'), regardless of whether the speaker is actually superior. The key is the manner, not the status.
Isti'la' is specified as 'talab al-'uluww' (seeking high status).
3
Define du'a'
Du'a' is the opposite: a request made with humility (khudū'). It is the countertype of isti'la'.
Typically directed to God or a superior.
4
Define iltimas
Iltimas is a request devoid of both superiority and humility; it is neutral.
Often used between peers.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في بيان نسبة الألفاظ للمعاني. لَكِنَّ المُقْسَمَ مِنْهُ إِلَى أَمْرٍ وَدُعَاءِ وَالتِمَاس هُوَ الأَوَّلُ , فَالأَمْرُ هُوَ مَا كَانَ عَلَى وَجْهِ الاسْتِعْلَاءِ ; أَيْ : طَلَبِ العُلُوِّ ; سَوَاءٌ كَانَ عالياً فِي نَفْسِ الأَمْرِ , أَمْ لَا. وَالدُّعَاءُ هُوَ مَا كَانَ عَلَى وَجْهِ الخُضُوعِ، وَهُوَ ضِدُّ الاسْتِعْلَاءِ. وَالالتِمَاسُ هُوَ مَا كَانَ مُجَرَّداً عَنْهُمَا
A chapter on explaining the relation of words to meanings. However, what is divided from it into command, supplication, and request is the first [i.e., request for action]. So the command is that which is in the manner of seeking superiority (isti'la'), i.e., seeking high status (uluww), whether he is actually high in reality or not. And supplication is that which is in the manner of humility (khudū'), and it is the opposite of seeking superiority. And request (iltimās) is that which is devoid of both.
Source pages p. 535

Commentary
This passage defines the three subtypes of talab al-fi'l (request for action): command (amr), supplication (du'a'), and request (iltimas). The commentator states that the division of talab into these three applies specifically to the first type of talab (request for action). Amr is defined as a request issued in a manner of seeking superiority (isti'la'), meaning the speaker adopts a superior attitude, whether or not he is actually superior. Du'a' is the opposite: it is a request made with humility (khudū') towards the addressee, typically directed to God. Iltimas is neutral, devoid of both superiority and humility. These definitions are essential for understanding the different modes of command in Arabic; for example, a command from a ruler is amr, while a prayer to God is du'a', and a peer-to-peer request is iltimas.

دعاء
التماس
استعلاء

D) A request devoid of any attitude.

Key Takeaway
Amr is defined by the manner of isti'la' (seeking superiority), du'a' by humility, and iltimas by being neutral; actual status is irrelevant for amr.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

Four Scholarly Opinions on the Conditions for Command (Amr)
Commentator presents and discusses four scholarly opinions on the conditions for amr.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and compare the four scholarly opinions on the conditions for command (amr) in usul al-fiqh, and evaluate the evidence for each, particularly the rebuttal of the verse about Pharaoh.

Core Idea
The conditions for a valid command — isti'la' and 'uluww — are disputed; the majority holds neither is required.

In usul al-fiqh, scholars debate what makes a request a genuine command (amr). Is it simply the form, or does the speaker need to be in a position of superiority? This passage from al-Bajuri's commentary presents four opinions — from requiring only isti'la' (seeking superiority) to requiring neither — and addresses a key Quranic objection.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four opinions
List each opinion and the scholars associated with it: (1) isti'la' only (Ibn al-Hajib, al-Amidi), (2) neither (al-`Adud, al-Baydawi, majority), (3) both, (4) 'uluww only (al-Shirazi, al-Sam'ani, Ibn al-Sabbagh).
2
Understand the key terms
Distinguish between isti'la' (seeking superiority) and 'uluww (actual superiority). The first opinion requires only isti'la', not actual superiority.
3
Analyze the rebuttal
Some argued that Pharaoh's verse shows amr does not require superiority because Pharaoh was not truly superior. The commentator rebuts that the usage is metaphorical, meaning 'you indicate', not a literal command, and that the people's worship of Pharaoh implies they considered him superior.
4
Evaluate the strength of each opinion
Consider which opinion Ibn al-Humam considered correct (isti'la' only) and why the majority might hold that neither condition is required for a valid amr.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثُمَّ اعْتِبَارُ اللِاسْتِعْلَاءِ فَقَطْ فِي الأَمْرِ دُونَ العُلُوِّ هُوَ قَوْلُ ابْنِ الحَاجِبِ وَالآمِدِيِّ، وَهُوَ أَحَدُ أَقْوَالٍ أَرْبَعَةٍ ; قَالَ ابْنُ الهُمَام فِي تَحْرِيرِهِ : وَهُوَ الحَقُّ، وَقَوْلُهُ تَعَالَى حِكَايَةٌ عَنْ فِرْعَونَ : فَمَاذَا تَأْمُرُونَ ﴾ [الشعراء: ٣٥] مَجَازٌ عَنْ تُشِيرُونَ»; قوله : (وَهُوَ أَحَدُ أَقْوَالٍ أَرْبَعَةٍ ثانيها : قيل : إنَّه لا يُعتبر فيه علوٌّ ولا استعلاء، وهو ما مشى عليه العضد والبيضاوي، وهو مذهب الأكثر، وصدَّر به السبكي، وقال قدورة: إنَّه الأصح عند علماء الأصول. وقيل : يعتبر كلُّ واحدٍ منهما . وقيل : يعتبر العلو فقط، وهو مذهب الشيرازي والسَّمعاني وابن الصَّباغ. قوله : (وَقَوْلُهُ تَعَالَى حِكَايَةٌ عَنْ فِرْعَونَ) المقصود من هذا الكلام الرَّدُّ على مَنِ احتج بهذه الآية على أنَّه لا يُعتبر في الأمر عُلوٌّ ولا استعلاء ; إذ لا يتوهم هنا علوٌّ ولا استعلاء; بدليل: أنَّهم كانوا يعبدونه ويقاتلون على دينه .
Then considering only isti'la' in the command without 'uluww is the saying of Ibn al-Hajib and al-Amidi, and it is one of four opinions; Ibn al-Humam said in his Tahrir: it is the truth. And His statement Almighty, narrating from Pharaoh: 'So what do you command?' (Ash-Shu'ara: 35) is metaphorical for 'you indicate'. He said: 'And it is one of four opinions.' The second: it is said that neither 'uluww nor isti'la' is considered in it, and that is what al-`Adud and al-Baydawi followed, and it is the majority position, and al-Subki prefaced with it, and Qudura said it is the most correct with the scholars of usul. And it is said: each of the two is considered. And it is said: only 'uluww is considered, and that is the school of al-Shirazi, al-Sam'ani, and Ibn al-Sabbagh. He said: 'And His statement Almighty narrating from Pharaoh' – the intent of this speech is to refute those who use this verse as evidence that neither 'uluww nor isti'la' is considered in command, since here neither 'uluww nor isti'la' is imagined, as evidence that they used to worship him and fight for his religion.
Source pages p. 535

Commentary
This passage presents the four scholarly opinions on what conditions are required for a command (amr). The first opinion, attributed to Ibn al-Hajib and al-Amidi, is that isti'la' alone is sufficient, without actual 'uluww. Ibn al-Humam affirms this as correct. The second opinion, held by al-`Adud, al-Baydawi, and the majority, is that neither isti'la' nor 'uluww is required – any request can be called amr regardless of the speaker's status. The third opinion is that both isti'la' and 'uluww are required. The fourth is that only 'uluww (actual superiority) is required, associated with al-Shirazi, al-Sam'ani, and Ibn al-Sabbagh. The commentator then addresses a potential objection from the verse where Pharaoh says 'fa-madha ta'murun' (So what do you command?). Some argued that since Pharaoh is not truly superior, this shows amr does not require superiority. The commentator rebuts that this usage is metaphorical, meaning 'you indicate', not a literal command. The evidence is that the people worshipped Pharaoh and fought for his religion, indicating they considered him superior, so the verse actually supports the opposite.

Key Terms
استعلاء (isti'la'): Seeking superiority; one of the two possible conditions for amr, distinct from actual 'uluww. [Note: In earlier usul, often not distinguished from 'uluww; here it is a technical term.]
علو ('uluww): Actual high rank or superiority; the second possible condition for amr. [Note: No significant shift.]
أقوال أربعة (aqwāl arba'a): Four opinions on the conditions for amr: (1) isti'la' only, (2) neither, (3) both, (4) 'uluww only. [Note: This specific enumeration appears in usul al-fiqh works; elsewhere there may be other opinions.]

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which opinion does Ibn al-Humam consider correct?
A) isti'la' only
B) neither 'uluww nor isti'la'
C) both 'uluww and isti'la'
D) 'uluww only

Key Takeaway
The four opinions on the conditions for amr hinge on whether the speaker must have actual superiority ('uluww) or merely a seeking of superiority (isti'la'), with the majority negating any condition.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

Defending the Term 'Muṭṭarid' in Definitional Theory
Commentator defends the use of 'muṭṭarid' against linguistic objections.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why 'muṭṭarid' is a valid term in logical definitions despite linguistic objections, and trace the commentator's response.

Core Idea
A term's validity in logic is determined by its technical usage, not its root meaning in every context.

In logic, a definition must be 'muṭṭarid' (uniformly applicable). However, some scholars objected that 'muṭṭarid' is not a valid Arabic word. In this passage, the commentator al-Bannani defends the term by distinguishing between different roots and showing that 'muṭṭarid' comes from a different derivation than the one criticized. This lesson walks through the objection, the response, and the importance of contextual semantic analysis in Islamic logic.

Guided Path
1
Identify the objection
Find what Wali al-Din al-'Iraqi and others argued against the term 'muṭṭarid'. They cited Sibawayhi's statement that 'iṭṭarada' is not used, and al-Ṣiḥāḥ called it a despicable dialect.
Note that the objection is based on authoritative linguistic sources.
2
Distinguish the roots
Compare the root 'ṭarada' (to expel) with 'iṭṭarada' (to flow continuously) or 'iṭṭarada al-amru' (to be straight). The objection confuses two different meanings.
Sibawayhi's comment applies only to the meaning of expulsion, not to the meaning of continuity.
3
Analyse the commentator's response
Al-Bannani shows that 'muṭṭarid' derives from either the metaphorical extension of water flowing continuously or from the literal meaning 'to be straight' as in al-Qamus. He argues it has become a conventional reality (ḥaqīqa 'urfiyya) or even a literal linguistic reality.
The response uses both metaphorical and literal justifications.
4
Evaluate the strength of the defense
Consider whether the commentator successfully refutes the objection. The defense relies on distinguishing the specific senses of the verb and citing authoritative dictionaries. The objection is based on a misunderstanding of the intended meaning.
This shows the importance of understanding context in semantic debates.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تَنْبِية: شخ البناني
البناتي على السلم المروني
اعْتَرَضَ غَيْرُ وَاحِدٍ كَوَلِيِّ الدِّيْنِ العِرَاقِيِّ، وَتَبِعَهُ بَعْضُ الشُّرَّاحِ تَعْبِيرَهُمْ بِـ «المُطَّرِدِ» : بِقَوْلِ سِيْبَوَيْهِ [ج/ ۱۹]: يَقُولُونَ طَرَدْتُهُ ،فَذَهَبَ، وَلَا يَقُولُونَ فَانْطَرَدَ، وَلَا فَاطَّرَدَ»، وَبِقَوْلِ الصَّحَاحِ»: أَنَّ اطَرَدَ لُغَةٌ رَدِينَةٌ )) .
وَهُوَ اعْتِرَاضٌ غَيْرُ صَحِيحِ ؛ إِذِ الَّذِي قَالَ فِيهِ سِيْبَوَيْهِ مَا ذَكَرَ هُوَ «الطَّرْدُ» بِمَعْنَى الذَّهَابِ، وَلَيْسَ مَا هُنَا مِنْهُ، بَلِ المُطَّرِدُ هُنَا مَأخُوذُ مِنْ قَوْلِهِمْ: «اطَّرَدَ المَاءُ بِمَعْنَى : اتَّصَلَ جَرْبُهُ، وَ: «اطَرَدَ الشَّيْءُ) : تَتَابَعَ؛ كَأنَّ التَّعْرِيفَ الَّذِي لَا يَنْخَرِمُ، وَكَذَا القَاعِدَةُ الَّتِي لَا تَنْخَرِمْ شُبِّهَا بِالعَيْنِ الَّتِي لَا يَنْقَطِعُ جَرْبُهَا، وَاسْتُعِيرَ لَهُمَا الأطْرَادُ، ثُمَّ شَاعَ ذَلِكَ حَتَّى صَارَ حَقِيقَةٌ عُرْفِيَّةٌ، أَوْ مَأخُوذٌ مِنَ: «اطَرَدَ الأَمْرَ أَي اسْتَقَامَ؛ كَمَا فِي القَامُوسِ»، فَهُوَ حَقِيقَةٌ لُغَوِيَّةٌ، وَهَذَا أَظْهَرُ، وَاللَّهُ تَعَالَى أَعْلَمُ.
A Caution: [The commentator] al-Bannani on al-Sullam al-Murawnaq. More than one, like Wali al-Din al-‘Iraqi, and some commentators followed him, objected to their expression 'al-muṭṭarid' by the statement of Sibawayhi: 'They say: ṭaradtuhu, fadhahaba, and they do not say: fanṭarada, nor faṭṭarada,' and by the statement of al-Ṣiḥāḥ: 'that iṭṭarada is a despicable dialect.' And it is an objection that is not correct, because what Sibawayhi said about 'al-ṭard' meaning departure, and what is here is not from that, rather 'al-muṭṭarid' here is taken from their saying: 'iṭṭarada al-mā'u' meaning its flow became continuous, and 'iṭṭarada al-shay'u' meaning it followed in succession; as if the definition that is not breached, and likewise the rule that is not breached, are likened to the spring whose flow is not cut off, and 'al-iṭṭirād' was borrowed for them, then that became widespread until it became a conventional reality, or it is taken from 'iṭṭarada al-amru' meaning it became straight, as in al-Qamus, so it is a linguistic reality, and this is more apparent, and Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 562

Commentary
This passage is a critical defense of the term 'muṭṭarid' used in definitional theory. Some scholars, such as Wali al-Din al-‘Iraqi, objected that 'muṭṭarid' is not a valid Arabic word because Sibawayhi states that the verb 'ṭarada' does not have a form VIII reflexive 'inṭarada' or 'iṭṭarada', and al-Ṣiḥāḥ calls 'iṭṭarada' a poor dialect. The commentator responds by clarifying that the objection misunderstands the derivation. Sibawayhi's comment was about 'ṭard' meaning 'to go away', not the term used here. The 'muṭṭarid' in logic is derived either from 'iṭṭarada al-mā’’ (water flowing continuously) or from 'iṭṭarada al-amru' (the matter being straight), as recorded in al-Qamus. The term was first used metaphorically, then became a conventional technical term (ḥaqīqa ‘urfiyya) or even a literal linguistic term. The commentator notes that the latter interpretation (from al-Qamus) is more apparent because it avoids metaphor. This defense preserves the logical condition that a definition must be 'muṭṭarid' (uniformly applicable) without linguistic criticism.

Key Terms
مُطَّرِد
اطَّرَدَ

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is the term 'muṭṭarid' considered valid despite the objection from Sibawayhi?
A) It is derived from 'iṭṭarada al-mā'' and not from 'ṭarada'.
B) Sibawayhi did not mention it, so it is acceptable.
C) It is not Arabic, so it is a technical term.
D) It means 'to expel' in a different sense.

Key Takeaway
The validity of 'muṭṭarid' as a logical term is preserved by tracing its correct linguistic origin, showing that technical terms must be understood in their specific context.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Explain the objection raised by Wali al-Din al-'Iraqi and how al-Bannani refutes it. In your own words, why is the objection incorrect?
?
Find an example of a definition in Islamic law (e.g., the definition of 'fasting' or 'zakat') and evaluate whether it is muṭṭarid. Justify your answer by showing that it applies uniformly to all instances.

What Is Mantiq?
beginner
7 min
The Genus and Differentia of Qadiyya
Commentary defines qadiyya with genus and differentia.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the genus and differentia in the definition of qadiyya (proposition) and distinguish it from other compounds.

Core Idea
A proposition is a compound that by itself admits truth and falsehood.

This lesson unpacks the classical definition of qadiyya. The commentator identifies its proximate genus (compound) and its differentia (inherent possibility of truth and falsehood). By grasping this structure, you will be able to classify any utterance as a proposition or not.

Guided Path
1
Locate the term being defined
Find the phrase that defines qadiyya. The definition is: 'ما احتمل الصدق لذاته جرى بينهم' (what admits truth by itself runs between them). Identify the definiendum (qadiyya) and the definiens (the rest).
2
Extract the genus
The commentator explains that 'ما' means 'مركب' (compound), the proximate genus. This excludes simple terms (mufrad) and includes both complete and incomplete compounds.
The genus is broad, covering all compound expressions.
3
Extract the differentia
The differentia is 'احتمل الصدق لذاته' (admits truth by itself). This distinguishes qadiyya from other compounds that do not inherently admit truth or falsehood (e.g., commands, incomplete phrases).
4
Test the definition's completeness
Check if the definition includes all propositions (declarative sentences and implied performatives) and excludes all non-propositions (simple terms, incomplete compounds, pure performatives). The commentator later refines it.
The definition is a hadd naqis because it uses 'truth' rather than 'falsehood', but it is corrected in the commentary.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بَابٌ فِي القَضَايَا وَأَحْكَامِهَا هَذَا شُرُوعٌ مِنْهُ فِي الأَمْرِ الثَّالِثِ مِنَ الأُمُورِ الأَرْبَعَةِ الَّتِي انْحَصَرَ فِيهَا الفَنُّ كَمَا تَقَدَّمَ، وَهُوَ : مَبَادِئَ التَّصْدِيقَاتِ، بَعْدَ أَنْ فَرَغَ مِنَ التَّصَوُّرَاتِ وَمَبَادِئِهَا وَالقَضَايَا جَمْعُ: «قَضِيَّةٍ» كَـ : مَطَايَا جَمْعُ : مَطِيَّة. وَأَحْكَامُهَا هِيَ : النَّقَائِضُ وَالعُكُوسِ. ثُمَّ أَشَارَ إِلَى تَعْرِيفِ القَضِيَّةِ بِقَوْلِهِ : «قَضِيَّةٌ» وَ«خَـبَـرَ مَا احْتَمَلَ الصِّدْقَ لِذَاتِهِ جَرَى بَيْنَهُمُ: فَقَوْلُهُ: «مَا» أَيْ: مُرَكَّبٌ؛ بِقَرِينَةِ مَا قَدَّمَهُ مِنَ التَّقْسِيم ، وَلأَنَّ المُرَكَّبَ هُوَ الجِنْسُ القَرِيبُ لِلقَضِيَّةِ، فَيَخْرُجُ عَنْهُ : المُفْرَدُ، وَيَشْمَلُ : المُرَكَّبَ النَّاقِصَ وَالتَّامَّ، وَالإِنْشَاءَ وَالخَبَرَ. قال النَّاظم : (مَا احْتَمَلَ .. (البيت كان الأولى أن لو عبّر بـ «الكذب بدل «الصِّدق» ؛ لِمَا تقرَّر - على ما سيأتي - مِن أنَّ مدلول الخبر الصّدقُ فقط، وأمَّا الكذبُ فليس بمدلول اللفظ، وإِنَّما هو احتمال عقلي نقيض مدلوله. مرادهم قال الرَّضيُّ في شرح الحاجبية وأمَّا قولهم: «الخبرُ يحتمل الصدق والكذب»، فليس أنَّ الكذب مدلول للفظ الخبر كالصدق، بل مرادُهُم : أنَّ العقل لا يمنع أن يكون مدلول اللفظ غير ثابت، فهو محتمل الكذب من حيث العقل، وبه يتبيَّن أنَّ نسبة الاحتمال إلى المين أولى، كما فعل شيخنا في خريدته حيث قال : مَا اخ تَمَلَ ـلَ المَيْنَ لأنَّه أظهر في امتياز الخبر عن غيره مِنَ المركَّبات الإنشائيَّة والتَّقييديَّة؛ لأنَّ كلَّ ما عدا الخبر لا يحتمل المين. وَقَوْلُهُ : احْتَمَلَ الصِّدْقَ .. إلخ : مُخْرِجٌ لِلمُرَكَبِ النَّاقِصِ تَقْيِيدِيَّا كَـ : الحَيَوَانِ النَّاطِقِ . أَوْ إِضَافِيًّا كَـ: «غُلَامِ زَيْدِ». وَمُخْرِجٌ أَيْضاً : لِلإِنْشَاءَاتِ، فَإِنَّ هَذِهِ الأُمُورَ لَا تَحْتَمِلُ الصِّدْقَ وَالكَذَبَ لِذَاتِهَا . وَقَدْ تَحْتَمِلُهُ لِأَمْرٍ خَارِجٍ عَنْهَا ، نَحْوُ : اسْقِنِي مَاءً» ، فَإِنَّهُ لَا يَحْتَمِلُ مِنْ حَيْثُ مَفْهُومُ الطَّلَبِ صِدْقاً وَلَا كَذِباً ، لَكِنَّهُ يَسْتَلْزِمُ بِحَسَبِ العُرْفِ نِسْبَةً خَبَرِيَّةً مُحْتَمِلَةً لِلصِّدْقِ وَالكَذِبِ، وَهِيَ : «أَنَّهُ عَطْشَانُ». وَكَذَا : النِّسْبَةُ التَّقْيِيدِيَّةُ ، نَحْوُ : زَيْدُ العَالِمُ، فَإِنَّهَا مِنْ حَيْثُ هِيَ لَا يَتَطَرَّقُ إِلَيْهَا الصِّدْقُ وَالكَذِبُ، لَكِنَّ فِيهَا إِشَارَةٌ إِلَى نِسْبَةٍ خَبَرِيَّةٍ تَقْبَلُهُمَا ؛ لِأَنَّ المُتَبَادَرَ أَنَّهُ لَا يُوصَفُ الشَّيْءُ إِلَّا بِمَا هُوَ ثَابِتٌ لَهُ. وَكَذَا يُقَالُ فِي : الإِضَافِيَّةِ، إِذْ لَا يُضَافُ الشَّيْءُ إِلَّا لِمَا هُوَ كَائِنٌ لَهُ، فَبِهَذَا الِاعْتِبَارِ
Chapter on propositions and their rulings. This is a commencement by him in the third matter from the four matters which the discipline is confined to, as previously mentioned, and it is the principles of assent (tasdiqat), after he finished the concepts (tasawwurat) and their principles. 'Al-qadaya' is plural of 'qadiyya', like 'mataaya' plural of 'matiyya'. And their rulings are: contradictions (naqaid) and converses (ukus). Then he pointed to the definition of the proposition by his saying: 'Qadiyya' and 'khabar' is what admits truth by itself runs between them. So his saying: 'Ma' means a compound (murakkab) due to the context of the division he presented, and because the compound is the proximate genus of the proposition, so it excludes the simple (mufrad) and includes the incomplete compound (murakkab naqis) and the complete (tamm), and the performative (insha) and the declarative (khabar). The poet said: It would have been better to express with 'kadhib' instead of 'sidq' because of what is established – as will come – that the signification of khabar is only truth, and as for falsehood, it is not significant of the utterance, but rather it is a rational possibility opposite to its signification. Al-Radi said in his commentary on al-Hajibiyya: As for their statement: 'The khabar admits truth and falsehood', it is not that falsehood is signification of the utterance of khabar like truth, but rather their intent is that the intellect does not prevent the signification of the utterance from being non-established, so it is possible for falsehood from the perspective of the intellect, and by this it is clear that attributing possibility to al-mayn (i.e., falsehood) is more appropriate, as our teacher did in his Khariqa where he said: 'What admits al-mayn', because it is more apparent in distinguishing the khabar from other performative and restrictive compounds because everything other than khabar does not admit al-mayn. And his saying: 'Admits truth' etc. excludes the incomplete compound: restrictive (taqyidi) like 'al-hayawan al-natiq' (rational animal), or additive (idafi) like 'ghulam Zayd' (Zayd's slave), and also excludes the performatives because these matters do not admit truth and falsehood by themselves, and they may admit it due to an external matter, like 'Ishqini ma'an' (Give me water), for it does not admit from the perspective of the concept of request truth nor falsehood, but it necessitates by convention a declarative relation that admits truth and falsehood, which is 'He is thirsty.' And similarly, the restrictive relation, like 'Zayd al-alim' (Zayd the learned), for it in itself does not admit truth and falsehood, but in it there is an indication of a declarative relation that admits them, because the immediate understanding is that a thing is not described except by what is established for it. And similarly it is said in the additive, because a thing is not added except to what is existing for it. So by this consideration.
Source pages p. 572

Commentary
This passage is a definitional expansion of the term 'qadiyya' (proposition). The author first sets the context: the chapter begins the third of the four pillars of logic, namely the principles of assent (tasdiqat), following the treatment of concepts (tasawwurat). He notes that 'qadaya' is the plural of 'qadiyya', and that its rulings (ahkam) here refer to contradictions (naqaid) and converses (ukus).

The core definition is given via the poet's line: 'What admits truth by itself runs between them.' The commentator explains that 'ma' (what) means a compound (murakkab), indicated by the earlier division of utterances into request and report, and because the compound is the proximate genus of the proposition. This excludes simple terms (mufrad) and includes incomplete compounds (e.g., 'rational animal'), complete compounds (full sentences), and both performative (insha) and declarative (khabar) types.

A critical refinement follows: it would have been better to use 'falsehood' (kadhib) instead of 'truth' (sidq) because the declarative's primary signification is truth; falsehood is only a rational possibility. Al-Radi clarifies that 'admits truth and falsehood' does not mean both are equally significations; rather, the intellect allows that the content may be false. Hence, attributing possibility to falsehood (al-mayn) is more precise, as it better distinguishes khabar from other compounds (e.g., commands, restrictive phrases) that do not admit falsehood at all.

Finally, the passage explains what the definition excludes: incomplete compounds (restrictive like 'rational animal' and additive like 'Zayd's slave') and performatives (e.g., commands like 'Give me water') do not themselves admit truth/falsehood, though they imply a declarative statement that does. Restrictive and additive relations also imply underlying declarative judgments.

Key Terms
قضية
مركب
صدق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the proximate genus of qadiyya according to the passage?

C) Khabar (declarative)

Key Takeaway
The definition of qadiyya hinges on its genus (compound) and differentia (inherent possibility of truth/falsehood).

?

What Is Mantiq?
intermediate
8 min
Refining the Differentia: Truth vs. Falsehood
Commentary refines differentia from truth to falsehood.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the commentator prefers 'falsehood' over 'truth' in the definition of khabar and how this clarifies the differentia.

Core Idea
Using 'falsehood' in the definition better excludes performatives and incomplete compounds.

The commentator notes a subtlety: the differentia should mention falsehood (kadhib) rather than truth (sidq) because truth is the actual signification of khabar, while falsehood is a rational possibility. This refinement sharpens the definition and is preferred by later logicians.

Guided Path
1
Understand the objection to 'truth'
The commentator says using 'truth' is less precise because the khabar's signification is truth; falsehood is not signified but is a rational opposite. Hence, 'admits truth' might mislead.
2
See the proposed correction
Al-Radi and the poet's teacher (Shaykh) replace 'truth' with 'al-mayn' (falsehood) to make the differentia more distinctive: only khabar admits falsehood, while other compounds do not.
'Al-mayn' is a classical term for falsehood.
3
Apply the correction
The definition becomes: 'Khabar is a compound that admits falsehood by itself.' This excludes performatives (commands, etc.) and restrictive compounds, as they cannot be false in themselves.
This is the preferred definition in the text.
4
Test the improvement
Compare the two definitions: 'admits truth' includes khabar but also could include some performatives by implication? The commentator argues that using 'falsehood' is more apparent in distinguishing khabar from all other compounds.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بَابٌ فِي القَضَايَا وَأَحْكَامِهَا هَذَا شُرُوعٌ مِنْهُ فِي الأَمْرِ الثَّالِثِ مِنَ الأُمُورِ الأَرْبَعَةِ الَّتِي انْحَصَرَ فِيهَا الفَنُّ كَمَا تَقَدَّمَ، وَهُوَ : مَبَادِئَ التَّصْدِيقَاتِ، بَعْدَ أَنْ فَرَغَ مِنَ التَّصَوُّرَاتِ وَمَبَادِئِهَا وَالقَضَايَا جَمْعُ: «قَضِيَّةٍ» كَـ : مَطَايَا جَمْعُ : مَطِيَّة. وَأَحْكَامُهَا هِيَ : النَّقَائِضُ وَالعُكُوسِ. ثُمَّ أَشَارَ إِلَى تَعْرِيفِ القَضِيَّةِ بِقَوْلِهِ : «قَضِيَّةٌ» وَ«خَـبَـرَ مَا احْتَمَلَ الصِّدْقَ لِذَاتِهِ جَرَى بَيْنَهُمُ: فَقَوْلُهُ: «مَا» أَيْ: مُرَكَّبٌ؛ بِقَرِينَةِ مَا قَدَّمَهُ مِنَ التَّقْسِيم ، وَلأَنَّ المُرَكَّبَ هُوَ الجِنْسُ القَرِيبُ لِلقَضِيَّةِ، فَيَخْرُجُ عَنْهُ : المُفْرَدُ، وَيَشْمَلُ : المُرَكَّبَ النَّاقِصَ وَالتَّامَّ، وَالإِنْشَاءَ وَالخَبَرَ. قال النَّاظم : (مَا احْتَمَلَ .. (البيت كان الأولى أن لو عبّر بـ «الكذب بدل «الصِّدق» ؛ لِمَا تقرَّر - على ما سيأتي - مِن أنَّ مدلول الخبر الصّدقُ فقط، وأمَّا الكذبُ فليس بمدلول اللفظ، وإِنَّما هو احتمال عقلي نقيض مدلوله. مرادهم قال الرَّضيُّ في شرح الحاجبية وأمَّا قولهم: «الخبرُ يحتمل الصدق والكذب»، فليس أنَّ الكذب مدلول للفظ الخبر كالصدق، بل مرادُهُم : أنَّ العقل لا يمنع أن يكون مدلول اللفظ غير ثابت، فهو محتمل الكذب من حيث العقل، وبه يتبيَّن أنَّ نسبة الاحتمال إلى المين أولى، كما فعل شيخنا في خريدته حيث قال : مَا اخ تَمَلَ ـلَ المَيْنَ لأنَّه أظهر في امتياز الخبر عن غيره مِنَ المركَّبات الإنشائيَّة والتَّقييديَّة؛ لأنَّ كلَّ ما عدا الخبر لا يحتمل المين. وَقَوْلُهُ : احْتَمَلَ الصِّدْقَ .. إلخ : مُخْرِجٌ لِلمُرَكَبِ النَّاقِصِ تَقْيِيدِيَّا كَـ : الحَيَوَانِ النَّاطِقِ . أَوْ إِضَافِيًّا كَـ: «غُلَامِ زَيْدِ». وَمُخْرِجٌ أَيْضاً : لِلإِنْشَاءَاتِ، فَإِنَّ هَذِهِ الأُمُورَ لَا تَحْتَمِلُ الصِّدْقَ وَالكَذَبَ لِذَاتِهَا . وَقَدْ تَحْتَمِلُهُ لِأَمْرٍ خَارِجٍ عَنْهَا ، نَحْوُ : اسْقِنِي مَاءً» ، فَإِنَّهُ لَا يَحْتَمِلُ مِنْ حَيْثُ مَفْهُومُ الطَّلَبِ صِدْقاً وَلَا كَذِباً ، لَكِنَّهُ يَسْتَلْزِمُ بِحَسَبِ العُرْفِ نِسْبَةً خَبَرِيَّةً مُحْتَمِلَةً لِلصِّدْقِ وَالكَذِبِ، وَهِيَ : «أَنَّهُ عَطْشَانُ». وَكَذَا : النِّسْبَةُ التَّقْيِيدِيَّةُ ، نَحْوُ : زَيْدُ العَالِمُ، فَإِنَّهَا مِنْ حَيْثُ هِيَ لَا يَتَطَرَّقُ إِلَيْهَا الصِّدْقُ وَالكَذِبُ، لَكِنَّ فِيهَا إِشَارَةٌ إِلَى نِسْبَةٍ خَبَرِيَّةٍ تَقْبَلُهُمَا ؛ لِأَنَّ المُتَبَادَرَ أَنَّهُ لَا يُوصَفُ الشَّيْءُ إِلَّا بِمَا هُوَ ثَابِتٌ لَهُ. وَكَذَا يُقَالُ فِي : الإِضَافِيَّةِ، إِذْ لَا يُضَافُ الشَّيْءُ إِلَّا لِمَا هُوَ كَائِنٌ لَهُ، فَبِهَذَا الِاعْتِبَارِ
Chapter on propositions and their rulings. This is a commencement by him in the third matter from the four matters which the discipline is confined to, as previously mentioned, and it is the principles of assent (tasdiqat), after he finished the concepts (tasawwurat) and their principles. 'Al-qadaya' is plural of 'qadiyya', like 'mataaya' plural of 'matiyya'. And their rulings are: contradictions (naqaid) and converses (ukus). Then he pointed to the definition of the proposition by his saying: 'Qadiyya' and 'khabar' is what admits truth by itself runs between them. So his saying: 'Ma' means a compound (murakkab) due to the context of the division he presented, and because the compound is the proximate genus of the proposition, so it excludes the simple (mufrad) and includes the incomplete compound (murakkab naqis) and the complete (tamm), and the performative (insha) and the declarative (khabar). The poet said: It would have been better to express with 'kadhib' instead of 'sidq' because of what is established – as will come – that the signification of khabar is only truth, and as for falsehood, it is not significant of the utterance, but rather it is a rational possibility opposite to its signification. Al-Radi said in his commentary on al-Hajibiyya: As for their statement: 'The khabar admits truth and falsehood', it is not that falsehood is signification of the utterance of khabar like truth, but rather their intent is that the intellect does not prevent the signification of the utterance from being non-established, so it is possible for falsehood from the perspective of the intellect, and by this it is clear that attributing possibility to al-mayn (i.e., falsehood) is more appropriate, as our teacher did in his Khariqa where he said: 'What admits al-mayn', because it is more apparent in distinguishing the khabar from other performative and restrictive compounds because everything other than khabar does not admit al-mayn. And his saying: 'Admits truth' etc. excludes the incomplete compound: restrictive (taqyidi) like 'al-hayawan al-natiq' (rational animal), or additive (idafi) like 'ghulam Zayd' (Zayd's slave), and also excludes the performatives because these matters do not admit truth and falsehood by themselves, and they may admit it due to an external matter, like 'Ishqini ma'an' (Give me water), for it does not admit from the perspective of the concept of request truth nor falsehood, but it necessitates by convention a declarative relation that admits truth and falsehood, which is 'He is thirsty.' And similarly, the restrictive relation, like 'Zayd al-alim' (Zayd the learned), for it in itself does not admit truth and falsehood, but in it there is an indication of a declarative relation that admits them, because the immediate understanding is that a thing is not described except by what is established for it. And similarly it is said in the additive, because a thing is not added except to what is existing for it. So by this consideration.
Source pages p. 572

Commentary
This passage is a definitional expansion of the term 'qadiyya' (proposition). The author first sets the context: the chapter begins the third of the four pillars of logic, namely the principles of assent (tasdiqat), following the treatment of concepts (tasawwurat). He notes that 'qadaya' is the plural of 'qadiyya', and that its rulings (ahkam) here refer to contradictions (naqaid) and converses (ukus).

The core definition is given via the poet's line: 'What admits truth by itself runs between them.' The commentator explains that 'ma' (what) means a compound (murakkab), indicated by the earlier division of utterances into request and report, and because the compound is the proximate genus of the proposition. This excludes simple terms (mufrad) and includes incomplete compounds (e.g., 'rational animal'), complete compounds (full sentences), and both performative (insha) and declarative (khabar) types.

A critical refinement follows: it would have been better to use 'falsehood' (kadhib) instead of 'truth' (sidq) because the declarative's primary signification is truth; falsehood is only a rational possibility. Al-Radi clarifies that 'admits truth and falsehood' does not mean both are equally significations; rather, the intellect allows that the content may be false. Hence, attributing possibility to falsehood (al-mayn) is more precise, as it better distinguishes khabar from other compounds (e.g., commands, restrictive phrases) that do not admit falsehood at all.

Finally, the passage explains what the definition excludes: incomplete compounds (restrictive like 'rational animal' and additive like 'Zayd's slave') and performatives (e.g., commands like 'Give me water') do not themselves admit truth/falsehood, though they imply a declarative statement that does. Restrictive and additive relations also imply underlying declarative judgments.

Key Terms
صدق
كذب
مين
خبر
إنشاء

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the commentator prefer using 'falsehood' (al-mayn) in the definition of khabar?
A) Because falsehood is the primary signification of khabar
B) Because falsehood is more distinctive, as only khabar can admit it
C) Because performatives admit falsehood
D) Because the poet made a mistake

Key Takeaway
The differentia of a definition should be as distinctive as possible; using 'falsehood' instead of 'truth' better isolates declarative statements.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
In the definition 'al-insan hayawan natiq' (man is a rational animal), some logicians prefer 'al-insan hayawan dahik' (laughing animal). Apply the same 'falsehood' logic: which differentia is more distinctive?
?
Rewrite the definition of 'nabidh' (date wine) in fiqh: 'every intoxicating drink is forbidden; nabidh is intoxicating; therefore nabidh is forbidden.' Identify the differentia.

What Is Mantiq?
intermediate
7 min
Exclusion of Performatives and Incomplete Compounds
Commentary explains exclusion of performatives and incomplete compounds.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why performatives (insha) and incomplete compounds are not propositions by themselves, but can imply propositions.

Core Idea
Commands and incomplete phrases are not propositions but may carry declarative implications.

The definition's differentia 'admits truth by itself' excludes performatives like commands and incomplete compounds like 'rational animal'. However, these often imply a declarative statement that does admit truth/falsehood. This lesson explores that nuance.

Guided Path
1
Identify what is excluded
The definition excludes incomplete compounds (restrictive like 'rational animal', additive like 'Zayd's slave') and performatives (commands, requests). They do not admit truth/falsehood by themselves.
These are called murakkabat naqisa and insha'at.
2
Understand the implication
Take 'Give me water'. The command itself is neither true nor false, but in context it implies 'He is thirsty', which is a declarative that can be true or false.
Similarly, 'Zayd the learned' implies 'Zayd is learned'.
3
Distinguish inherent vs. implied admission
The definition requires that the compound itself, by virtue of its meaning (bi-dhatihi), admits truth/falsehood. Performatives and incomplete compounds only do so indirectly via an implied declarative.
This is why they are excluded from the strict definition.
4
Apply to Islamic sciences
In usul al-fiqh, a command like 'Pray!' is a performative. Its meaning is not true or false, but it implies the obligation that can be evaluated. Understanding this separates linguistic form from logical proposition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بَابٌ فِي القَضَايَا وَأَحْكَامِهَا هَذَا شُرُوعٌ مِنْهُ فِي الأَمْرِ الثَّالِثِ مِنَ الأُمُورِ الأَرْبَعَةِ الَّتِي انْحَصَرَ فِيهَا الفَنُّ كَمَا تَقَدَّمَ، وَهُوَ : مَبَادِئَ التَّصْدِيقَاتِ، بَعْدَ أَنْ فَرَغَ مِنَ التَّصَوُّرَاتِ وَمَبَادِئِهَا وَالقَضَايَا جَمْعُ: «قَضِيَّةٍ» كَـ : مَطَايَا جَمْعُ : مَطِيَّة. وَأَحْكَامُهَا هِيَ : النَّقَائِضُ وَالعُكُوسِ. ثُمَّ أَشَارَ إِلَى تَعْرِيفِ القَضِيَّةِ بِقَوْلِهِ : «قَضِيَّةٌ» وَ«خَـبَـرَ مَا احْتَمَلَ الصِّدْقَ لِذَاتِهِ جَرَى بَيْنَهُمُ: فَقَوْلُهُ: «مَا» أَيْ: مُرَكَّبٌ؛ بِقَرِينَةِ مَا قَدَّمَهُ مِنَ التَّقْسِيم ، وَلأَنَّ المُرَكَّبَ هُوَ الجِنْسُ القَرِيبُ لِلقَضِيَّةِ، فَيَخْرُجُ عَنْهُ : المُفْرَدُ، وَيَشْمَلُ : المُرَكَّبَ النَّاقِصَ وَالتَّامَّ، وَالإِنْشَاءَ وَالخَبَرَ. قال النَّاظم : (مَا احْتَمَلَ .. Commentary

Checkpoint
According to the passage, the command 'Give me water' does not admit truth/falsehood by itself. What does it imply that does admit truth/falsehood?
A) The water is clean
B) He is thirsty
C) He is generous
D) The command is true

Key Takeaway
Performatives and incomplete compounds are not propositions, but they often imply a declarative statement that can be true or false.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Analyze the fiqh statement 'Sell!' as a performative: what declarative does it imply?
?
Identify whether 'al-rajul al-karim' (the generous man) is a proposition or not. Explain your reasoning.
